Galiens tells us of a cure by which some honourably cured the pain of the sciatica and the vein of the groin, and he says that we did no other cure, and that he became well once when we did this cure, and he bathed as he is taught afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And thus take part of the green fresh chickpea flour and grind it moist with a little fat, and put on the hip and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it for three hours by the quantity that the patient does not feel the burning again
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	Then let the patient enter the bath while the limb is still slightly bent, and let him enter the water, and the pain will vanish and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And do not let anyone use such medicine as cautery except after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Diascorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with fine needles, if it helps with moisture; and it must be done gradually
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in oil, and pour it over the pit between the thumb and the great toe and the other which is called the fossilized pit
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking fine needles dry, and burn them until they are charcoal, and pour them over the linen, and leave it until it is stained; and then move the bone again, and do not stop making pressure until you think that it is coming out until the heel, and that the pain has ceased; and this method of cautery is called "cautery of needles".
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or by sitting or percussion or by too great an evacuation, or by similar signs of cold matter spread, of none of these symptoms is the cautery of any value, except for what comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	When the patient is free from foul pills or other symptoms, we make three lines signed with a needle on the back, where the pain is, and in between these lines we make two or three cauteries, according to the virtue and the quantity that the patient can suffer; and the cautery is to be made according to the cautery called "points"; and if you see it, make two or three cauteries at the middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes as a small pulse, and signs of its beginning are when the veins are torn when they swell, and there is pain; and you find it at the lower spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes after the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it healed, if you cauterize with the fire according to this fashion.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery burns any part of the spine excessively.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	If you see that the burn penetrates the spine as far as the tip of the cautery twice or thrice, and that the points are close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After that, cure the limb until it is sound, as we have said above, and beware that you do not touch the cautery to the bone that is in contact with nerves
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb, and when pain originates from a wound, call it "podagre" indeed; and when the cause is cold and medicines fail to cure it, it is often cured by cautery in part: make the opening of the cautery around the joint that is painful, and let the cautery be of olive oil in this fashion:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you touch the cheek of the jaw, if you touch it with the cautery, call it "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is pain that comes up to the joints and other parts, and this happens often, if you must burn each joint three times or four times with the olive cautery; and if you must do more than this, but do not keep your hand too far away from the fire until the burn is over
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend down to the groin and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are as far as the hands, if you prick twice at the base of the thumb; and if there remains no pain in that area, if you prick on the wrist and on the nail of the hand; and if the pains reach as far as the buttocks or as far as the shoulder blades, if you cauterize some part of it, and make the patient comfortable and give him medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make him comfortable and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the root of the throat</start_of_turn>
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the scapula is dislocated, and the ball descends like nails and this is new, if you see that when you cure it, it does not mend the marrow; and that it uses things that leave the belly, so that the marrow descends from the belly; then make it sit on its back between your hands, and command that it grasp its wing until the ball is repaired, and keep it at your sides, and sign the incision on the edge of the scapula, and as a sign that it is like half of a circle below the bones; then withdraw the cautery like this.
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as he is soft and secretes sensations.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then bind the belly to his body; and he will hold your hand so that they do not return backward; and work well the wounds of the patient, and put on him some lint and some silk on the wounds, and something else on his hand; then put the cautery on the sign at the top of his hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you touch the bone, and if you do not reach the bone the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and beware cautiously that the belly does not swell when you are doing the cautery; that you do not burn him; and that by this means the patient does not die, or anything else wrong.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And scraps of hair that you do not burn down to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And you must know that hair must be cut close to the skin according to the measure of the patient, and of great men also according to their measure; after three days cure the leg of the burn as long as the scab has become bony; after that cure other wounds as long as they are healed; and keep the patient lying down for forty days on his back until the wound is well closed; and you must know that his movements must be gentle so that the swelling does not rise when he lies down to go to bed.</start_of_turn>
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	After forty days, when he wants to get up, let him have a well-made bandage and keep him quiet for forty days; and let him rest well, that he works a little and avoids eating too much drink and greasy food, and too much haste; and when he has learned this, if he is completely healed.</start_of_turn
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall tell you afterwards the treatment of the thigh in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the route of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds come out of other parts and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, if you do not prick them at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the edge of the wound and make a line along the width of the wound, and another at the bottom, and keep your hand steady with the whole of your arm on the cautery clamp
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and softer.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether the shoulder or the hip or the wound, and this pain lasts a long time, and the treatment of medicine is not worth it, then you must cauterize with the cautery which is called "points," and cauterize according to the length of the limb and the smallness and weakness and the toughness and the swelling and the pain
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is sane after the first cautery, it is well; if not, repeat the cautery upon him, for it is customary that it must move to the neighbouring limb, because it is certain that you must make the cauteries while the patient is sane.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, whether from injury or from a wound, and the pain persists for a long time, the remedy of medicine is not worth it; therefore it is recommended that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called the "points," or that the cautery be performed according to the length of the limb, its thinness and weakness, its toughness and its location of twists and pain. If it is successful on the first cautery, well and good; if not, repeat the procedure. Indeed, it is customary that it should be repeated as close to the painful part as possible, for it is believed that the more cauteries are made, the sooner the patient will be healed.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The diseases do not yield to the cautery at any time, and even the diseases that come from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see the cautery? Take heed if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured as we have said in the division, and do not linger, and you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the whole illness, then make five cauteries on the head: one at the new bone, and the other towards the front at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the shoulder; and leave the hand as long as the cauteries come up to the bone, and as long as the scabs issue forth so that the vapors of the humors can escape; and cauterize the mouse according to what is before you.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if there is widespread moisture everywhere, and it becomes manifest, if you command these cauteries that we have spoken of or chief, namely cauterize on the top of the thumb and index finger, and two on the elbow of the shoulder, and three on the elbow of the back, and one large on the wrist and one other below, and two on the two thumbs, and two on the scapulae, and two on the tendons of the wrist, and one on each joint of the fingers and toes, and on the recesses of the hands; take care that you do not burn the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, and do not make any cautery on the bones of the heel or the stomach or the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And so it is that the more often the fire cautery is done, the more it helps; and the more the patient feels relief; and so it is that the patients do not feel pain from the fire cautery as they would from the pain of a healthy person, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it must be known that the fire cautery should be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in handling various instruments
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating the wound several times with flour of wheat and honey and other cures until it is healed
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and is not healed, then you must make cauteries on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and that the cauteries be done deep enough so that the marrow is pierced; then cure with ointments until it is healed
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never make the cautery on hand, foot or back, at the issue of a nerve that moves the limb, and thus if it is bony it swells; and in no way should anything intervene except one who is skilled in limbs and the issues of the moving nerves close to the bone.
de albaras	When swelling arises in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and dressings, and is not completely healed, then you must perform cautery on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and either make the cautery a little deeper than the depth of the nerve which moves the limb; then cure with ointments until it is healed. And in no case must you perform cautery on the hand, foot, or back, at the exit of the nerve which moves the limb, and if it is bony the swelling will remain. And in no way should anything interfere with it except one who is skilled in limbs and the exits of the moving nerves.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and the remedies of medicine do not help, then you must cauterize with a needle a little deeper than the depth of the nerve, according to the quantity of the tissue; until the swelling is bony and changes color; then cure with flour of times and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, with colon and almond, each part a third; mix them all together, and bind with a bandage, and keep it in place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for carbuncles by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil starts, and you see it stop, if you burn it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the boil
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And everyone says that it is done at the middle of the boil; and I do not think that is good, because I fear that it will ulcerate and corrupt, and I have already known several times that this has happened; and there is no greater thing than to cauter around it, with the cautery which is called the circle, as we have said before.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an ailment called "adubelati", and it delays in healing or because of the excessive swelling it causes or because of the decay of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old), and there is much blood, or because of tension; and you see it haste to heal: then cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; after that, leave it be.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will haste to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce with all the cauteries, if the cautery is too hot: this is the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this ailment called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries perceive the pain, and let them be such that the patient feels relief in parts as the course of the decay progresses.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After that, cure it as long as it is perfectly healthy
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease that is called "corrodens" exists, and it is nothing other than the softening of limbs, for it causes the limbs to become as brittle as dry bones.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in which the fire cautery can be used together with fire, then shave the hair close and moderately, according to what is convenient for the limb or the disease; after having cauterized all parts until you have eradicated all corruption, and nothing remains except the bone itself.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized limbs, and keep them covered with ointment until the burned hair becomes ossified, and all the corruption is gone
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of the wounds engendered by char.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	If after three days the hair does not grow back, it is good; and if this does not happen, repeat the cautery on that which remains corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	This torment is never cured by means of water medicine, but indeed the fire cautery is of greater aid, as I have already said in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The fire cautery. Another method for disease which is called "corrodens" is nothing other than the softening of a limb, because it makes the limb as dry as the lines of fire. If you see this disease in a limb which can suffer from whole-body cautery, then burn the small and great nails according to what is appropriate for the limb or the disease; after that cauterize all parts until you have eradicated all the corruption, and nothing remains except the bone. And then leave it for two days, and put on the cauterized limbs, let them be broiled with oil until the burnings of the fire are ossified, and all the corruption. After the cure of the oily nourishment. And if after two days the limb is well, that is good; but if not, resume the cautery on what remains soft of the limbs corrupted. This softening is never cured by medical treatment in place of fire cautery; but every time fire cautery is of greater aid, as I have already said in the division: take as much as you need.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often there arises a wound by boils that grows into a disease which we call "clos" according to our understanding, and is a burdensome burden that festers the spirit.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	The cautery for this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and warm water cautery
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	If you are to burn with fire, do as with a quill of a goose, and make it of good iron of the size that can penetrate all parts, and leave it with subtle margins; then put all around the boil, and keep your hand firmly around the boil until it comes to the front of the boil; and leave it for three days until it begins to fester; then make an ointment of wild mallow seeds boiled with oil, and leave the ointment on all night, and close it tightly and it will be scraped from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the swelling by applying pressure until it is sound
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if there are converted by discharges of pus, and many times happen and in hands and feet, if you must bring a burn of hot water; and it is in part like this: take a fennel of rue or iron, or a quill of goose, and put it on the boil and the thumb, that is to say, nails; and put the fennel on so that it covers all around, then put on a pot of hot water, and keep your hand firmly, and press your hand by turning so that the margin of the fennel comes to the root of the boil, and can find the hot water going deep until the root; and offer the patient a pot of the biting of the hot water an hour; then leave it like that, and it will spread out all at its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So do another one, as long as you can reach all that is on the skin, then cure the wounds that cause the hairs to fall out.
li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from cold, or from a quarter-fever or from another, if you make for him three or four cautceries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, one cautery or pinch, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave it like that, it will cause the sickness to depart quickly.
des pustules puans	When someone trembles from cold, or from a quarter-fever or from another, if you make for him three or four cautceries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, one cautery or pinch, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave it like that, it will cause the sickness to depart quickly.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Blood sometimes appears by discharge from the skin, or boils, which come from corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is possible at the beginning when they appear, make a cautery on each head of the boils: a subtle burn with a twig of myrtle, or when the point is grasped by the fire, or with long iris root, or the lenticular cautery.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never burn at the beginning when they appear, according to this method, for they do not grow forward but are broken by the excess from which they come, and are cured; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.</start_of_turn
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a mournful thing to extend it.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, if you are in a hurry to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and you strain too much without calming the pain, and no blood comes out any more; then take the olive cautery and make several small and large burns until they are all red; then touch, that is to say, great or small as it is appropriate for the wound and the limb in which the artery is obstructed, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery as long as it is necessary to stop the bleeding
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out when you remove your thumb from the vein, and the cautery is finished, take hold of another cautery that is on the fire immediately.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to perform this one after the other until the limb is stretched out; and beware that thou dost not tear away the nerve which is beneath, and that no other evil arise upon the patient; and keep that when without excision of the artery, one cannot well reattach the limb itself when the artery is large, except by three methods which we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not otherwise treated, or by strong ligation of thread, or by medicines placed upon it which have power to reattach blood.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who brings about the restoration of the limb with great care is by the strict draping of cloths or the putting of things burning upon, or other similar things, if these do not profit, it is of no use.</start_of_turn>
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if there is no other remedy and there is no medicine present, if he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and keep it steady until it is rested from the wound and from the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water often so that it is as cold as the air until the wound is frozen and thickened and rested; and make incisions before that which must be cauterized and medicated.</start_of_turn>
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encourag li seconde livre des cures de taille.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have already said in the first chapter that every disease in which it is necessary to perform cautery of fire, or applied medicine, and the symptoms, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and in this chapter we shall speak of these matters from the head to the toes, for we have found it easier in this way to explain what we wish to convey.</start_of_turn>
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, I must inform you, dear friend, that there is more peril and fear in this chapter than in all the previous cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you should not act rashly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For out of the actions of men come cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they arise from such people who suffer greatly from their ailments that they move lightly because of the fear of their disease, and from the greatness of their malice; from these things we must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And from these things there are those who make you understand, saying: "Wait, I am ready"; and the disease is desperate
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	I advise you only that you allow these things which come to you which have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not carelessly trust only what you are certain of, and what you have learned; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your diseases so that salvation be either confirmed or converted; and this will help you to acquire a good reputation, glory, and memory forever
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Lords, you do well to understand and approve, and if the Holy inspiration of his hand returns to you, amen.</start_of_turn>
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I vos ai ordonné ce chapitre en divisant par Chapitre, selon ce qu’il est devant ou Chapitre des cauteres, que j’avais devisé de celui du chef jusc’à pied, pour ce qu’ils trouvent plus légèrement ce qu’ils ont dû faire.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have commanded thee this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I had commanded thee from head to foot, forasmuch that ye shall find it more lightly what ye have to do.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	The sickness often comes from the swelling of the belly of the child, and when the navel is too tightly strained, the head of the child is often thrown off.  Never does this happen for any other reason than that it does not go back into place
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen such a disease vanish except in the countryside, and with all those whom I have seen, it hastens death; therefore it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in parts for cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw that in childhood, when the shoulder was dislocated and the head swelled up so much that it could not be supported; and I believed that there was too much moisture, and this moisture if it is gathered in the bone above the socket, between the head and the bone; and the work is such that if the moisture is between the head and the bone, and the incision is small, you must make a wide incision; and as much as .ij. we have seen, until the moisture moves.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is greater and the incision is larger, if you make two incisions in the form of a cross, following this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if moisture is on the bone, and you see the sinuses of the cheek swell out on the outer side, and it becomes taut when you press your hand inside, and this does not go back: if you suspect that the jaw is fractured, make two incisions according to this manner.
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, drain out the moisture with all your might.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After that, drain the blood clots and pus, and pour wine and oil on it, and leave it until the fifth day; then remove the dressing and cure the wound with stitches and medicines, and leave the head of the wound open, and give the patient dry meat until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look or open the orifice of the abscess, and the collection of pus; for it is never before; never behind; never to the right; and never to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.
de reume	When the shoulder or the armpit is open, and the injection of liquid, and you do as you please; keep away from the artery; let the vein flow blood, if the patient dies from excessive bleeding and moisture evacuation.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no known disease that is called "catarrh" which has boils or swellings, and the disease is ancient, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then the last cure is to cauterize with this that we will cover the arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary therefore, when you see them covered, that the patient move his head; then press the limb with a rough cloth until the veins open, and then draw out the patient’s neck with all the cloth; then look if the vein is bleeding, and if its edges are above the ears, and if so, restore them; then sign the edges of the wound, then close one and the other with a needle of two parts, until the vein reaches the bone, and that is by the width of the head
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	If you see it, withdraw the sponge from the artery and hold it above, cutting as much as two fingers must pass through.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is cut, if you do not keep hold of it steadily, it will continue to bleed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open with sensation, if you know that three finger-breadths measure the space, mark the [point] and withdraw until bone; what must be done is to pour out blood if six cubits, and sometimes more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the point of the spur, if the cord that follows the stitches does not reach, then strain the wound and bind, and cure it with oil until it is healed.
de emigrainne	If the artery does not open despite feeling it, if you must measure the quantity of the space of two fingers, then mark it and keep it until the bone; and what is to be done with blood that must be put out if it is more than half full, and sometimes less or more, according to what the patient can suffer, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the point of the bone where the stitches were placed, if the wound that was closed together does not move, then strain the wound and tie it, and cure it until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient secretion comes and acute catarrh, because of the tears and the choleric humours in the temples and the ancient saliva forsened and similar things, it is treated by medical cures and other things that do not benefit it, if the arteries of the temples are extracted and cauterized, as we have said
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The manner of extracting them is that if the patient makes the hair of his temples grow long, and understands the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating; and is not put back violently as in certain persons who are too rough.  If it is put back, the patient tightens his collar with some bandages, then wipes the limb of any rough hair, and raises the limb of warm water until the artery resumes its normal pulsation; then take the sponge and that which is the shape of a spatula.
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then gently stretch the skin until you see the artery, then pull it up with tweezers, and withdraw it well from the cloths that are below the shoulder; and if the artery is small, if the nail has at the tip of the elbow, then close that part according to the quantity of two fingers
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not firmly held, if it does not jump from me without pain in all things.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	Then drain blood from the groin to the navel, just over two fingers; and if the artery is large, it is prudent to ligate it with two strong threads of silk, so that no blood will remain below the support of the wound, and drain the blood; then cut away the excess that is between the two ligatures in that part, and if you see that there is still blood, cauterize with a small cautery until the hair is cut off; and that is the end of the operation, if the patient has no fever and is of warm complexion.</start_of_turn>
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is helpful to finish off moisture: because of this it is of more great aid for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the fire cautery is useful for extracting arteries that are filled with much cotton and are placed under well-made stitches; and when they are loosened, if there is no cure for dry medicines that cause new blood vessels to grow, and stitches, until they are healed; and if the artery is not stopped as it should be with the cautery, or if you use too much of the cautery, the hand will be scorched; and if you do not have this present, if you must withdraw the hand, you must do so until the hand is no longer numb, and raise the hand with cold water until the sensation returns, and strain as it should be strained; and what is milder and lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein of this cautery through a cut of about one-third of an inch, but the cut should be well thick to prevent it from burning for a longer period.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too tight, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And must have between the .ij. needles space one must have of great distance. Then when you have signed the .ij. loops, and you must let the loop burn over until it reaches the bone, and close the wound in .ij. loops; and be spaced out between the .ij. bones because it is not firmly soldered from this cautery in all. This is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	And must have between the two needles space one must have of great distance. Then when you have signed the two loops, and you must let the loop burn over until it reaches the bone, and close the wound in two loops; and be spaced out between the two bones because it is not firmly soldered from this cautery in all. This is the form of the cautery.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are above the test of the head of the sufferer, and it brings no relief from medicine what is being done, and you see the face of the patient to be swollen, and feels heat of the body if like a flame; and if there are tensed and moist if the papers are rough, and are chafed by the tears, and scorched by the heat of the tears, if there is any hope of this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	For if it is not firmly held, if it does not jump from me without pain in all things. They call it the ancient "cure contuse", and you must make the patient who has this disease let the hair grow frontwise and backward, then make three incisions or an even front according to the length of the front; and let one of the incisions be as long as two teeth should be, with two costles below the paper, and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and let there be a wound about the quantity of three teeth between the joints; and put a piece of sponge and a cloth under the wound to soak up the blood, then tighten the sponge with two fingers, which is like this shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is over the temple down to the second incision; and remove all the bone that is between the two incisions to the very surface of the bone, then make the other half of the wound down to the other second, and then take out this instrument.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first incision the instrument which is called the “cultellaire,” which is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, does not penetrate deeply, and is smooth, that is the shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the knife-edge towards the marrow at the knee, and the knife-edge towards the bone, and keep it there until it reaches the middle fissure.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut the veins that descend from the head as far as the incision is continuous until it reaches the knee, and then do the rest in the middle fissure until the other end; then drain the blood equally, and express the limb for the blood taken; then put in the wound a small patch of cotton, and put on wet cloths soaked in wine and oil and balsam, and keep the wound closed; and at the third hour remove the dressing, and mix in great quantity of fresh rue, and treat the wound with basilicon oil and rosemary oil, and other cures for wounds in general until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
dou reume des eulz	because of the return of the blood vessels
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When no acute cautery is done, and you see the eyes tense and small, and the pupil dilates, and the papers burn; the hair cries out, and where it breaks off, there is great pain, and the patient vomits; then the discharge from these causes is greater than from many veins, and the cure is that which is.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And command the patient to rear his forehead, then make a great fissure from ear to ear, and another of good size at the other.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And commence from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and grasp your hand from the nerves of the temples that move toward the ear; and when the bone is exposed, if there is blood, drain all the blood with a sponge, and then dry between the two layers of the incision and put in cotton wool, and try to hold it in place; then cover with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil, and keep it from moving about; when it has healed, it is good to rub the bone until it begins to grow back, and then treat with drying things that cause it to harden.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In part: take three parts of flower of fennel and three parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and apply it to these wounds to swell up all around.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	And so be careful and wide in the opening. And as for the most subtle chief of the ear according to the quantity of the patient’s suffering, then follow with all the antidote; do this often until you see it issue. And if it does not obey to issue, if I push around the cotton around the ear as I said at the stone; and if it still does not issue, if we have said, give distillations which the ancients have proved useful in the incision of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, in this way: Let silver or lead be split into small pieces, and above put on distillations; and pressing from these instruments, let there be a raiser and encircle the point immediately with cotton; then pour out your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the can; and let the can be in the ear; then press from the raiser all around the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or almost until the ear is emptied; and let the patient feel within, and let the distillations be neither too hot nor too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Whatever is causing the swelling of the ears is one of three things: grains of sand, pieces of metal, stones, or other such things; seeds, such as peas, beans, or barley; or pus, which is watery and foul smelling.</start_of_turn>
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it is chipped in the earlobe or any other way that does not fit into the ear, do not put it in the ear, but put the ear on the sole of the foot.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if it does not secrete any purple oil or poppy seed oil, then order its extraction; and make him spit out the seeds, and stamp his nose when he spits, and put around his ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear down.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times blood comes out because of this treatment; and if it does not come out, order its extraction as thin needles are formed: for this is the way:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it bursts out with needles, that is good; if not, perform an extraction with fine needles; and if it does not burst with the needle, make a scar on the side of the ear or remove a large part of the ear, and wipe away what is around the scar with butter if it comes out without the needle; then the blood will flow, for often it comes out by itself; and if it does not come out in this way, take hold of the testicles and put on no instrument that can cause damage, and put a plug of cotton in; then press on the testicles above the stone or whatever it is, and the blood will flow.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things do not suffice, if you are in haste to make an incision, do not hesitate to perform the incision above the earlobe as well as on the abscess. Incise the earlobe cautiously first, making the initial incision at the crown of the head; let blood escape according to its quantity. Then hold the patient between your hands and turn the ear downwards, make a small incision at the root of the earlobe, either at the fat or the cartilage. The incision should be as wide as a moon until you reach the bone, and then remove the bone as much as you are able. Exude the pus from your mouth and leave the wound until it has healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If the grain is swollen and painful, administer extraction; if it cannot be extracted, administer a sponge tencel soaked in vinegar in this fashion:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and order the incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this until you think the grain is moistened by the moisture of the ear, until you have made many incisions; then extract with thin needles and suck, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	When the ear is acutely painful, then the patient must immediately use an ointment first, and fill the ear with much cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And if there is no longer any pain in that ear, or if the pain persists.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it is burst, that is good
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it does not burst, take many stones according to the length of your finger should tighten and loosen, and put the patient one or two of his ears out, and pull from the other side of his ears; and burn from another piece on the piece that is in the ear; and do this burning from piece to piece until the pain is all gone, and when it is burst, if you see it, take an onion, and put one of the heads in the ear, and the other head put to the fire as much as the onion is round; then do the rest of the onions until the pain is all gone, as we have said concerning the stone
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the wisdom tooth, if it is of little bone, as like a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great bone we must feel it, if it brings about the extraction of teeth; and that is the lightest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of the worms in the ear, when you cure as we have said in the division and or treat with distillations, and the cure does not benefit, if you must know that the ear is exposed to the sun: if there are no worms to be seen, if the boils are small, and if they are not seen, take tweezers of this kind:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let the hair grow wide and abundant.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And keep the hair more sparse at the root of the ear in proportion to the severity of the patient’s suffering, then act quickly to all the pain; do this often until you see that it is healing.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey this, if I am forced to stretch the cotton wool around the wound as I have said in the stone; and if they do not bleed as I have said, administer distillations that the former have proven useful in the incision of worms, and you will find them or treat them with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And so be careful and wide in the opening.
