Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some imperfection in their ears; and the same thing happens as adults with wounds or earwax that has become impacted. Such impacts never depart without leaving a mark on the ear, if we are not able to see them; and never happens without some loss of hearing, which we see well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When such impact departs without being seen, it is a sign of serious disease in many cases, and in this case it is seen that you put the painful ear into the sunlight; look inside: if you see pus dripping, if the wound has all the pus, this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And so be attentive both front and back all around, if it does not bleed the ear; if the pus is of earwax or a piece of the ear, if you see small teeth and the lump is lighter, as much as the bone is whole.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the shoulder dislocation is caused by moisture, take a slight lever and hold a little fire under it, then put or bind up the ear.</start_of_turn
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel swelling at the ear which the patient complains of, pierce lightly, and hold back the nerves of the ear; then insert a plug into the ear according to the size of the opening, and pour in oil of Egyptian origin.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not do anything until the wound is healed, or take a sponge soaked in rose-water and powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear flee, it is likely that you have pulled out the plug and put in another sponge soaked in oil of rose and wax until the swelling subsides.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If there is discharge of blood, soak a sponge and cover with cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that will staunch the bleeding which are either to apply distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of paper scrolls.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Thus comes the paper from the eyes when they are moist and dry, if you extend them with thumbs and nails, and grasp with the tip of a spatula from their roots; then withdraw the vitreous body bruised
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if you do not take care, if you burn with the lenticular cautery, after the incision it is worth moving; and often it breaks, so that nothing remains of their roots; and when they are burned by fire, their roots are scorched and do not come back anymore
de la gresle	Of the scab.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come together in paper writings of ulcers of various things that seem to wrinkle in their form and in their duration, and for this reason this disease is called "granulin", and is an assembly of great moisture in the substance of the papules and the outside; the work is like this: take hold when the granulin moves from one side to the other, and it is a light matter to know; make the wound wide, then slightly burn the surrounding area, then take hold as hooks, and bind.</start_of_turn>
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not perceive that the papule covers the wound, if it does not grieve the patient; and if the wound is great, if the collection has a bulge, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not use force, for the swelling will restore itself quickly and cause pain.</start_of_turn
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granulin descends downwards towards the ear towards the upper part, if you reverse the limb, and extend the granulin with one grasp, and close and press from one side to the other; and if the tissue is loosened by the incision, this will cause no harm; and when the granulin is closed, if you leave the dirty oil, cure the limb of what is left behind until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the blood.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is enclosed in paper tissues, and this happens more in stupid people, and grieve much at their eyes, and they come with tears at dawn, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears are hastening at their eyes; and because of this they sleep with their faces down, and they sleep on, and their papers are soaked with their tears which swell and appear to cover them with exinach that bursts in oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your hand to your side and feel the exinach between your shoulders.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	If the patient puts his head in his sound health; then take one linen cloth and make a loop in the manner of a circle according to the quantity of oily exudate from the chest part, and put it on; and press on the thumbs from one side and the other, so that the exudate is assembled together like the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture a trench with a wide incision, and let it not be more extensive than the wound made to the vein; and make the leather tough as long as you see the exudate; and in various situations comes exudate from the incision, according to the shape of a white fatty piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out all the fatty tissue between your thumbs at the back of your hands, and twist your hand to the right and to the left as much as possible; and keep that you do not put anything into the incision, until you have reached the oil, that you do not stain it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it escapes not at the beginning of the incision, if you widen the incision slightly as much as it opens; then extract it as we have said, and moisten the bandage in oil and water, and put on the limb, and bind tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who break their bones and put on to corrupt this moisture that is remaining
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the doctor must cure it as long as he is sane
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to the vein being cut, if the cure of cautery has healed as it should be sane.
des poilz des papieres	paper hair
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like substances grow hairs, adjust them other than their natural state, and are thickened, if they prick the eyes, they cause tears like customary tears and soften the papers and mucus, up to the point of destroying the eyes; the cure for this is threefold: either by entire fire cautery, or by medicine according to what is before or alongside the cautery, or it is made by incision and suture or by strings, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the patient’s head in your left hand, then draw the paper from its root; if it is straightened, it is good; if not, if there is a splinter at any point of the root, either cut off the margin of the paper or the hairs will be torn out; and take one thread at the base of the paper and draw it to the tip; then stretch in the lower part of the paper, remove the hairs that have been adjusted, over the whole area, from the large tear until the small; then draw out one thread and place on the paper a small patch of cotton and bandage, then mark on the paper a sign like the spur of a myrtle, and it is known that the sign should be according to the quantity you see that the paper that is destined for you has been elevated.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If the vein is cut, and the cautery has healed, as it should be. If there is a portion that has gone black with thick blood, then make a large incision two lines above the navel and from the great toe to the heel; and if there is a wound from the natural hair in the thickness of an almond, then insert the sponge into one of the two angles as close as possible, then draw the edges together; then sew the two layers together with a fine needle and strong thread, and wipe away the surplus of thread from the two edges, as you see me doing; if this is not done, if there is no improvement, then leave the stitches in for three days or four. Then cure the wound with dry and constricting things, for the blood will gather up at the bottom of the wound and reunite the tissues, but the stitches are useless (as the old people say), and this is done in vain; or if there is another method: and that you mark the blood with a figure that is just like the head of a berry, as we have been told, at three inches distance according to the form that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then grasp what covers it with small forces equally according to the shape which is like this:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are unable to hold the nails, and the thing is not equal, take a needle or two, and pass one thread through the larger loop, and the second thread through the smaller loop, and gather between your two fingers the two threads equally; then keep your hand equally, and keep all the skin above that which you have signed, as we have said; and gather the two layers of the wound by suture, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, if you apply cerate and some other soothing substances. Never have I seen that the hair of a patient has been converted: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for boils is as follows: convert the beard and hair downwards as I have said, then make three incisions by art, and three threads as long as the beard and expand with mustard seed; and put in three hairs or hold the threads. Then assemble the one and the other securely above what is covered by beard oil, and strain the three hairs of the three parts. Leave it like that for several days, and the skin which has been strained will become black and dry and will fall out, as long as it persists.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the wound has a great force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound has healed, and if there is still blood, and it will not stop bleeding; and this is the form of two nails you will make following this figure, and following this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a needle with its subtle thread; and there is.i. a silken thread which is subtle; then join the heads together and do not leave one and the other subtle, and let the length of the threads be equal; then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk briefly, and do not leave the chief of the thread; then put the patient's head in its place; and let the sun go if the work is clarified, for this is a subtle and minor work; then draw out the needle throughout the chase at the root of the hair in the armpit, and make it pierce in the paper hastily as much as you can; then draw out the hair until it is at the chase, and bring back to the chase that hair, if there is.i. or .ij. or .iij. or more; then draw out your hand until the vein comes out throughout the chase in the paper with the natural movement.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase to the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase vein comes out from the hole and you see it by the sight of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair has grown back in its place and the wound has healed.
de la porriture de l’oil	From the putrefaction of the oil.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this ailment which is called 'aleacrati' or the putrefaction comes to light, if there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And there comes from the wound, or from a cut or cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way of working in this is that you make the suture, dry the flesh, put in stitches of linen, and leave it until it is healed; and do not do anything except use in the treatment of it things that dry and restrain
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, if the disease returns worse than before; but there is need for softening things, such as fennel; and alum or salt and linseed seeds boiled, and fat ointment melted in no oil, and it covers a cloth, and treats this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you must keep guard that it does not heal in a different form than before; and these works that we have mentioned are not fierce but only with regard to this disease, that it does not return in a different form than before.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the wound that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is often called «axacrati», is natural and sudden.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The cause of this disease comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of the disease progresses is that if you prick with a needle, if it has two roots, and the pith in the flesh, it causes the three-quarters of the blood in the vein to bleed out immediately; then the flesh above all the needle is raised up to the height of the wound, and the wound is about the size of a large almond.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the limb returns to its normal position as it should, that is good; but if not, take a pair of forceps and place them in the wound, and draw the limb out, make two incisions or cut through the flesh; and if the two incisions are at a right angle to the incision which you made, make one angle so that when they are put together, the limb forms the shape of a letter which does not have two right angles; then break the bone according to the quantity of its costae and the disease, of what will sustain the flesh, and then join the two severed parts together with a thread of silk; then treat this as we have said of the mollifying medicines and bandages, until it is healed
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the disease comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if it is recommended that you make a full incision over the hairs of paper; and as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the learned doctors appear to know everything from great poverty to great wealth as to how to restore the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is to be done of the work and the instruments in many situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	If the disease comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if it is recommended that you make a full incision over the hairs of paper; and as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the learned doctors appear to know everything from great poverty to great wealth as to how to restore the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is to be done of the work and the instruments in many situations.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling arises at home in a part as delicate as the nail of the thumb is soothed with oil, and cannot move or perform its natural works, if it is recommended that you should bathe the tip of a scraper over the swelling, and hold it high up; and extend as many times as necessary, until you have reached the point where the pain is neither too great nor too slight, so that the patient can endure neither too much pressure nor too little; and that your incision, which you will make to reassemble, be light, so that the nail returns to its natural shape; and all the reassembled parts must be thoroughly cleansed, and no longer bathed in salt-laden water, but in fresh water, and oil; and between the nail and the oil place a layer of linen, and cover with oiled wool in abundance; and afterwards apply poultices and other soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nails of the oil are two kinds: one is nervinous and seems like hard paste, and the other is not nervinous but seems like white moisture frozen; when one touches them with iron and boils them, they do not burn; both seem to commence towards the great marrow, and cross so much that they cover the whole cavity, light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his hand in his side, then opens the wound; and keep the hand at your side, then grasp the nail with pincers of little double curvature, and stretch it upwards; then take a needle, and put in one hair of horse, or of sheep, or of beef, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and fix it in the nail, and pierce through the whole needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it upwards, and wash away to the outside of the nail all the surrounding tissue that encompasses the nail and the hair to the hair, and leave the natural fat or marrow, if there are no tears usually from the incision; and in no case is the nail stretched only with the incision and the thread, as we have said; then it is washed with all the surrounding fat so that it is like this:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the spatula does not touch the fatty tissue and break it, and that the needle is not perceived; and after the incision pour in oil a little ball of bruised silk, and put on a collar of litarge, and leave it until the other side; then cure what is left until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot push out the needle, and the thread cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail of medicine is cured; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if the patient is feverish, take the spatula slightly blunt as in this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the nail superficially, and if you see that it has diminished point and the bone is pressed, if the liquid distills from your mouth into the oil collar of litarge and red ligature and bruised silk, and squeeze out the oil until the other side; then repeat the other work as before, until it is entirely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing hinders thee in the oil, as with an abscess, then milk, and first cure the abscess with fire until it is healed, and then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if there appears cartilage softened at night in the oil by great discomfort, if you suspend it to the bone, cut off a part and not all, that blood does not arise; then distill in the oil of colera red which is made of litharge.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that comes from the navel.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige. de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not fierce but dull, which is assembled in oil, resembling descending ice, and it is not truly ice; and the manner in which it appears is that if you make the patient sit on a comfortable and straight chair, and you grasp the chief between your hands from two parts, and move it until you see the dullness coming towards your eyes; then either bind it tightly, and do not let it go down, or break the light, and see the patient the things as he alone would see them; and if it does not come down even after that, consider that it is ice, and that when it comes down it is not noticeable as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. des aigues de l’oil	When the belly of the oil is swollen, it is not fire that causes it but the oil itself which is thick and sticky like descending water; and it is not so. de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint to the elbow.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	From the shoulder to the elbow often arises a disease called "telul," which grows and becomes very large, to the extent that it is seen as an abnormal thing; and because of this it is commanded that you should begin by applying pressure at the start, and then break the bone, then apply the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay in applying pressure until it is large, if you do not take precautions, it swells with blood, poor sense, and great pain: for if you touch it with iron, it is an inflamed abscess. For when it is once treated, if there is no blood swelling, you can see that you can easily control it; if the abscess is of soft touch, not of blood swelling, and you see that you can control it, you must evacuate the patient and control it in a timely manner, and treat the limb with drying and restraining things.
