Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Do not do this until you have ascertained that the solution of the continuation has come in one of these recent works; for in some homes it is of benefit, because in others it is not.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not happen to any, if you see that the wound is fresh throughout its entirety; then join the two layers with a staple, and cure until it is healed. If the layers are already separated at one end and the other, if you suspect that you must support all the parts around it until they are firm, then join the two layers with a staple, and strain, and sprinkle on powdered dragon's blood, and incense. Then place over the powders a piece of firm or other adhesive dressing, and leave it until it bleeds by itself, then cure until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the splint is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we have said in the belly splint; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the fractures of the thumbs
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, in the hands of the physician, are diverse wounds that resemble grains of barley, minor and greater; thus it is commanded to grasp the wound and make incisions around each hair, and grasp them with tweezers and pull them out from their root. Then apply pressure to the wound after the incision of the vitriol broth, until the bleeding has ceased. Finally, remove the dressing and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the root of the jaw.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times it happens that there is an abscess on the gums that the old people call "albulus"; if you support it, grasp the root and pull out the swelling or the blood; then put out the vitriol broth or other restraining and drying powders; and if the swelling returns after the incision, and happens many times, if you grasp it a second time and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; this is the shape of the instruments to carry out this work.</start_of_turn>
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	The teeth are never together at the root, between the gums, where the teeth are white and sharp; and never are the teeth black and yellow and toward, until the decay comes to the gum, and the teeth are biting; if you command that the patient sit between your hands, and their head be still, and open the teeth or the gums will burst, until nothing remains; and then you will make black and green, and yellow and other stains, as long as they remain; and if one breaks what is at the first root, that is good; if not, if you must repeat the second and third time, until you have everything back; and teeth that have had to move from various instruments to repair them, as this is what the work shows, for these teeth have other shapes than those that are between the teeth. And these shapes and others will appear to you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth from its pain that you leave it too long without treating it, because one must not be ashamed to do so; for it is a material that is highly moist, therefore one has no excuse for neglecting it
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is groaning with pain, if you suspect that he is about to faint, you must be certain that he will not be able to do so.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	There is often pain in the patient, and care must be taken that it is neither too great nor too little; and make the patient groan with the pain; and although the pain does not depart completely because of this, as long as the illness persists, for we have already wanted to make them endure it; and when you are well certain that he will faint, if you suspect that he is about to faint, then you must support his head and shoulders firmly with your hands at the first moment and moment until they are well fixed; and then confirm them well. And let the patient groan between your knees, and hold him firmly so that he does not move
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After that, if the tooth is loosened in the direction of breaking, and if it does not come loose immediately, take no instruments and hold it in the cheek slightly lower, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is seen to be fractured and broken, if it is recommended that it be filled with cloths, lay or pierce it; and if it is strained secretly, that it does not break while straining; and it is recommended to rinse salt over the gum around the tooth to soften the tooth
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take care that you do not break it further, and leave some of it, and return to the patient with the greater pain of the first time.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Take care that you do not do what the ignorant layman do, who break the jaw at every opportunity and do not heed what we have told them; but they bring no remedy for the great disease except for the roots which remain, or the jaw which is broken. As we have often seen, when the tooth is extracted, wash the blood from the wine or oil and salt; and if there is still blood, often happens, apply a little vitriol broth; and if that does not suffice, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of instruments, on which one must keep silence first, are either with long points and thick handles, that they do not double in number when you draw out the tooth; these are the shapes.
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of large limbs if they do not bend when drawing out, and be of iron well made, and be toothed so that one may hold them.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains fixed at the shoulder, if you must put out the moist cotton swab that is in the wound, do so with care lest you break it.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	While the limb is soft, because there are teeth that are split apart like nails, which makes the head of the shoulder appear like a beak of a bird; and they must be made as with a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not suffice to withstand all these tensions, if you must uncover the flesh completely around the root, and place the instrument which is called «althali», namely tweezers, so that this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it must be forced and large so that it does not break, and if the root leaps by this means, that is good; if not, if you aid with all your instruments, so that the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has teeth, so that this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments that are before the teeth, and this instrument that seems like a great clamp, whose form is like this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And other instruments that are before the teeth, and this instrument that seems like a great clamp, whose form is like this; or that its force is such that it cannot break, and its jaws like those of instruments for teeth; and like other instruments which are not mentioned here; the master surgeon will find himself alone with his instrument, according to what his work and his illness show, for there are many diseases for which no instrument is taught in former times; and if it breaks not from bone or from any other part, or if it is necessary, if it seeks other instruments, as I have said, and helps him with gestures, for whose form is like this.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and firm to hold the bone, that it escapes not, but can hold and restrain; and then restore the limb of medicine that is convenient for this, and if there is inflammation in the bone, and it is small, if the disease has passed with all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear contrary to their natural course, and the shape is deformed, even among women of gentle birth, if it is suspected that the tooth is deeply lodged and cannot emerge naturally, and is not properly aligned, it cannot be soothed or comforted: therefore, extract it. And if it is close to the tooth, take hold of this instrument which is like a small beak, and which is made of iron without a sharp edge at the base:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And hold it there with the thumbs and palms of your hands for the duration of the extraction, and because of that do not move the others, and if it appears, you can limber it, if you file a piece of file like this which is the shape of it.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is like filing nails; and while holding the tooth firmly with the thumbs and palms of your hands, slightly move the instrument to and fro, so that it does not move too much, and when you finish, leave no burr, for if the tooth is too deeply lodged and it bleeds the tongue, you must remove the sharp edges as much as possible so that it does not bleed the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth is loose.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth loosen, by percussion or chewing, and the patient cannot press on anything that will cause them to bleed, and you must treat them with restrictive medicines, which is of no use; if you must restrain them with a gold wire, for the silver wire becomes green and falls out, but the wound does not move.  If the wire is neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are aligned, take the wire and pass it double between the two front teeth, then place the head of the shoulder between the teeth that are next to each other, if there is one or more of them, until you see it is level up to the sound tooth on the other side; then resume the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and carefully, until it does not move; and if the wound is at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the head of the arm with a pair of forceps, assemble them, and bring them between the sound teeth; and hold them in place until they bleed no more. And leave them in place as tightly as possible, until they loosen or the thread breaks, or the strain of another thread; if it persists and serves its purpose, that is the form of teeth and the arrangement of the two front teeth, and the two lower teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let nothing interfere that is not wise and soothing, and never make the form of a tooth of a cow’s jaw, and put it back in its place or where the defect is, and strain it as we have said, and hold and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper, lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is this thread which comes from the tongue or nature that is not born anew; or by accident of a deep wound; and the work is such that you see the mouth of the patient, and put your hand in his mouth, and take hold of the tongue; then grasp the large nerve until the tongue is loosened from its dwelling, and if there is any delay or not, and that is a sign of healing, if the wound is dressed and grasped tightly; and keep that the wound is not too deep, for the artery which is from the tongue; and when you have done this, if you lift the pale and easy blood, or cold blood, then put the tongue back with a little tension; and bind the patient tightly at night, so that the wound cannot be soothed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood comes out, take out the glass vessel that is bleeding; and if it does not stop, cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with other treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see pus of a color or black or hard, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a abscess; and if it is declining and there is moisture, if it spurts blood, grasp the cautery with a sponge and deliver from both parts; and if it does not stop your work, if necessary, apply a piece of vitriol to the tip until it is blackened, then return to your work until you have completed your procedure; then raise the limb easily and gently, and treat the wound further until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes comes from the throat black spots which are called "godath", and these spots have two almonds properly placed, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is abscesses of small size and color like rust, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, even though blood comes out; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will take it out, or it will break by itself; and if it is white in color and the root is thin, if you have brought the instrument to cover it, but look first if the abscess is relaxed and calm
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit before the sun, and let the arm be at ease, cover the mouth with the hand, and grasp the genitals between the hands, and press the tongue down to the very instrument, as it is the form; and let it be of silver or gold as fine as a needle.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	The abscesses of the throat.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you can grasp it with tweezers, know that this is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you can grasp it with tweezers, know that this is its form: grasp one claw at a time; when you have grasped one claw, grasp the other in the same way, and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm, bitter, and soothing liquid; when blood spurts out, if there are pomegranate seeds or myrtle berries or similar things in the vomit, until the stain is gone; then wash the wound until it is healed. Never again shall there be any other incisions in the throat except for the two claws, if you grasp them as they are always grasped.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I prescribe for a woman who has an abscess in the throat, which is to say a small abscess; and I must keep the throat closed tightly so that the woman cannot breathe through the passage that is blocked, and cannot eat or drink, and she would die if she remained like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it forced two grains of barley out through the two holes that were not closed
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I had eaten much and drank wine in abundance, and had lain in one place, then went forth with fiery fever; and with fiery pain I bore a great portion of the bow. Then I returned to the other side, where I found the tongue bound, and the throat oppressed. Having bound the other limb in these abscesses, and having closed one part, I left only a little blood; and the woman who was with me plucked out the cord of the throat, and we began to drink water and wine, and I did not cease biting at that abscess for a long time. And the abscesses rejoined again, and filled up my mouth as much as I could bear; so I embraced it and cauterized it within the throat: and thus I went away from those parts, and only God knows what happened to me afterwards.
de l’uve	De l’uve, le feu ne doit être appliqué que quand les poils sont longs et égaux; et si l’on le pique à la racine, garder les yeux ferme jusqu’à ce qu’ils ne flottent plus.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the limb hangs downward, and it is fleeing and is long, it is called "perpendiculaire"; and if it is large and round, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit me, and you see that the surrounding skin is calm, and it is soft, if you must, you must hold it firmly; and that which is round and thick is not long; and it is bloodstained or dark-yellow or black, if you must avoid the incision of the latter.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril upon the patient.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, as I have said, according to its color and length, you must make the patient sit in the sun and press the tongue with the instrument which we mentioned before; then put the ointment on the limb and draw out the wound, and hold it with two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two thumbs.</start_of_turn
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must know that you should not cover more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; for if you do more, it will grieve the voice and the ear; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, you must know that you should use an engine in the cautery in the direction of the fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of cautery must be gentle and slow
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And that the patient places his head in his sound condition, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or the treatise of cautery, and grasp with live forceps, if it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, for it is thus formed:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you have put on a bandage or something to put the medicine on, if like the hairs of a sickle, put the instrument over the medicine on the navel; and the patient must rest on his side, so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth from the medicine inwards, if it does not reach the throat, and the hiccup; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it on the navel, for the amount of half an hour, until you see it wrinkled and the medications of the medicine are appeased; and if you see that, take hold and cover with any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and remove the instrument from the wound as much as the cotton fills it; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it dry and wipe off after three or five days. And if you must renew the cautery of the medicine, if you renew it, and after the cautery wipe off the surrounding with cotton wool, and pack what is around the medicine; and rise up cold water, and be cured of hiccups until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is more effective than incision, for it is cured by fumigation according to this manner. Take calamine and isops and origanum and rue and chamomile and avron and similar herbs. Assemble all or some of them in one pot, put in oil, and boil. Make sure the pot is well sealed with strong earth, and put in one instrument that has a handle according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be it of silver or gold, or be it one of the bones broken in the mouth of the patient until the vapor ascends to the nose by the vinegar, until the nose be mortified; after which, it must be repeated often, until the nose dries, and keep that you do this only from the commencement of the outbreak of the fever, for many things happen; do not do this before the outbreak of the fever.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, if you take vinegar and put in the chief of the patient an egg shell, so that the patient’s mouth does not become too hot; for the egg shell does not make the vapor rise up through the mouth, and this is a good remedy altogether for health
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened at the throat bone or fish spine, or nothing at all; if you therefore suspect that you see something, press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing; and what does not appear to you and remains in the throat, you must make the patient vomit the morbid; for by chance if it comes out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or some hardened bread; and tie the sponge to one thread, and then transfix it. And when it comes back, if it is swollen, then draw it out; and if it does not come out of what we have said, take one instrument of sponge according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the instrument is bent at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily and the head is raised up; keep your hands away from the epiglottis, for if you touch it, you will lose consciousness; do not press too hard on the bone inwards; and move the instrument only as much as necessary, for if the patient coughs or the thing is reversed, it will be all the same.
de la sansue de la gorge	If the instrument is bent at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily and the head is raised up; keep your hands away from the epiglottis, for if you touch it, you will lose consciousness; do not press too hard on the bone inwards; and move the instrument only as much as necessary, for if the patient coughs or the thing is reversed, it will be all the same.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is medicine without sense, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sun, and that you press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the shoulder, if it has a slight twist at the top or has subluxation that is worth this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this is not worth it, take a purgative medicine, and make the patient swallow it down with a gulp of water; then make a slight incision with the needle and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	If the patient experiences acute pain all over.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full view of the face, cover the mouth, and make the patient vomit in the direction of swallowing, and move his hand frequently; and if the patient still experiences pain in the shoulder, then pierce him with the needle again
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not pierce him as we have said, if you fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will be of use to him
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And concerning fumigation, if you take one pot or there are charcoal pieces visible, cover the patient’s face with a veil, and in that hole put the head of the instrument; then pour the fumigation, and the patient puts their chief of the cane in their mouth, closes their mouth, so that the smoke does not go out, but comes out only at the nose; and the nose will now sneeze, and if it does not sneeze, restart the fumigation many times; and the patient will suffer thirst, and will eat dirty and vile things, and will not drink water; and then it will be necessary that it be driven out by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument is thus that which we mentioned in treating the nose, if indeed it can be seen, resembles a pair of hooked tongs to enter the throat; and it has the shape of a beak of a rooster, and has lime-peel, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and thus is the form
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The wounds of boils are, as it is remembered in this book, diverse in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which they are similar, one of which is in their appearance alone, and the other in that they hold moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And in the second method, if it is for the arm or if it is at the bone.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the swelling at the head is different from that at the root, and the swelling at the bone is different from that which comes at the joints, and the bones have their judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if the swelling does not need to be pierced, as long as the limb is limp according to its completion; but if there are such ones that it is necessary to pierce when it is hardened, and does not die according to its completion, like an abscess which is in the joints
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	for when the swelling comes from the joints, and it is left as long as it is rigid, by chance if the vein and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because of this there is contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if an abscess is pierced too late, when it is already grown large, it will go to the principal limb; or if it is pierced too deep, if the perforation is not made high enough, it will not suffice. One must only pierce the abscess in the forward direction, following digestion, except for that which is pierced too deep, which must not penetrate too far, but must be left along, and thus an fistula will form; and it will not heal in great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it must be known that you should close the wound of the apostemes that is dead according to its companion, when the pain is calmed, and the departure of fever, and the cessation of pain and redness, and the swelling and the tingling of the head of the apostemes, and other signs; and that you should make the perforation or more dependent on the apostemes, and the place where the wound appeared; and that the perforation should be long enough for the hand or foot, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and on all bones equally or there should be no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, the limb is hanging down by its side.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh, if it is left to fester for a long time without being confirmed in digestion, as we have said before
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before this, if it has been left to fester, it will swell and cause the flesh to burst with foul breath; and by chance it will harden the veins and pierce them to the depth of the abscess
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no wound that is perceived according to the great pain, according to what the limb has suffered.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it must be known that you must bring in small wounds, small incisions; in great wounds, great incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the wound; and if there are such wounds or it must be suspected that the wound is deeper than it appears, and if there is suspicion of infection, if it has become as thick as a drape and is softened, if it is possible to do so like we do with boils: and if there are such wounds that are split into three angles, and such as we cope with the burr of a nutmeg, like wounds of anger; and if there are such wounds that we make circular, and other sizes and similar to those that we cauterize.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	He who has no head, if he has a superficial wound, must know that you must pierce him directly; and know that when the wound is large and has gathered great blood, and you pierce him, if you do not drain all the blood at once, but only a part, then stamp the wound up to the other side, and do not do anything else; do this many times until the blood is gone; even if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman in childbirth, or young children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For indeed, experience teaches us never to hope for the issue of the blood except in the case of death of the patient; and you will not be blamed for it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have recognized the wound, if it is small, leave the wound alone; and if it is a large wound, if there is much bleeding, do not attempt to stop it with linen or old cotton; if it is a large wound and there is much bleeding, and you have squeezed out a portion of blood, if you have split the skin of the wound, and you have closed it, do not fill it with anything but fine cotton or flaxseed soaked in moisture, and leave it for a third of an hour; then remove the bone and cure the wound until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood flows from a wound during the work, if you mix cold and pure water with vinegar, and soak it up, draw out the offending discharge many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If blood continues to flow from the wound during the work, if you mix in cold nourishment and healing herbs as I have mentioned previously in this book, and if it is summer or the wound is painful, if there is suspicion that there is nerve damage, you must put on tight bandages and soak with vinegar and oil; and if that does not work, soak with cold water and oil or with vinegar and oil, up to a third of the way, as we have said; then remove the dressing and dry the wound, if possible, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is known throughout in the treatment of abscesses: or as I have said before concerning the precautions before treating abscesses, and thus in this chapter.
des soros	And this is known throughout in the treatment of abscesses: or as I have said before concerning the precautions before treating abscesses, and thus in this chapter.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or care of chief comes petty aftershocks, and are managed by us as are in tapestries, as the joist of a beam, and mouthfuls of it appear like something.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Or there are some that are fat and such as those where there is moisture like mice; and if there are such as are hard and rough at the navel, and there is no doubt that the artery will not oppose it
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of its size is that you expect all the instruments that are called "endoscopes", from which the shape comes afterwards, whatever thing it contains
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, if the liquid flows from long ago.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, if you leave the peel that contains that moisture, it will return in its place when you leave it alone; then soak cotton wool Egyptian style, if it is present; if not, in water and vinegar, and apply the bandage, and leave it until the other side; and that will correct what is remaining that is demented
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the burn comes round again, as before, the second and the third time, until you are certain that it does not stay put at night; then cure the wound opportunely, as is right.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the wound remains open after the fat has solidified, if the wound follows this form, long; and the pus runs out, and the edges are scorched, and put all your care in place for the dressing, or where the blood is; and if the artery is opposed, do what I have said afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same with an abscess if it is painful, and cut and cure as I have said before
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the size of the incision for a painful abscess and moisture, if it is less severe, because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are any abscesses or swellings or if there is no moisture, and if these are old abscesses that I cauterise or swellings of a woman in her old age; and if I find the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and cannot break it; and if there is no sign of healing, we must make as good a wound as if it were a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head or the root of the ear, forasmuch as they come from the neck and the roots of the ears, they burst open every day even the most dependent of the limb; and they must be treated as they should be treated.</start_of_turn>
des scrophules	And the size on the pierced abscess and moisture, if it is less severe, because they are of little blood. Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	If you prick the vein or artery, and this prevents you from working, put in the wound a bit of vitriol broth, or any powders that remain bloodless, and hold the wound; and leave it until the swelling has subsided, and soften the wound, and begin to work.

When the swelling has subsided, if you return to your work, as long as you accomplish it; then whenever you must do something, if there remain no small abscesses, cope and crush them.</start_of_turn>

And if there is in the root of the abscess a large vein, if you cannot do anything but grasp that abscess at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread, and leave it hanging free; then apply the wound with much cotton wool, smeared with Egyptian balsam, and cure.</start_of_turn

si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	Know that you must grasp the root of the matter, treat the cause, and sew as we have said

The swelling that remains will disappear when the matter has been grasped and the cause treated, in accordance with what has been said; if there is remaining swelling, this is due to corruption; and when the wound is thoroughly cleansed, if the wound has been thoroughly drained of pus, as long as it is healthy.
de squinance	When the wound is well drained, if you apply an ointment dressing that is healing, as long as it is healthy.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old men spoke of the greatness of the gorge; but I have never seen it in our land, and that is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	As to those who grumble, it is right that the swelling of the gorge which is called the epiglottis must be cut away; and this will not help, for all the veins and the blood vessels of the patient are at those who have placed their trust in them in the mouth, in the throat or in the ears.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the chest of the belly, it is right to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, when our voices tear the epiglottis, to cut them three circles or four, slightly through, between the two circles or in the quantity of the fissure from the surface; and if the cartilage is soft, it is convenient to join the epiglottis immediately so that there is no swelling and the blood vessels are long

If the master is fearful, if you command him to extend the skin of the throat to the chin, then cut the earlobe as far as it goes to the nail; and avoid the blood vessels, for if you see nothing, then close the wound; and if necessary, ligate the artery, as we have said; and demonstrate by the section of the smoke of the nail that the spur has escaped from the broken bone, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and doubt about strangulation persists, assemble the upper and lower eyelids of the wound with the thumb and index finger, and hold them together with the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause the hair to grow, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	The patient must not do this until the throat is completely healed, and the patient is deemed to be dying, and the default is to leave it alone.</start_of_turn
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, ligate the epiglottis because the patient cannot move, and he breathes through the wound; and thus is preserved from death. And for this reason they command the old man to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it is passed in three days or four. And then they command to suture the wound and cure it, when it is cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a damsel took a knife, plunged it into her throat, and cut part of her windpipe; and I fled called for help, and found her as dead.

I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and saw that it did not penetrate any vein or artery except for the throat, and that the cause of this was the wound itself.</start_of_turn
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and dressed the wound, and cured it until it healed; and the damsel did not suffer except that her voice was hoarse, and returned after a while; for in the surgery of the epiglottis I did not find any fear
de la grosse gorge	of the great gullet.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	These abscesses are called "throat hernia," and are great abscesses in the color of jaundice, and are very common in women; and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; or the natural one has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement. des nous	And encircle all around, and cure it as it should be, until it is completely healed.

I say that dislocation is caused by heat and fever that persist, as long as the inflammation has not passed, and is accompanied by swelling; then rest the fever and heat.

Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of the inquiry of abscesses of the body is that you take more moisture from the wound than you find in the abscess, and press your thumbs and fingers until you feel that the instrument has grasped the knot, then do what is suitable for the size of the abscess; then draw out the entraumeatus and take care of what may spur out.

Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the entromittent instruments, and they are of three kinds: great, medium, and small; and there are three squares of them which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small, to embrace the fistulas. And they are like needles which are used to stitch wounds, and they are of golden, or iron, or silver, and they cost little which are yellow, and are more proven with black pitch to embrace the cortices of fistulas. And they are of three kinds: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the large size of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the sponges are like the seeds of plants, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and there are sponges which have two cortices of three kinds each; and there are sponges which have three cortices, and they are also of three kinds; and there are sponges which have two cortices, and a single cortex only, and they are of three kinds each; and all these are necessary in their place.

et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And put it nowhere near blood vessels or arteries, never again in the same form.

de la routure de l’artere	of the root of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	If the artery is stopped, and the skin is tough which is above, if there are many abscesses again, and also with the vein leaving and incisions; if the surgeon knows when this is due to the artery, when there are long abscesses, they are split open; and when he feels it at his side, he knows it is extraction; and when it is due to the vein, there is running discharge of pus. It is necessary to eschew the treatment of fire, and he who is at the head must eschew also, and in the one who is of swelling of the artery has become by these above the skin long; then uncover the size as we have been taught, and depart well the artery from the cloth, as long as it is uncovered; then take away a needle, and pierce until the other side, and strain the artery with a doubled thread in two layers, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples; then point the place which is between the two links of an intro-missor until there is no more of it there; and be you delivered of the incision; then bring back the treatment as before, until the pain be gone; and if the abscess is of the size of the vein, you must know that you must keep your hand there where you put in the abscess to all the skin; then take out the needle which you have in your hand, and pierce, and there shall be two doubled threads, so that you can handle it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have said, or bind two parts of the two fingers with two threads; and if you doubt that the threads will hold, if they rebound a third needle to all the threads which are beside the first needle, and strain the threads in three layers; then cut the abscess as much as it supersedes in size, then cut away the excess of the wound and leave that which is bound; then put upon it a moist drape in wine and oil, and give it treatments of bands and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Des apostemes des ners.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	The abscesses come from the nerves as well as from the veins, as from the nerves when they are cut or overworked, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And often in adjutories and in two and in all limbs or where there are joints, it is grief after incisions, and its color appears like the color of dark porridge, and is in multiple positions causing pain; and when it is strained, if the patient feels pain, and is not moved by dark porridge, but by sweat like urine; and it mutates well from all sides, neither forward nor backward, neither up nor down, and that which is in the joints does not cover with iron: by chance there will be contraction; and he who is either chief or front, makes the skin taut at the staple.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the incision is small, if he has one or two teeth, grasp it at the root; and if it is large, if he has swelling, abscess, then bone and reunite the wound at the suture, and treat until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	From the armpits hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never have I seen such a thing in the belly and nowhere else, for it is a disease which is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to nails, and its root is subtle, and its head is large; and there are many small and great ones. I have seen many people who have had two or more of these in the belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a soft root, and were full of water.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I saw them swell up in the belly and weighed them, one was 18 ounces and the other 6 and a third. When I opened the incision, if you look carefully, you will see that the patient is moist. The color of the artery is pale and moist with a soft root; if the bladder is large and soft, and you are present, I order the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the shoulder comes often too great a discharge of blood, and if it does not go away, if you delay, then you must certainly cauterize; and if you see the patient shivering with fear and weakness from the incision of the flesh, if you take a thread of gut well made, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then the restraint, and do not cease to drain the thread of gut until it has closed the artery; and take care by it. And if the roots are black, if there is weakness on the side of the gut itself for the belly, but you must take hold of half of it, and then cauterize that it does not return; then cure the wound, and keep that you do not take hold of the nipple which is of a dark colour and of bad sense and of milk returning.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the abscess later.</start_of_turn>
quant li boude ist fuer	When the abscess is full.</start_of_turn
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If there is swelling of the belly, it comes from cautery of a wound or incision of the bladder; and is above the navel and there are some bowel movements, as in other routes, or blood which clots veins or arteries according to what is before, or windiness; and if it is through the bladder route and the issue of the bowel, if it is the color of the abscess, it is a slight thing causing pain, and has various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	If by passage of the intestine, then it is more diverse; and when it is pressed, it returns, and by chance if it is choked, and expands the mouth at the entrance of the bath and with great effort.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is due to moisture, it is a slight thing, and opens readily when you press it with your hand; do not restrain me. If it is due to blood, if it opens with these signs, the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed according to quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is rough to the touch, and the work is that you must look to see if the swelling is due to the blood vessel or the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you believe that you have left the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said or in this chapter about abscesses, concerning the vein and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	If you believe that you have left the cure. For there is doubt and fear, as I have said or in this chapter about abscesses, concerning the vein and the vein. Keep the patient still and extend the limb fully; then mark the point where you wish to make the incision. Then take hold of the limb firmly between your hands and stretch it over the swelling. Then bind the limb securely with a strong thread or cord, and leave it in place for a while. Then remove half of the abscess and bring your finger and thumb close to the skin. If you find the intestine or bone caught, if you pull them out, leave them out. If you find the vein or artery, if they are bleeding, tie them off. Then return to your work and make two holes and insert two strong stitches, and tie the two holes together as you did before. Then strain the abscess for three days over the stitches. If you see that the stitches are loosening, remove them and leave the limb alone until it has healed. Cut away the dead tissue by itself or by trimming it off carefully, and cure the limb of this. Then remove the abscess as I have said. Drain the blood or moisture that you find. Cure the limb of this.
dou chancre	Then strain the abscess for three days on the needles; if you see it, pierce the needles, and leave the wound open until it bursts, and remove the dead tissue by itself.
