Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have already mentioned the signs of an abscess, and how it should be treated with medicine and how to shun the cautery; and we say that an abscess swells in the marrow, and has great swelling in the cure. The ancients say that when an abscess is in the flesh or can be scraped out as when an abscess is in the marrow, in the spleen, and in similar places, it must be removed as soon as possible; and when it is large and old, if it cannot be cured, do not approach it, for I know of no cure for it. No one has ever cured one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And as for the work, when it is in the flesh or can be removed, as we have said, do not purge the black bile from the patient once; then make the patient healthy if there is still any swelling left; then expel the patient, i.e. give him a good drink to make the work; then draw out your needles or abscesses, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and expect well the limb at your hand or at nothing, and if the wound becomes infected from the incision of the artery or vein, do not cauterize too much lest it be stained; then cure with another cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Nos avons dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be trenchant from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And be trenchant from two parts: a point, and in such a way that it cannot be closed until it comes to the intestine when it is grasped; and do not close it; then look to see if the dropsy is ingrained towards the intestines: if it is certain that you must make an incision three fingers breadth to the right of the navel; and if the dropsy is due to the disease of the liver, make your incision on the left side of the belly three fingers breadth; and if it is due to worms, make it on the right side, and do not make the wound deeper than necessary; then pierce all the leather with the instrument, and grasp the gut, and keep your hand over the wound as wide as from the nail of a finger or as much as you can endure; then pierce the gut as far as the width of your thumb until the gut comes out whole; and that is the cause of the pain; then withdraw the instrument and go. This is the form of the instrument.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver nail, broad or thin, and has at the upper part a little hole; and where it costs on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head of the nail is cut off like a pen, and this is the form of the incision which they write to cut off the head.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	And at the top of all this is the staple, so that when the instruments come to the height, if they suddenly rise up onto the instruments; you must immediately empty out half or a third of the contents, for if you empty out more than that at this hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he will bleed profusely, or he will approach death; but empty out according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pains; then take out the instrument and retain the liquid, and it is retained now by the nail which stops the hole which is above the socket, as I have said, that you pierce according to this manner; then put the instrument back the other way, if you see the patient suffering from this, and take out a small quantity of liquid. Do this under no circumstances, and keep using it until it no longer remains but a little bit of liquid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient, and you see him mouthing with pain, if the surgeon treats him with charcoal from a sepulcher or sand cautery, and by mouthing with sweat or bath and sun, and if he drinks; and the surgeon gives him drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterizes on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the poison, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Do nothing of the sort; keep yourself from using it until it stops hurting. And if you are in doubt about the patient, and you insert too much water, if the cure be of burying or washing with sand, with water or bathing and in the sun, and abstain from eating; and let the physician give drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Never are children born without a mark in the belly, or the mark is small, or it is not firmly in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If the physician has sojourned for a long time that he cannot perceive anything from afar, as in this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or perforate a hole in the middle of the great swelling, and bind and hold it for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, if you leave it closed, he will urinate, and then you will reset it; and by chance it will not be able to close, because the urine which comes out will not leave it closed
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, if it is medicine with lead weights, as we have said, if it dilates.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the opening is not wide enough, if it is treated with lead weights, as we have said, if it dilates. Those who have the opening at the root of the bone are blistered, for no hair grows where the opening is at the head of the bone, until it has raised its hair high; and they cannot cover it over for that reason, and it is a bad ailment.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that if the patient lies recumbent on his back, then the head of the thigh and the knee are as large as a pen; if the opening is small, if it comes to a thousand, as it is convenient; and you must take care of the evacuation of blood which comes often, and if it comes, if the stain of that which stains blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pus of the thigh.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times come these boils to the verge, and are an unsightly sight; and in them are both malignant and non-malignant things; if you take them at their face value, with ointment of subtlety, and press and squeeze them all out, then put on a wet bandage in the Egyptian fashion; then cure with diafinicon until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the swelling is malignant, of a dark color and swelling, it is necessary that you bring cautery there.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have grasped it, and if the swelling is at the root of the bone, and has some in the marrow and some outside, you must break the swelling that is inside first; and when it is loosened, if the wound is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you have cured it whole, if it is not firmly held, the head of the shoulder will not be perceived and will come black and corrupt in its root or head; if you must remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply honey and flour made of pomegranate peel and sometimes, cure it of other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood comes out, if you mix the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is of two sorts in these two situations: that is to say, at the discharge of blood and at corruption; and if the head of the shoulder is corrupted and withdrawn, if you drink or force down the hair of the root a span of lead, and the patient urinates; and when the hair has grown over the head of the shoulder which has not been cut around, or there is wound or incision, if you must indeed remove these things, then you must burn the hair around the circumference until the hair is loosened; and when it is loosened, deliver the head of the shoulder from all parts; and if this should cause division of these things, if you must indeed burn at the root of the hair and the head, then dry thoroughly between two, and put on a soft bandage of wet linen with cold water, which should not be moved.
de la circoncision	If this be a grievous matter, if you must certainly undertake it, then grasp the limb firmly without inflicting any wound to the root of the thumb and the heel; then gradually separate the skin between the two joints, and place a fine strip of moist linen over the cold water, so that it does not slip away.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a continuation of the other wounds; however, when our will commands it, and is properly undertaken, if it is necessary that our workers do the best work, and the most gentle for the patient.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old folks do not tell me of circumcision for their children, for they do not use it in their laws, and we have only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and physicians who perform circumcision to make incisions around the head of the penis, and with force, and with great bleeding; so that the testicles often flee because of the two layers of skin, and by chance if one severs these below and leaves the upper one behind.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the wound closes again, and the pain is doubled, and there is swelling which is painful when the point of the limb is not securely held; and by swelling of the cord by chance escapes the wound, corrects the work, and many times comes out without having had to perform any swelling and I think so.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the alteration which is made with force throughout the whole thread, I have observed the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well downwards as upwards.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand, if it is even all around the thumb, but the nail is well stretched and tight around the skin; and if the nail is somewhat bent from the start, as if you were making the child understand, if he understands, do not force the nail to lie only around the nail; but put it aside in every way you can; then put it between your thumb and index finger, and bring the forces between your thumb and index finger or take away your little finger so that the nail does not see them, neither any of the instruments; then stretch your thumb to the nail and blow or pinch, and pull the nail up as much as the nail of the thumb is long; then thoroughly cleanse the wound which is assembled, then tie the sign of a double thread, and tie the little finger from one loop to the other; and keep two fingers of the second loop to the pouch and the little finger, and keep between the two loops, then loosen the pinch from the thumb and pull the nail out; then leave the blood to flow freely, because that is the remedy; and put powder on and over the powder I drape a gauze which is glued with a clove of clove oil, scented with rosemary oil and fresh, and leave it on until the bleeding stops.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	When the forces are formed at the armpit, it is thus: the two arms are tense and stretched, and the arms are as great as the palm of the hand equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the armpit is when the nerves are injured during the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend your nail, even if it causes the wound to split; and grasp it equally, and if you do not manage to hold it with your nail, if you grasp it with your teeth, hold it firmly, and then grasp it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they trespass for two days, and what is below the ribcage is inflamed, if you leave it as long as the spasms cease, and the swelling is slight; if you touch it as you wish, and hold on to the lower part of the ribcage, it will do you neither good nor harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have treated the wound with powder, as we have said or mentioned, if you touch it too hard, it will go deeper; so treat it as we have said until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
dou retenement de l’urine	When the urine is retained.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The urine is retained if it is due to the stone, or blood congealed, or bile, or worms, or other things which we have mentioned in the previous division; and if the urine is not released, you must know that it is held back by the stone which is in the belly or the neck of the bladder; if you can make the patient hunch over his knees; and put his feet on the back, and extend his belly from the part below his back, and restrain the patient so that he cannot move; and then you must constrain the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come out, as we have mentioned, and the patient feels great pain, you must give an extraction with all the instruments which are called a "siringue"; and this is the form: either of silver or lead shot like a hen's quill; or the caine of a palm of a long and a half, or shot like a bean.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And thus the method of issuing urine is as follows: if you take one doubled thread and bind one end to the head of a cushion or cloth, and pass the other end through the syringe; then close up the excess cloth and pass it until it reaches the head of the syringe, and join the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on the chair, and raise the bladder and testicles with oil and olive oil and warm water; then put the syringe gently into the testicles, as far as it reaches the root of the testicles, then double the testicles towards the scrotum; then withdraw the syringe before it reaches the bladder, and let the patient feel that it is coming out until it reaches the empty state; this must not be done except in the case where the thread leads or goes astray; then remove the thread at both ends, and the urine will follow the thread, and then expel it forcefully, and correct the urine; and begin the syringe again until the bladder is empty, and align the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are dropsy or blood in the bladder, or putrification has set in, and you see urine and medicines distilled, if you do everything that is called the «clepsedre», which is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and if there are three holes: two from one side, and one from the other, as you see; and the lord physician must keep his head firm so that he presses well the verge towards the addition, if we can remove the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you see the medicines flowing in the bladder, put the chief physician in the moisture, and draw out the one who is inside; if you draw out the moisture from the chief, and then push him back firmly; if the moisture enters again, and comes to the bladder, if the patient feels it; and that is the form of a subtle cluster from which we clusterize the bladder: if this is the case.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and from one side or the other; then take a bladder of mutton and put the moisture in it which you see clustering the bladder, then bind it between the two breasts forming a double bow, and burn one half of that moisture on the fire; then strain the chief of the cluster into the verge, and pull your hand over the bladder until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, if you take a piece of parchment and make a circle, and pierce it round; then draw the string firmly through these holes, and assemble the circle as if you were assembling a wheel, and put inside what you see of oil, moisture, and water, and bind it with the instrument; and do as if you had made the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the previous division the methods of dealing with stones, and their extraction alongside medicines; and we have mentioned the difference between a retained stone and one that must be extracted, as well as the signs and in what case a stone must be opened; in the bladder and in the kidney; and I will tell you openly and briefly.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone that is retained in the bladder often causes vomiting, which is a sign that the stone has burst from the bladder similar to the pain in its subtlety; and it opens gravel, and grinds the patient’s side, and causes them to urinate frequently, and then it swells; and from these vomits the foundation is loosened; and the healing of these vomiting spells is light up until the age of three years, and is more grievous in the elderly, and is like that in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure for these who have a large stone is lighter than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, first cleanse the patient thoroughly with vinegar, to drive out all the worms that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never happens to inquire about the stone [kidney].
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then grasp the patient by the side, and loosen and move to the navel, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder; and it never happens to go up high; then make him sit between your hands and his hands should rest on his buttocks, so that the bladder is completely drooping downwards; then inquire and touch within; if you feel the stone in the space, hasten now to cut above the stone
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out on touching, moisten your left index finger if the patient is an adult, or your middle finger if the patient is a youth accompanied; and press it to its foundation, inquire for the stone, and when you feel it at your middle finger, if the bladder is swollen at the neck; then press above your middle finger, and the stone will come out either by itself or you will see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his thumb on his right hand and his little finger on his left hand the skin that is between the thumb and little finger in the part where the measure is taken; then insert the sponge, which is shaped like this.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And between that which is between the collarbones and the sternum, do not insert it in the middle but at the cost of the left nipple; and on the right side of the stone, and two of them either adjoined or fixed to the sternum, and as much as the breadth of the stone, not too great; for by chance the press if it must be on the stone, that it leap in the direction of the work; and strings that there is a part of the stone or there are angles, and margins: if it is grasped to twist; and if there is a part which is swollen, like a gland, round, from which there is a clear discharge.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And if there are angles and margins there, make the size greater; and if it does not jump, it is certain that you must strain over the teeth which are as sharp as a file at the head, for the stone must be strained if it does not escape; or you can take out the instrument which is curved at the head; and if you do not know how to manage it, if the wound is large, and if the stone does not move, if the tightening of the vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, strain out the greatest first at the belly of the bladder, then press on, then force the stone out, and the smaller afterwards if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is much swollen, if you cover it with silk, and make it even more painful.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And if it is much swollen, if you cover it with silk, and make it even more painful. For in this matter two things happen to the patient: either he dies or his urine comes out again at the same time as his wounds will not close; but whatever you do to relieve him, or to remove the splinters, as long as you are pulling them out by pieces; and when you have finished your work, if you apply incense and aloe and blood of dragon, and bind it, and put above it a wet cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to calm the burn; then raise the patient up to his collarbone, and do not release the ligature until the third joint.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, if there is much moisture in the limb from oil and water, then treat with the astringents diafinicon and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if pus and blood clots come into the wound and corruptions, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and either because of that the urine is retained, which is known in part as not coming out with the urine: drink wine in the wound, and remove that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and carry it away; then wash the wound with water and salt and oil, and give him every kind of help that you can, as long as he is alive; and know that all the times that you are curing him, that you must bind the two seams and assemble the medicines on the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the bladder or the urethra, and it is fixed there, and the urine cannot pass; if the physician does what I have said above, that you must let it go many times, we will hear of the size of this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proved this to be true.</start_of_turn>
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take hold of the iron according to this form and make two angles grasped firmly in one space:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the edge of the bladder near the stone, so that it will not be able to move backwards into the bladder; then pull the thread gently until it reaches the stone; and turn the thread towards your hand over the stone until you can see the stone from the other side; if the urine comes then, press your hand on what remains of the stone which is in the bladder.</start_of_turn
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the fracture is great, and the urine spurts with blood, and the patient is in pain; if you are unable to do this by any means, take a thread and pass it through the hole and another through the bone, then pass the needle through the wound between the two lines, and then withdraw the needle, and remove the thread, and close the wound with a cold compress that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the limb above and below, then push the bone sideways between the two joints, and then extract it with force, loosen the ligament, and congeal the blood that is in the wound; then cure as before.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the bone is dislocated in a woman, and this does not happen often, it is a grievous cure, and is defended by two things: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that one cannot find a woman who is truly virtuous, even among the most chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	If by chance one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of hands; and if the woman’s bone is thicker than the man’s, because she can make a deeper incision and there is greater pain in her. And if it is necessary for this, if you must take a lesser measure, take a mark that is well known, and prick the flesh, and if you do not find it, do not cast aside the obvious; and present a sign of wisdom in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command of her with the inquiry of the bone; and look well whether the woman is a virgin: for if she is, she can push out her shoulder or foundation and inquire the bone; and if she finds it, if you constrain her shoulder, command her to push out her shoulder or with the patient, and desire and press her left hand on her bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If this be true, if you command her to move from the entrance of the bladder to the root of the thigh, as far as she comes to the root of the thigh, then grasp on the stone at the root of the thigh and discover the middle of the stone, where it is usually hidden, and feel the thigh in that part; and do not move her head up or down, or from side to side, until she is as small as at first. Then gently restore her to her natural size, if you feel the thigh is becoming relaxed as much as the stone can bear, and the discharge as many kinds of stones as you have seen: for example, small and large, sharp and round, long and short, and those that have rains.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if the discharge resemble these things, it is an issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if she does not go away, if you put on the brow of vitriol and hold it for an hour until she is stained; then return to your work until the stone is gone, and have the instruments that I told you of for extracting the stone as your companions; and if she still does not go away, and it is the artery that has been cut, if you put powder on the wound and bind tightly with threads and bandage, and do not attempt to do so again; leave the stone alone and do not touch it, except by chance the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the blood flow of blood is calmed and the limb is relaxed, if you return to your work, as long as the wound is open.
de hernie carnouse	Of hernias of the groin.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is like lead when cold, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and never is it truly in the yolk of the egg, if we take care that this is not the case; and it is the skin of the coion between the white fat that we have mentioned.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramiculus is weak and comes from the coions, and the matter is spread out
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never if percussion comes upon the joints, and this moisture has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without redness, or black, or aquous white, and these are signs of corruption in this assembly, for if it is white or pale yellow as we have said, if the abscess is renewed, I advise that you do not open the joints, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess is renewed with a part of the egg, and because of this it is thought that it is another wound; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white substance, if you feel it well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if you suspect that there is something inside that makes it appear, of course the form is as it has been said before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, following the introduction, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cauterize with iron, if it be known that the patient is in pain, that he should be well-nourished and have a full belly; then we anoint him on his back, on something high, and put a cloth over his face; we sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and stretch his arm to one of the two costles between the ribs; then we take the sponge soaked in vinegar, and cut the skin between the ribs from the navel down to the loin; and let the incision be straight, dividing the skin of the ribs right up to the white membrane; and we burn it subtly as it should be; then we pierce the white membrane with a needle to let out all the fluid, and we drain away all the blood; and we put on our sponges, and extend the white membrane upwards; and do not touch the ribs except for the white membrane; cut through all or in pieces immediately the cartilage under the skin, if you do not cut it well it will return the blood; and if the sinew leaps up to your work, if you leave it in its place when you have finished the work on the white membrane. Then we reassemble the two leaves of the ribs to their natural position, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find the eye corrupted by another disease, you must tie down the blood vessels that are suspended, doubting the discharge of blood; then cut the eyeball out completely, drain the eye, and cure it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	If the swelling is put together in two parts, their branches are two roots; if you press the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe out the blood, and put in the wound a piece of clean cloth soaked in rose oil; and put over it another cloth soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two bones, and put under doubled cloths, and tie it up as it is proper in this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and use coarse wool thread as described above and sew them together at the groin; and one of the bones grasps on the foundation up to the shoulder, and the other at the bony prominence; and the other two fingers grasp on the two angles, and all are assembled together with the restriction in the loop of the armpit; and never is medicine the root of the cautery instead of the size of a needle, and take only one cultellary needle and prick the skin of the bones, and if there is a white spot that contains the blood is discovered; if you take the cautery as described above and burn that spot as we have said, the blood will clot at that subtle cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And look at all the ways you can do it, as long as you remove everything; and keep that fire away from the egg; and remove that which is more harmful; and take care of the discharge of blood, and do not be afraid of the work of size; and if anything opposes you, or if there is suspicion of infection or other things, if it is possible, cure that which opposes you, as it is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is pale and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, if you think it necessary, make an incision, as I have said; and when you are sure by the signs that the swelling is liquid, make the patient sit on a high chair; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with a broad knife and make a hole as long as the thumb; and if the wound is large, let the blood flow out fully; then put a bandage on the wound and bind it, and leave the remaining blood to drain out naturally; and cure the wound until it is healed; and if the white fluid does not stop the bleeding in the wound, as I have said; you must drink a penny or the instrument used for treating the hydrophobia, because it is like this; and widen the wound, and remove the blood that has returned, and reassemble after six months or when the pain has ceased, and when it is reassembled as before, the patient will be able to live his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the bones
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Wounds that in this section of the twig have fear in more than one place, for it seems to me that it is worth leaving them alone; and I shall tell you the work and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, I say that abscesses come from boils or carbuncles, and sometimes from wounds; and this is by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known by excessive swelling and pain, which is spread as far as the joints, or by percussion; and the colour of the abscess is like that of fresh cheese; and there is no pain, and is an abscess that is grieved; and by chance there is one abscess which is large, bloody, and purulent, and of dark colour, and does not come from any artery, or from swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not from an artery, if it is known by the arrangement of the abscess, when you press on it with your hand; and I do not know of any other way of treating it.</start_of_turn>
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the swelling of a vein is known by his disposition at the expression of the touch of the thumbs, and can make quite as much of this semblance as of the others; and it is that you must grasp like nails, then the egg is high, and the thread is thick white silk, and deliver the suspendor from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already softened with these thorns, if you must then carry the egg, and grasp; and if it is at the surface or in what is within the vessels, if you must deliver all that holds, and grasp roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the bone is high or behind the joint, if you must grasp it entirely, and draw out the head, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is done, if you are using wool yarn, soak it in rose oil and wine, then bandage it with other bandages until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the bones
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess covered with a covering resembling a burdock, with the softening of the nails, and the patient groans greatly when he walks; and the cure for this disease is very near as poor as this one that we have just said, and all that we can do is tell you the work of it, according to what the old ones have said
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit upright on a chair, then suspend the arm from the armpits to the waist, holding it firmly with your hands and stretching it out; then cut through the skin at the elbow, as far as it is necessary, and then remove the callous part, just as we have said in the extraction of the arteries from the temples; then insert a needle or double thread and tie it to the first bone or where the nail has gone, and tie it loosely at the other end; then cut around the elbow joint, according to the length of the bone, and remove the corrupt humors; then cure the wound as usual or apply an ointment, so that no artery is bleeding other than those already bled; for by this means there will be no harm, and if all the arteries are bled, you must drain all of them.
de la routure dou syfac	of the root of the throat</start_of_turn>
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The coming of this branch is by section that comes or by fracture, or extension upon the belly in the part of the intestines, for the intestines descend from that route to one of the buttocks; and that route is either by fracture or by extension of the bone, and these two methods are from cause: by percussion, or by jump, or by pressure, or by elevation of grief failure, and by similar things; and the signs when it is by fracture of the syfac are that there is swelling and swelling in length, and does not come immediately; and the fracture is equal up to the navel, for the syfac presses the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the face is sectioned, that it makes sudden pain appear at the edge, and the swelling is diverse in appearance, from the splitting of the skin to the bursting of the bowels, because of the evacuation of the intestine and the displacement of the bone from the face.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never should the bones be closed with the intestine, and is retained when it is held, and causes great suffering to the patient, even when it is pressed.</start_of_turn
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of fire with fear, for it is known to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	If you command or the patient orders that the intestine be rapped at its root in the wound if it can enter; then either saw above its collar between the hands, and grasp the thighs; then extend the thumb above, and cut all the skin of the buttocks along; then draw inwards the intestines of the size of unces as much as you must to open the wound, and so on until the bladder is found; then uncover the syfac that is under the skin of the buttocks, until the thick syfac is discovered throughout; then put your index finger in that which lies between the buttocks, between the white syfac which is under the skin of the buttocks and between the second syfac, and depart that which is behind the buttocks and between the second syfac; and thus move the thumb of the hand to the buttocks, and place the white syfac at the top of your left hand, and keep the buttocks to the whole of the syfac; and command the minister to stretch the buttocks up, and unfasten that which is before the ligature; and ask at your sides if there is any intestine or white syfac that is hard, and if you find nothing, if the bladder is down; then take a needle or there is a thick thread made of X threads, and pass it into the back part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the buttocks; after the size, then cut the veins that appear from the threads, until there are three threads; and gather the threads together in the manner of a cross, and bind the syfac, as we have said, with a strong thread of two parts; then wrap the threads together and bind them in two parts, so that no vessel that sustains them can enter into the wound, except for the fistula; and put the liening back according to the first liening which is two fingers from that, and after these two fingers leave the syfac which is under the thumb the greatest of a finger; and after all the rest according to the circumference that the egg has; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the buttocks, as much as it is without error, and bow; as we have said before; and administer coarse wool with oil, and apply to the wound, and administer the liening that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never shall the flesh be cauterized save in the manner that we have mentioned after the incision, in doubt of bloodletting.</start_of_turn>
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For in this work, there is often the evacuation of blood, and leaving the limb long as it aches for it; and if it delays at the seat, if it is raised from warm water, put on what we have said, until it aches; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	Of hernias of the groin.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this chapter, I have never seen anyone cure it with iron.</start_of_turn>
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the old men say that it is made just like the twig which binds the screw, in part as you bind the vessels, after the size above lightly downwards; then pierce it in the middle, and treat the abscess of what causes it, until the vessels cease to bleed; and treat it as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes comes rupture inwards, as we have said, and opens the wound; and do not cut any intestines as long as they remain connected, and if there are any, it is thus, and repair them every hour; and whatever remains stuck there for too long, if you believe the wound or tumor, until the intestines are released; and this comes from the extension of the sinew which is inwards, as we have said, because it is taut, then is softened and relaxes the wound and opens; and it is treated as we have said before. And never is it treated with iron in this manner: and that the patient lies comfortably on his back between your hands, then grasp the limb of the rupture inflates outwards to the extent of three fingers; and then draw out the sinew which is below the leather that covers it, then take the root and put out the limb appearing from the sinew; and press at the bottom of the belly, then cut out the two fingers appearing from the sinew on the top of the root, and cut one and the other; then draw out the root of the root, and do not cover anything from the sinew nor extend anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the intestinal radix; and then treat it with the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you grasp the hair, if the wound cleans and heals the wound, as long as it is sound.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is constrained and does not appear on the surface, and the cautery is muffled in this limb, and more proximate to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the nails.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the nails of the thumbs are softened in water-soaked homes, because the nails that are inside are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when you see it being cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to scrape off the softened skin from the natural skin; then join the layers together with a suture, and if you see that, close the superfluous softened skin with two or three sutures firmly; then scrape between the sutures, and cure as the other wounds, until it is healed, and pull out the hair.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement,
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	As for boils that erupt, it is forbidden in our law, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary to force them except for two ways: one is that the eye of the patient responds when asked, and the other is that we often mix in the treatment of these boils with other beasts, as with goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that boils are made in two ways: by traction or by incision
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the traction method, we make the best one sit in warm water, until the swelling softens and relaxes; then we grab it with our hand, until it is reset and you no longer feel it
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the shoulder-blade: it is commanded that you hold it firmly, and press the skin of the armpits to your left hand, then bind the suspension, and grasp upon each joint with two fingers, when you have well supported them; and leave no hair or superfluous hair which is on the vessels; and this method of cautery is milder than that which is done by traction, because by traction remains nothing of the hairs, for the best desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites are beings that possess both male and female sexual organs.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners as in homes: one if between the two testicles appears as with the nature of a woman, or if there are hairs, and sometimes it emits urine in the courtyard.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the navel as with a penis and two testicles
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And as for the treatment of wounds and ulcers, if you cauterise the edges of the wounds, it is cured like any other wound; in the second method, for those whose urine spurts through the skin of the scrotum, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is in two ways like that of women: one if between the two testicles is opened as with the nature of a woman, or if there are hairs, and sometimes in the urine they are emitted. And the other way if in women, and there is upon the navel like a beard and two testicles. And the cure of the swelling and the fame is if you cut out all the seminal vesicles, and the cure is like for other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine leaps through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The fire cautery is to be applied above the natural part [of the body] as long as it is too painful to see; and many women have had as much pain as with a hand, and this is the cure.
