Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to hold back the superfluousness of the shoulder at the arm or shoulder blade, and to grasp it lightly; and do not be too rough, for blood does not come from this, but from the breaking of bones; and the cure for this is like that of other wounds as long as it is sound; and there is another wound which arises at the mouth of the marrow, and the spleen, and by chance spurts forth, and is like the appearance of a wound, and for this reason it is called the ancient "lame disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you suspect that it has slipped, as we have said previously, hold it firm until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If the character of the woman is not clearly understood, or if the wound is small; it is by birth or by disease that it comes to be; or by a sudden injury, or by the bite of a dog or by a wound caused by a blunt or sharp object, and is made manifest in swelling, bruising or haematoma, in the bone, in the muscle or in the skin; and if the cause is not known, and the child is in danger, or by chance the flowers have to be plucked. And this knowledge is from the experience of the midwife.</start_of_turn>
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If swelling appears near the joint, if at the root or at the head.</start_of_turn
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If he is lying on his side, and he is close to two books, if you are in a hurry, grasp two thumbs together, and let the woman be behind him, spreading out his legs; then the two books will form, as long as the side of the face is round, and over the thumb-stamps; then take hold of the hair, and mix it with oil, and put it on the limb, and hold the woman at home chest-to-chest, so that he cannot sneeze.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the face is hard and thick, if you can, cover it with a cloth resembling a laurel leaf
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the thumb-stamps are of charred hair, if you suspend it at the onion and cover; and have medicines staying blood, such as acaice, dragon's blood, incense, together with a lot of eggs; then mix in a large dose of lard, so that the wound cannot heal; and let it be long, and mix in a handful of dry lint; then let the other treatments follow until it is healed
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	When the marrow comes out whole in the marrow cavity, if it is covered according to this manner, except for postmortem swelling, it is not a fracture.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For swelling in the marrow cavity which is in the marrow, do not touch fire.
des emorroides	des emorroides.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which without treatment usually do not heal; and when hemorrhoids are old they become painful; and as we have said in the preceding chapters concerning the signs and symptoms, I will say here those which bring about a cure.</start_of_turn>
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the pain which is in the marrow, when they are pressed in the marrow cavity, and cannot be felt, must be cured by iron.</start_of_turn>
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the entrance of the marrow cavity can be felt, and these can be cured.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	You must therefore put the woman in a cold house, then raise the altar up to its roots, then sprinkle upon it medicines that restrain blood, such as alum and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then cover her with a cloth an hour later, then bathe her in cold water; and if there is blood, let her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then give her barley flour, mix it with honey and fennel, and put it on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stinks, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this does not happen, if she is bleeding at the back and has swelling, then take flaxseed and soak it in juice of plantain or in vinegar with old wine, and apply it to the wound
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is at rest, if the wound is clean and healthy; the one which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a chief aspired to, if you cover it as I have said before; then the wound must be clean and healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	Emorroids are openings of veins which, without treatment, are usually fatal. When emorroids are old, they become toughened. We have already mentioned the signs and symptoms; here I will tell you of those which are most useful for curing. I say that emoroids and the toughened vein, when they are inflamed in the belly, are not felt unless they are treated by iron. Those which are at the root of the belly can be felt; these can be cured. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then draw the belly tight, grasp the root and sprinkle on restraining medicines such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then remove the pieces an hour later, and put them in cold water. If there is still pain, give her a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then give her barley meal with honey and assails, and make her drink it. And if it stops bleeding, that is good. If not, make her breathe vinegar at her back and give her lead. Then give her lint, and soak it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with old wine, and make her breathe. And when the incision is healed, if it is a bleeding vein, it will stop bleeding as long as it is healthy; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a rough chief, as I have already said of the toughened vein; and then it will stop bleeding as long as it is healthy. As for bleeding from the belly, this must be treated by an opening at the root.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the belly, such as carbuncles and pyreous abscesses and herpes and worms and piles and fistula and haemorrhoids and burnt abscesses, and other diseases which I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I say concerning the burnt abscess which occurs in the belly, which is not like other abscesses which are only painful; and if you know the work of iron, look if the abscess is still in its early stages of formation, and is full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you see it
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	When thou seest that the pain is appeased, make the patient sit on a chair, and place two cushions or as many as he can bear beneath his buttock, and support him on his back and gather his limbs as if to defend his limb; and let his thighs be wide, and put his arms across his knees, and bind them firmly with a bandage; then pour the bail towards his breast, and bring the instrument which we use to open the mouth of the vein, and when you see that it comes, know the depth of the vein, so that what comes into it does not go deeper than it should, and does not damage the patient; and if the instrument is too large, cover the depth of the vein with cloths, so that the instrument does not grieve; and let him put on the cap of the instrument, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the abscess bursts open, and we pour oil over the hand, if it covers the head and the thumb, if the wound is emptied, then put in the wound some soft wool soaked in rose oil or in dry green oil; and put the dressing firmly over the wound and put over it a pad of linen cloth soaked in water or mallow, which must be cooked; then cure after two days of oiling following this, until it is healed; and never lift the wound and the abscess with a cluster of water and honey, and then with water or licorice root and alum.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	If the wound is closed in the wound, if you must take care not to burn, but cure it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	From infancy.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The master first of all should know the figure of normal birth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down on her belly and desire to smell the head: then the child hastens to be born; then draw the head that the birth is in accordance with the natural figure, and it will issue from his chief, and support it with him; and when you see these signs, if you must press gently on her belly, so that the child comes out head first; for when it descends upon his head, if he supports it with him, the child is born of itself, and the mother is delivered of her superfluities by natural birth.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes from his feet, or from his arm or hand, or from his belly, or from his bowels, but it comes from his collar or from some other bad figure; if the master is at the dance that he be wise and discreet in these matters, and he beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how we must help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out head first by natural birth, and the woman is groaning, and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and when she has given birth of the oile or fenugreek seed, then lie between her legs the little cushion which is its form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And cut the secondine, and hold its nail as long as the moisture which is in its core escapes; and press the woman’s belly until the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to clench the woman with the muscle of fenugrec with oil of sisament; then make her take it down and vomit, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if it is now delivered.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands issue forth fiercely, if you must hold them gently still; and if they will not enter, put the woman on a seat, and support her feet high; then withdraw the seat from the earth, and hold the woman, that she does not cough; and if the hands will not enter, and the fetus is dead, if you press the hands to the collar which is before put, and draw out the child, and comfort her equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the issue of the child upon his feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon his feet, if you can push upwards; and then twist a little to the front and a little to the back, until they are even; then take hold of the feet and extend a little to the front and a little to the back.</start_of_turn>
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he jumps up to the buttocks, if the command is to seize him, and make him spit out the bad things; if he jumps up, God help him.</start_of_turn
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	If not so fierce as we have said, if the limb hangs loose and limp, as long as it follows the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For in such a case it is easily done.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he does not jump up so willingly as we have seen, say that you take muscle powder of elevation, and oil of lavender, and gum masticatory, and grind them all together in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and drive away this vomiting, then make her sit in cold water until below the ribs; and when she is softened down below, give her a collar of myrrh, and put on her clothes, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her vomit and strain her mouth and nose, and take hold of her belly lightly, for the child is now jumping.</start_of_turn
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	because of the issue of the child on his knees.

If it be perceived until the hip joint, if it is the vein that is coming out as far as the limb; if there is no twisting and the cause of the pain is not evident, if it is merely bowed and not seriously injured, there is no remedy save labor and the vanity of fools who are meddling with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one which is neither new nor old, hope of recovery by fire exists, as I have seen; and that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and let the legs rest on his thighs, and incline his thighs towards his belly; then attempt an embrace, or plunge if there is twisting, until you feel safe or the attempt comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in the foundation, if you must bite your thumb index, if you sense that the attempt has been perceived; or that the fracture is uncovered or you sense between your thumb and the index finger the marrow or the bone, then stop for it is dangerous; if it does not break through, it cannot be healed
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can easily cure all sorts of ailments, but it is thus; and the aid which we make is, if it is to be done, to circumscribe the cautery narrowly in accordance with the size of the fistula, as is said beforehand; and draw out all the pus from the fistula, until it comes out from its foundation; and do this twice or thrice, until you perceive that these boils which are like a penne of oil must be burned; and then cure with moist patches covering the wound until the boils are gone, then cure with ointment coating the wound and stitching.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, that is good indeed.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If thus, nothing else can be done; and if one attempts it and does not pierce to the root which is or underlies, and between your thumb and the attempt put on a thick covering of hair or fat, and you will see the fistula at this point where the covering ends; if you touch the beginning of the fistula, and hold it before the attempt, and then apply the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the head of the attempt; and the attempt will be freed, and rejoice; then anoint those boils which seem like a penne of oil, and there will be nothing left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if it does not go well for you, and if there is a break between you and the work, if the burn is done by fire or medicine is applied.</start_of_turn
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery, two bones are joined together: that is to say, the burning of these hairs causes the evacuation of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of soft bandages bound up with rough sponges or broken bones, until the hair burns through the sponge; then cure the wound of the oozing sores with dry sponges, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed and does not return.</start_of_turn>
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the foundation, and is expelled from the flesh, if the bone or foundation is fractured, inquire about this.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the attempt, and between two is the cloth or the sponge or hair, or it is almost going to burst, if there is no other way out but by surgery and hope, by the administration of one of these three methods: or you cauterize as we have said, or you cut right through, or if you wish, put on soft sponges and cure as before; do not go too deeply, that you do not cover the foundation that holds the bottom, and let the evacuation go in the natural way; then cure as we have said; by chance if it is well, or you remove the covering and the wound, then when it is cut off from the foundation, by attempt or by other pointed instrument; then tie up this burnt hair that is in the wound, as you wish; and then study to restore the wound and to stop the fistula in the lower part of the foundation: if it is less painful for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas like this: when you bite the attempt at the fistula, and it is either cost with dou pain at the bottom of the skin beneath, or take an attempt pierced at the head like this.
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And always break the thread twice, and hold the lump throughout the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	And if it is pierced in the margin of the pain at the bottom of the skin beneath, then draw out the thread of that which is pierced, so that you bite your toe or the pain; and draw out the head of the thread, and join the two ends together, and restrain one to the other, and leave it for one or two; and do not restrain it at any time, until the thread has overcome these two burdens that are between them, and that swell up; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not break through, if you make it break through in every way you can, it will not be too thick.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not worth making the dressing too tight if they are inflamed, and then the cure must be as we have said, until they are healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny bladder from which we make the fistula is mouth-shaped and one-sided and trenchant; and on the other side not, for we must not touch this or we must not touch that, as you see here.
des emorroydes	bleeds.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racine; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you command me to suture in this manner: take one thread, pierce it through a needle, then pass the thread through from below and pierce the needle through from the other side, and turn two threads of the thread around the needle, and if it is thick; tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and make sure of all the others, and leave one to hold the surplus of blood; then put upon the foundation a moist drape in oil of roses or cerote, and put upon the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then leave it until it blanches, and when it is white, if the wound of oiling and other remedies, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	until the fire has consumed the hair or root.</start_of_turn>
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is the loosening of the bowels by the intestines, and by the constricting of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is of no avail.</start_of_turn
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you order me to remove a splinter or nail from the nail or cuticle, which does not allow it to moisturize; then cure it until it is healed if it is possible; and if it does not heal, if you renew the scraping more strongly than before, until it comes out, and be scraped away; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	when he is calm.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small swelling that appears before a limb, and goes out from within to without; and never does the trueve touch it, and it is felt as though dead from pain, and comes to every part of the body, and more so in the hands than in any other place.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure for it is that you take a bandage of one inch of goose feather, or a strong inch of flax, and put that bandage upon the wound, until the circle turns pale the wound throughout; then draw out your hand all the way to the bandage until you have embraced the wound all around, and press it inwards, and squeeze the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that it is done with a spider or iron in this fashion, and be quiet and attentive beneath:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see that it is done with a spider or iron in this fashion, and be quiet and attentive beneath, do not move, for it must be held firmly and pressed. And if you see that the fire cautery has arrived, if it is before or alongside the cautery book.
de la forme dou clistere	of this fashion.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is silver or gold wire, or molten spider or enamel made; and never are these small and great instruments made in this fashion, as they are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who suffer from ailments that are feeble and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their form is small and great if they are soft, or the belly is tight according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is swelling or pain in the belly or side, if you see, or if there is pain in the chest, and there are two holes on one rib and one on the other; or if the belly or an organ has medicine inside or outside, or if there are many holes throughout, put between each hole one space, then pass through these holes one strong thread of thick thread in the shape of an X or around, and assemble the belly as if it were a nail; and when the medicine is inside, if there is an instrument before a strong thread, then tighten it; and that is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold; anoint the head with oil or balm of eggs, or something similar; then bind it lightly. Then grasp the minister with both hands together, until it is thoroughly numb, then draw out the blister, and leave the patient his legs exposed, and if the medicine sees that it suffices, if the swelling has gone down; and if he sleeps all night, it is more effective.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he does it in the morning when the patient is suffering from the discharge of the belly, and the physician arrives quickly, if he can do so while he is still sane.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is bruising or swelling on the skin or abscess, if the blister is as fine as for one child; this is the form of a fine blister that arises when the skin is stretched tight.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in the previous chapter the treatment of wounds; or rather the treatment of hands and surgery, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various depending on how they are made, and depending on the parts or wounds that are made, and how they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are bites of stone, and the size of spear and nail, or lance or fist or sickle, or similar things; or that are made according to the laws of nature, as for example a wound that bites on the cheek, or on the head, or the heel, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for a simple wound, and we will begin with wounds of the head alone, for the memory will come to mind in this chapter
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a head injury occurs, and the bone is not fractured, take care if it is from a wound of stone or other things, and the skin is completely ruptured and the wound is large, and you doubt the wound itself: if you do so immediately after injury to the head itself even if there is blood from the wound, or vice versa; and listen to the patient’s swelling of wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not recover, if either he vomits meat or does not drink wine, does not eat meat; and put out the wound, if there is pus coming out, cotton wool soaked in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no pus coming out, put a bandage on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, dust, or anything; and if it has been moved, put on some ointments, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a nail and similar, and the flesh does not naturally reunite, if you reunite it with stitches, as I will say for wounds in the belly, with sutures.</start_of_turn>
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed by the bone, and is raw, and will hold only at one point, if it be possible; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat coarse food, such as meat and bread, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or cut through bone, if it does not penetrate the bone, if you can remove it whole, and drain pus, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicine, if you see it, and if you find it displaced, if you bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, if you must cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, if it is a mild cure: then you shall apply this powder which makes them adhere as soon as they have moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and mix them together finely, and apply the powder to the wound, and hold it firm until it is well healed and joins together all its blood; and then bind it well and leave it alone, if it does not swell; for we do not cauterize the medicine until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we do this charcoal burn only, when there is no incense nor blood of a dragon, but that the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, even in this state, if one does not put on my powder; but put on some unguents digested, or poulps of oatmeal made of water and honey, until it is soft; then cure with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, if the extraction has fine teeth; and I will tell you later about the fractures of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and is simple, if there is no difference between it and the fracture of the skull, but if the artery is severed or the neck is fractured
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, if there is no other burden than to leave the cure, and do not put anything restrictive, because it hinders the nerve and makes it shrink; and do not put anything rough on the wound, because the substance of the nerve is cold, and the continuation of the pain is with the brain, which is the most tender member; but if the medicine is soft, like molten chalice in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cypress washed in sweet water, and other stones of lead according to this method, and moist unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, if the edges are torn and bent, then the cure must be prolonged until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and swollen and full of pus, if the wound is pierced or lower in the limb; and if an artery is severed, blood flows profusely, if the swelling, and the pus, and the cautery mix together; and if the thorn of the throat is severed, or the tonsils, and the cord is grasped, by which the meat will go; and if the thumb rests on the chin of the throat, do not touch the throat but restore it to its natural position; and then strain it immediately, and leave it untouched for a while, then cure the wound from the inside outwards until it is healed; and if the wound has caused an indentation in the bone, if there are pieces of bone, if the fragments are forced out, do not attempt to remove what you cannot; leave as much as the wound permits, and when it is drained and aligned, issue the wound; and if the wound is fresh, if powder is applied as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, cut as I have said in this chapter.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a lance or knife.</start_of_turn
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it be lance or dagger wound, and the wound is deep, if thou seest that from the wound comes out wind with speed, that the wound is mortal; and if it be not deep, and it be fresh throughout, if thou set not at the first hour the powder, thou shalt not bind it with the blood that comes out, but shalt remove the wound, and anoint the patient; but thou shalt put in an effectual astringent, and bind it twice the first time. If thou hast no astringent, if thou put in the wound old cotton to soak up the moisture, and shalt make the patient sleep upon the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there come no spasms, neither tremor of the body nor straining of the bowels. And when thou seest the bones arranged, that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the tonsils and other cures, as long as they are sane; and if they cannot be cured, and if there is an opening, drain the pus that has formed; if the cure is necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut or a knife, and it is simple, or worse at the front or behind, if the treatment for what is before is necessary; if it is large, suture; if it is small, powder; and if it is fixed in the bone, and has broken pieces, if you wish to close the wound, and the surrounding parts are loosened; and if they are not loosened, if you leave it open, if it aligns the extractions; and for other wounds, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	But about the loosening of the belly...
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The bursting of the belly is great and medium and small; from a great wound never does the intestine come out, or the nerves of the intestines, because of the introduction of blood; and the suture is more painful, and never is better than the small wound than the great, because it returns to its points more easily; for as the intestines swell up as much as they feel the pain, if they return more to their points, and for this reason is better the lesser wound, because it makes us return the intestine to its place as with others. And pus that the wound of the belly is in three ways: the two common sutures come in the suture of the belly, and the suture of the other wounds of bone and two other proper sutures are common as other wounds; and all of them are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say one word and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestines is pressing, and only a little thing is protruding, this may be remedied in two ways: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, soak a little in a mild way: moisten a sponge or lay a damp cloth over it only, or soak in lukewarm water squinching and spiking, and draw out the intestine as long as it swells; and do not do anything that might restrain it, for it is better that it swells out naturally.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is filled with water or is high and tough, because by this is the entrance to things; and if it cannot enter, if you make a hole in the wound at the instrument, you can compress the blood clots; and the first cure is to make it soft, that we should not cut without great necessity, for this is the instrument for the wound: if you dig inwards in the curve and push outwards no, and if you do this the shape will be like this:</start_of_turn
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen, and the intestine leaps forward, if you stop breathing according to nature in its own place, you will have done nothing, for this is of no avail.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, if you must manage the patient lying on his back, and lift his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, put the head and arm higher than the lower parts, and if the belly is twisted in one of the two parts, put the effort in that the upper part is higher than the lower. And thus you must manage what I have said in great and small wounds.</start_of_turn>
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, do this: put between your hands I minister of pity that holds all the twist at its hand, and unite the lips; this is the common method of stitching, and take a needle or more according to the quantity of the wound, then leave the head of the wound I should have space, and pierce the two holes of the skin with the two holes of the siplac, which is the skin under the skin, until you have pierced it from that part, and reunite the two heads of the siplac the three together; then strain a double thread around the needle at two parts, then reunite the two holes of the wound backwards, and then leave I should have space, and pierce another needle; then join the thread as you did for the first needle, and do not cease doing this until the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be moderate, between slender and thick, for the slender needles are too slippery and the thick ones do not penetrate well; for this reason they must be moderate; and do not push the needles too far from the skin and leather, for they do not penetrate and open the wound before the suture; then close the holes of the needles, that they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and put on bands or dressings over the holes of the needles to hold, and leave them on until the wound is sutured; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds, for there is only one needle or two at most for the second suture, and that you reunite the two holes of the skin and the two holes of the siplac with one needle or there is I strong middle thread.</start_of_turn
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I will restore the intestine when it has been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound has healed for fifteen days; then the cure will be complete and he will be healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the patient had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any medicine, for I was in a land where there was no medicine, no remedies; and I treated him only by applying pressure on the wound twice a day, and by giving him honey water until he was healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me two ways to suture: take the needle and pass it from the underside until it reaches the midpoint; when it has pierced the right edge, if the tissue is soft or slippery or if you have slipped the needle, and you must pierce it from another part of the underside until you reach the midpoint; and you must understand this method as if you were a leatherworker, and that you leave once the spicule on one side and take it back on the other, until the suture is complete.</start_of_turn
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does with care, if done as others do not, which brings together the two parts naturally, and joins one chief to the other chief in part: pierce a needle or chief near the margin and pass it through only the lower part, leaving the two chiefs of the margin; then draw up the needle and pass it through from the underside until it reaches the middle, leaving two chiefs of the margin; then pass through one and the other from the underside until they reach the middle, in two other chiefs of the margin that are on the other side; and this is the wisest method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens says concerning this matter that no one testifies to it; we must sew the belly with two needles, or there must be a thread in the yarn; and one needle must be pushed in from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and when the gut has returned to its normal position, if the stitching is tighter than others on the gut.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judge of the wound is such as the judge of other wounds: when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even though it has moved, if you stop the intestine and the gut; then put on the healing powder, and if it has moved, do not put on any ointment except what is present, until the wound is healed; and close the wound, and let the dressing and bandage remain; then cure the wound as with the others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicine, put on nothing until it begins to secrete blood, cotton wool, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	You need no other medicine in many cases except for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound will not heal as usual, cover the principal parts with loosely woven linen moistened in warm oil of poppy or rose oil, and bind them around the wound; and if there is pain or gangrene in the bowels, and it happens repeatedly, if you give the patient black vinegar enemas, and in the same way if the gangrene reaches the intestines; and pierce it through, and drain what is inside as soon as it is the large intestines, for it is lighter to heal than the small intestines.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeuns" cannot recover when they are swollen, because of the swelling of the veins, and the slightness of the whole body, and the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if blood spurts from a wound, if it returns backward just as much as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is black and becomes towards or black, if you must tie the black part, since there are veins and arteries there; then close what is between the ribs, and suspend the two ends of the limb from the part below the wound until the spurting stops, to align the extraction when the blood spurts out, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	except for the root of the boil.</start_of_turn
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, if one can restore it in small pieces, because I have seen that one bone has been swollen or injured by a lance; and the wound was at the stomach and became filled and became a fistula, and in this there was vomiting and diarrhea; I put a cure for this according to what I could, and did not cease to make it gentle until it was healed, and the wound healed
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	When I see it soldered, I doubt that the patient has no harm in his belly; and there is no harm, but it remains in many better conditions, meals and drinks; and they say no experimenters have observed that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be ligated in parts: take tweezers and grasp the edges of the wound, and when the tweezers have grasped the edge, if it comes loose, put two fingers on it, so that it stretches its edge upwards; and then pull the tooth, and this will hold if it does not slip, and put another clamp afterwards in that manner until the wound is whole.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief of the intestine bursts, and there is no other nuisance to the patient, and it can be ligated with a thin silk thread which is cut from the intestine of a beast, in parts: take the head of this thread of intestine that is freed, and then join to the head of this thread one thread of silk that is twisted, then pass the thread through the needle, and in sew the intestine, and retain it in its place; and this manner of stitching with tweezers is not fierce except according to the way of making and hoping; and if the wound is great and wide, even if it is in one of the great intestines, if there is no other remedy, except for subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	or that it should be cut out.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds that open or are incised, when they burst, if they be called universally 'fistules', and even when they are shut and drawn in.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is truly a wound that must endure and swell, or else there is no pain, and it is as shut as the quill of a bird; and sometimes clear, sometimes thick; sometimes little, sometimes much; sometimes not at all, sometimes rather. I have already spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no decay, is only by one of the seven deadly causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the wound or the toughness of the flesh; or by its malice; or because there is toughness within, and on the surface, that does not allow new decay to arise; or there is too much swelling; or the blood vessels are hardened, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good at the cure; or because the corruption is like that of pestilence; or because the property of the region is late in digestion and in healing, and flees by nature; or there is a vein or bone: and I have already mentioned all these causes, and their signs and their cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you should know that I will tell you the cure for fistula, which is made by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Wounds that have occurred in all limbs because of pain; for there are wounds that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the jaw, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spine, or in none of the joints of the hands or feet; and if part comes from the property of the principal limb, and the rest.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All wounds of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance; and if there is no wound that does not come down to the bone except as I have said, you have no hope of a cure, and you must know that it is in vain to attempt to cauterize or to burn it, if the wound is straight; but if the wound is crooked, if you attempt to cover it over with a sliver, for it will swell up with the swelling of the wound; and if the wound is torn and you do not cauterize it well by attempts, if it bursts through one of the rents, for the moisture is too short from one rent to another, and it softens; then you must know well where the bone or nerve is, and if there is any break or fracture, and ask the patient of the pain he feels at the touch of your hand, and the place where it hurts; and when you know truly the place or it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or in some of the things that I have told you, if the dressing agrees with what I have said, and if there is a fracture, you must force the fracture and the corrupt bones that are within; and then the cure until it is healed, and if the wound is well penetrated from the straight side, if you must force it, then put on gentle dressings and keep them until the medicine has eaten away the superfluous matter that remains at the bottom; and then put on oily poultices to the wound, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, if you must cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is fractured from the wound, if it must be set.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve is not swollen or the principal limbs are affected as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, if the latter persists as long as the corruption is entirely bony, then cure the underlying cause as much as possible; and if it is not cured, and if the swelling persists as before, evacuate the matter until it is all gone; if it is evacuated and the corruption is completely removed, restore the limb; and if it is finally cured, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, evacuate the matter until the corruption is sufficiently gone; if there is nothing else to be done except to leave it to its natural course; and if there is a small fractured bone, and you wish to treat it, if the instrument is appropriate for the case, and if there is any remaining bone, break it off; do not leave it in place.
