If moisture opposes you, and there is no fear of error or fear of pain, crush and soften the bone and discharge it.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you do not remove them at an hour, put upon the wound some covering that will prevent corruption, and leave it until the flesh is fully healed around the bones; then it will be easier for the bones to knit together. And if it is a great bone, such as a leg or thigh bone, reduce the swelling as much as possible until the blackening is gone throughout the bone, and then restore the wound. If there is much of the bone that is corrupted, go up to the marrow of the bone; if you cover it and cover all until the corruption is gone, and then cure it until it is solid. I tell you of a fistula that happened to a woman in her leg, so that you may take notice and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man of about thirty years of age who had a pain in his leg for a cause that came from within the bone, so that the matter came to the leg, and he fled from a large abscess, and did not find any cause to open it; but he made it worse by his folly by opening it too wide, and corrupted a great amount of matter, and became a fistula, and there came out much pus that all the veins and moisture of the bone were consumed; and he remained there for two years, and there was no wisdom in the art of medicine, as far as I know, until I left, and I saw his leg and the medicines that were being given to him, and what was causing the pain from the abscess. His leg and the bones had become red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I stretched out a hand in one of these holes, and then circled all the holes, and found that one followed the other from all parts of the limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I made haste then, and grasped one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and putrid, and it ran from corruption right up to the bone within; I soothed what appeared to be corrupt bone, and I thought there was no further corruption, except for that which I had seen; and I began to restore the wound with soothing remedies for a long time, and could not bind it; and then I repeated the process, and again I uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I soothed it, and then held it steady, and I could not bear to bind it any further, so I left it with the wound open; but it healed and was bound up steadily, and did not swell again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and for the fear of death which I had avoided for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often is there bloodshed in the evacuation of an abscess, but he remained whole; and from his bone there sprouted a hard scale, and it was in good condition and caused neither pain nor discomfort in any way, neither from the heat nor from coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in no part of the limb, if you must bind it in this manner: take one thread, and stretch it to the head of the bone that is open, and command that no one extend it upwards; and put another thread of linen thicker than the first, and bind it over the scale which is coming out from the bone, and stretch the head, if you tear the corrupt scale away from the socket, and uncover the scale above the limb or where you see it bound, that the thread does not tear the scale; and put on a plug or a bit of lead at the bottom of the bone to cover the corrupt scale; and bind as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and bind again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open wide, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, if it uncovers the marrow fully; then put in a pair of tongs and then gradually join together the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, if you join the corrupted joint, join the bone that contains the other part; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, if there is no other angle except for the cover; and if the corruption is at the wrist or the elbow, if that thing is strong, but in any case you must inquire about that corruption, how it opened; and explain it in every way that you can, but that the vein or nerve does not hinder you; and that the incision and the stitches cover these bones many times, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of spots, and their thickness and thinness, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness. And for this reason it is necessary to bring to light a similar resemblance of work to that which is known; and that the work will show you the instrument which you must have, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manner of diseases. If you think that the instrument which you must have is that which is known to be necessary, according to this, then believe it.
dou feu	If you think the instrument is appropriate for the case, then use it as you deem fit.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head of the shoulder suffers dislocation through moisture, pressure, or violence; when you have treated the corrosion with medicinal means and it yields no benefit, if you cover that limb until the corrosion subsides, the patient escapes by this means of death or by the greater evil, the defect of the limb; the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corrosion of the limb extends throughout, embracing the whole body; if you are hasty in covering it, and if this is due to the percussion of venomous creatures such as scorpions of the sea and vipers, and similar things, if the corrosion is at the root of the bone, and you do not give it space to come out until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes up to the hand, if the cope is at the joint, if the corrosion does not reach the forearm; and if it comes to the forearm, if the cope is at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy but the quantity of its virtue; do everything as soon as the corrosion comes or leaves: if it comes in the first joint, if the cope comes afterwards in another joint; and if it comes or leaves, if the cope embraces everything; and if it comes up to the thigh, if the cope is at the knee; and if it comes below the knee, there is no other remedy but for the patient to die; and keep the limb covered or bandaged if you tie it below and above, and stretch one minister below and one above, and you remove the flesh between the two joints to the width of one thumb, until the bone is exposed; then cope or tie, and put some padding under the drape of linen, so that the silk does not touch the sound bone, and the patient will suffer no other lesion or incision except that.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood flows from a wound during treatment, if you cauterize the limb excessively, or if you apply restraining powders, then return to your medicine until it is complete; then bind the limb securely with a strong ligature and treat the wound until it is healed. And I will tell you of a case in which a black spot seemed to burn on the bone: that corrosion began at the root of the bone, as if by fire, until it consumed the entire bone. When we saw the corrosion, if we had covered the bone, it healed; but when we withdrew the cause of the corrosion, the corrosion returned. We were forced to amputate the limb because we could not stop the corrosion. I suspected that the patient's vital force was weak; and he died immediately after the amputation.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never comes abscess in the flesh that stays so long that it makes great swelling of the limb; then it returns and bursts, and in the jump the limb breaks, and remains limp as a vessel; and the skin which is under is as soft as a silken cloth, and does not go up to the bone, neither to the nerve, and such an ailment is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so prolonged that it comes down to the bone and breaks, it is called "fistula"; and if the skin is that you can cope that skin all around, and even when it is soft, like a silken cloth, and does not yield.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If you have suspected that the skin has hardened, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick like flesh, if the surgeon is skilled: look if the swelling is great, and the limb smells of urine, then make a blistering of Egyptian medicine which is made like this: take alum, oil, and alum, equally, and mix the ingredients in a vessel over a fire until the medicine is red and thick like honey; then take some of this according to your need, and make an incision in the abscess and drain the pus; leave the medicine in for two hours, then drain it while expressing; do this several times until the swelling is diminished and the limb is healed; never blister with vinegar, except when this medicine is not present; take vinegar of fennel, and vomit, then the pus will flow out, and blister with vinegar until you are certain that the swelling is well drained; if the patient cannot tolerate this, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the vinegar of vinegar and honey, or if there is a little bit of alum in the abscess, or if you have blistered with honey and wine, because honey has the property of softening and washing out, and the wine makes the pus rise up; when you have done this, and you are certain that the swelling is well drained, if there is any pus remaining in the wound, take astringents and make a poultice with oil rose and wine; or you can blister with other medicines and unguents, of which I have spoken of their properties or how to make them; and if the wound is too large, if the opening of the incision is too wide, or if the pus has flowed out, if the incision is too low, or if the wound is too deep, do not attempt to make the incision, but place a patch of unguent over the wound, such as Egyptian unguent or balsam, until it is sufficiently widened.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the shoulder is dislocated, if you do not leave the skin loose, and if you do not cover the wound as you see, the limb will move to the lowest point below its normal position; for when the shoulder is dislocated, if you do not leave the skin loose and if you do not cover the wound as you see, it will move in such a way: the shoulder will move easily downwards and leave nothing of the shoulder behind; and take consolidating medicines to bring back the blood, and extend over a bandage which covers the whole wound; then draw up the forces around the wound until the hole is wider than before, because there are sponges on the other bandage according to the quantity of the hole, and put the hole over the wound to align the shoulder, and do not remove the large bandage until after once; and whoever comes out of the wound often hinders the shoulder from being aligned, and tears what comes from the shoulder, whether it is blood or pus or enough, or digestion, or indigestion; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is swelling or not, and when your medicine is in such a way that it is extended and you see the nature that comes out of the wound, if the wound has already bled, and approach the health; and then take off the dressing in the morning or the third day, and when you take off the dressing, if the limb remains stiff, put on another bandage and restore the swelling.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if it feels sick with a sudden vomiting after eating, its saliva that it does not taste sweet.</start_of_turn>
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poison comes secretly after a long tension, if you do not arouse yourself from the danger, for the danger is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	And if subtle poison comes secretly after a long tension, if you do not arouse yourself from the danger, for the danger is approaching. For there are some who delay their ailments in their wounds, and some who do the opposite; and if it persists stubbornly after prolonged rest, the veins that should be closed remain open; and if they are tardy in closing, they are drawn out, if indeed there be medicines that can dry up moisture in their essence and make them dry in their virtue, as in the case of diaphinit, for there is a great part of vitriol in it; take diaphinit and mix it with rose oil and the juice of a vine equal in quantity; then confect and use it. de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the opening of the vein.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess which arises from the swelling of a pouch of the hand, or the foot, or by chance arises in other two places; and when it is inflamed and care is not taken, if it comes to an abscess of the nail, it swells and bursts as much as it can until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance it swells all the way; and comes the corrosion until the bone, so that there is acute pain, and the head of the nail is large, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you have cured it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit, if you must, you must perform all the superfluousness that is removed from the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help when the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy; and when the nail presses the marrow, and starts to prick, and the blood flows, if you must put off the root of the nail that the marrow does not protrude, and keep the nail elevated, and gently remove the soft tissue, and apply a medicinal ointment composed of burning and corrosive substances to the root; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the bone is corroded, if the swelling is great and the pain severe, for as much as the corrupted bone cannot be healed; and if you see the bone broken, if the swelling is in the joint as it is before, then treat it until it is healed. And if it is inflamed and swollen, and there is great pain, it is proper to drain it first; then cut the nerve that is beneath the swelling, and keep the cut from reaching the cartilage that is below the nerve, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if there is pus, put something above which will soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that most frequently occur in the hands of peasants by chance are completely cartilaginous, and by chance there is a part where there are bones, and never a nail, and none are born in the root of the joint, or they are born from the peasant’s bones themselves
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born without a wound does not move; he who is born at the joint of a wound, by chance moves; the size of him that is fleshy is slight, in part like this: size like the root of a large sponge.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which is born at the root of the shoulder joint is grief to cure: if you keep it covered.

He who is born or must at the rear without a wound, if it be that you must first circle the round flesh up to the bone, then circle the bone to a reasonable extent like this, then cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come from birth, or from a wound, or from the burn of fire, or from similar things.

des vils	From the wiles
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	From the wiles,
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not give them any purgatives of bile, and then the remainder of the nourishment.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure for iron is as follows: two methods. One is with the forceps, and draw out the black blood. The other method is if you tie up the vein, and draw out all the blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size is as follows: first stretch out the hot water-soaked limb, until the great vessel is not felt to be taut; then strain the limb of the patient from under the hip bone up to the knee; then clamp the vein in one, or two, or three places, of a large size, then cut and draw out the black blood from your hand, from the thumb to the little finger, until as many as the patient can bear; and then bind it up and command him to eat nourishing food; and resume the evacuation and the bleeding when the veins are full, and do not harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The wounds are treated thus: open the limb of the patient, if there be hair, then bathe it in wine or oil; elevate the limb in hot water until it turns red, and swell the veins. If there be no wine, if the fire is kindled, then burn the edge of the vein to the long side of the elbow or on the ankle; then strip off the skin to the bone, and draw out the vein from the bone end until it appears; and you will see it red and black, and when it enters or the skin appears like a white thread. Then withdraw the clot, until it is level with the skin, then reinsert it gently, then burn again in another place. Repeat this process until the clot is gone; then burn again. If you do not burn it out, if there is a staple left in the flesh, grasp and pull it out, and there will be blood loss. Keep your hand steady on both sides until it is all out.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the eye is contracted and tortuous and enclosed together, and it is not straight, as we have said, if you must force it open, do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of iron with which we cover the eye is curved, and do not pierce through, but only cover the vein; and is of great curvature, for if it were slight, it would pierce the vein, but let it be great as we have said, and this is the form.</start_of_turn>
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein.</start_of_turn>
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is enclosed in the limb, in hot parts or where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth or where there is no moisture; and by chance it arises from another part except the limb, and this comes from the corruption that comes from the decaying of the leather, as it comes from within the serpent's body and outwards, enclosed between skin and flesh.</start_of_turn
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if there is a sign of the commencement of this vein when there is a great inflammation in the limb, then it chains itself up, and the vein becomes swollen as if it were the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	If the limb is open, if it is suspected that the surrounding area has been affected by a wound for about one and a half inches, including the nail, and the nail is left in, and the surrounding area is left for a while, every time it swells, if the surrounding area is wrapped around the nail and the nail, and if it is too long, if a portion is pared off, and the remainder is wrapped around, and is not firmly secured at its root, for if it is left without support, it returns to its original position and causes swelling or pus and harm; therefore it is necessary that it be treated at once and not left for a long time, and that nothing remain or adhere to it; for in many instances concerning this vein, when it is treated with five palms of length, or ten, and one hand has already come to me, from ten palms of length, when it is pared off, there has been one or two fractures of the bone, and the bone has been perforated right through, so that everything has gone awry; and let the material that is within be evacuated, and mix with medications that will promote healing, without causing further pain, and then cure it like other wounds.

And never in this vein have hands rained, even when it opens at the elbow or the wrist, and there comes forth blood from the opening; cure it therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never in this vein have hands rained, even when it opens at the elbow or the wrist, and there comes forth blood from the opening; cure it therefore as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buffalo sickness", for it often causes swelling of the groin, and is a small vein that arises between skin and flesh, and runs throughout the body, ascending and descending, and causes pain throughout the limbs as far as the skin is taut or is stretched, and spurts blood; and is accompanied by the emission of various humors, as towards worms and serpents and lampreys and scabs or intestines; and it is doubtful of its malice, for when it runs through the body and reaches the head, and comes out, by chance it returns and destroys the marrow; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it healing and treating, if it will not force its way out, if it can be held in check, then indeed bind the limb above and below with a strong ligature, and then press above and it will come out. If it is not extracted, if you cauterize the fire upon it, until it dies; and the greater damage it makes, if it breaks the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the oil, then grasp the outgrowth and press it out, and press above and it will come out. It is proper to use the patient of various medicines for resolving humors and eating nourishing foods.

Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in various members, and because it moves from member to member; and I have seen this.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and found her arm swollen, and saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm; and after that, I saw it rise up like a worm on the shoulder, more erect than anything, as if alive and silver as when it bursts from its root; the pain departed from that root and settled in the shoulder, and then a moment later corrected throughout the limb, until it reached the other arm; and she told me that it often returned to its place, just as I saw it.</start_of_turn>
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it twisted back and forth between the limbs, for I had never seen such a disease in this way before.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I do not know whether to maintain that the pain moves from limb to limb, but I do not believe it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that it was because her limbs were stiff and her veins were exposed, and because of that appeared that constrained wind. I do not see it according to these reasons in those who have delicious food and moist limbs and veins replaced.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	When you see the healing of this ailment and the patient feels the pain, if it is shown to you that the pain is increasing, and that the swelling below and above has become inflamed, then you should apply a cautery to the limb until the swelling subsides; and if you do not see it disappear from your eyes, if you have cured the cause of the swelling, as for example with foul pills and serpin pills, and similar things.
des saiettes	When you see the healing of this ailment and the patient feels the pain, if it is shown to you that the pain is increasing, and that the swelling below and above has become inflamed, then you should apply a cautery to the limb until the swelling subsides; and if you do not see it disappear from your eyes, if you have cured the cause of the swelling, as for example with foul pills and serpin pills, and similar things.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The bandages are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the nature of the pain or the reason for their use.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their points is such that some have large points, some have small points, some have teeth, and some have sockets; and some have two angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces; and that which bites in no limb bites in two ways: either in the principal limb, as for example the brain, arm, forearm, breast, ribs, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it hurts and she cries out in no limb of these members, and a sign of death, that I will tell you later, I will teach you: if you doubt the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many dispositions; and when this sign is bad, do not doubt, the arrow is not withdrawn, if the wound is treated, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and jumps the blood vessel that is above the brain, is when scraping and soiling and twisting and vomiting and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of senses, and vomiting of bile; and by chance it is without fever or headache; and by chance it loses speech and voice; and jumps from the wound moist white pus resembling grapes, and just as with blood red of charcoal; and if this sign tells you, if you remain silent, take out the arrow if it is not embedded.</start_of_turn>
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	When the nipple is bitten or cut, the sign is that it is close to the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not soft; and by chance the nipple moves like a poulce, and in dark blood, and comes with cold sweat and chills, and fainting: the patient may die with doubt that the blood has drained out.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an infected wound is that it never swells without pus leaking from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes high and cries out in pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow comes out through the covering of the wound, if it is small, spit out great pain and great swelling and cries out; and moves all the limbs stiffly.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow comes out or through the stomach, by chance there is no undigested meat from the wound.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow comes out or through the belly, and there is no sign of stool in the intestines, if there is no hope for the cure, do not attempt to extract the arrow.</start_of_turn
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the bladder stone breaks in the bladder, and the urine spurts out and comes out forcefully, the patient feels great pain: such pain as the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	As for the other members, if the face, the neck, the chest, the armpits, the groin, the thighs, the arms, and the legs are affected, and the rest of the body, they are all subject to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the bladder stone is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I have said before, because of this I do not know what to say.</start_of_turn>
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	There was once a splinter which had penetrated the earlobe: I grasped it, and as I pulled it out, I extracted a piece of fat from the ear, and it was cured without any further discomfort
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out a splinter from the fat of the olive oil from the marrow of the bone, and the splinter was restored, and did not leave the head towards the heel, and it was as large as a Turkish bow; all that was left was to listen carefully to the ear, and the pain ceased, and there was no further discomfort
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And take out an arrow from the throat of a peasant, and the arrow was Arabic at the ear: I soothed the beards, and moved secretly as long as I took it out, and the peasant was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And took out an arrow from a wound, which was in the side or belly, and thought that it was going to die; and then when it had not passed three days, and it did not recover its position; I cut above the wound, engaged it, and pulled it out, without any bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if someone has an arrow wound in the side or back, and the wound is deep; and when the arrow has been pulled out from within, do not bind up its nature, do not hinder its natural works in any way
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And another man had an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound was deep; and when it suffered great pain; and many similar things happened.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And take out an arrow from the king's arm, that was stuck in the middle of the night, and was a great decline to the lower part; and the arrow was completely recovered. I was called to the treatment after that when it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If you find the wound very painful.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I would have you try to close it entirely and do not feel it; and there is no pain or tingling in the surrounding area
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I put on the plaster poultice digestive, so that it would not swell; and I found the arrow coming out on its own
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on the plaster for several days, and closed the wound, and left the patient lying down for a long time, until he felt the arrow still inside his chest; and he told me
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I place upon the wound the corrosive medicine of vinegar by hand and days, until it was overgrown; and I held it, and felt the head of the splinter which was breaking at the root; then I joined in the opening of the wound by that vinegar medicine, as long as the head of the splinter appeared visibly; and it passed well the end of the third month, and then grew so that I could put in the nails, and I held one part and the other, and could not stir; so I ceased to toil and to intrigue in ways of cunning, as long as I took it every day as the nails were well made, as is said at the end of this chapter, until I finished it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors say that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or tell me what is the quality of the extraction of these arrows, so that you put your cure on that which I do not say, for the books do not teach me all; but you know masters better than I do about many great things, and about that which is present and lacking, find nine works, and a new instrument, at the descent of the strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not go out of the limb or are fiched by force, for there are two ways: either by the force of the liquid or because they enter; or by another way. And that which leaps for the liquid or enters, that is the arrow that is pierced through flesh, and leaps never does it now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not leap now, if you leave it as long as the bones are carried inside, and if it is relieved, the issue will be released; and just as if it is pierced through bone and cannot withdraw, if you leave it there for some days, and move it every day; and then it will leap, and if it does not leap, if it is pierced through all the soft parts, until the bones are swollen, and then you pull it out
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the splinter is firmly fixed in the bone of the shoulder, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and any other ailment that I have mentioned to the patient: do not grasp it out immediately, but leave it until it is even again afterwards for several days, because if the splinter comes as far as the surface of the skin, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	If the splinter is only firmly fixed in the bone alone, and goes only as far as the surface, and remains in the patient for several days without any other mishap, then the patient must be treated for it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is firmly stuck and will not yield, if you administer oil around the circumference, as I have told you; then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	If the splinter is embedded in the bone so that it cannot be seen, if it has been tried in every way; and if you feel it, if it has to be grasped with no visible instrument; and if you do not wish to risk the wound and the depth of the splinter, and there is no bone, nerve or vein in the vicinity, then hold the wound open until the splinter is removed; and if there is any cartilage that is attached to two parts of the muscle that you must grasp, and then break or crush the cartilage of the splinter as much as you can, until you can remove it; and take care that you do not break the splinter, that you grasp it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not do it at once, if the limb remains limp at its entrance, then carry it out, for the extraction is joyful.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if bleeding opposes the treatment, if necessary, remind the patient of the cure mentioned in this chapter; and beware of incisions of the nerves and veins, and put in place what you wish to remove the arrow safely, either quickly or slowly; and lay the patient as he was when the arrow went in, for this is the greatest aid. If you cannot do this, follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or if it reveals nothing of itself, or if the skin is swollen in the place where it is seen or felt: then make the opening wide enough so that the forceps can grasp it, and then extract it: if possible immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if you round your hand around it until it enters the bone, widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be grasped, if you leave it in, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; if the arrowhead has become loose, if it has all its force; if it is split, and you see it is necessary, if there is a curved instrument, so that the tip of the arrow enters the curve of the instrument; and then extract it, and if the arrow is hooked, if the instrument has a pointed entrance, to facilitate the extraction.</start_of_turn
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the wound is surrounded, if you must, grasp all the surrounding tissue or the poison is there; if you do, then cure the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the wound is bleeding from the armpit, the hip, the belly, the bladder, or the ribs, and it is close, and you must cover it, if you grasp; and keep covering the wound and the nerves, and then extract it, and then close the wound, if necessary; and cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the nails with which we treat the saiettes is like the beak of an osprey, and thus is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many methods: great, moderate, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape at the end of the shoulder is like the wing of a bird, to push the point of the wound outwards, as it is like this.</start_of_turn
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the nails to push and to grasp if this is the case:
des voinnes dou cors communes	From veins of common cause
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins that we must know are about sixteen in number: two veins that are behind the ears, which are close to the two «herbs»; and two arteries that are in the two temples that appear; and two veins that are in the two armpits, which are close to the «aspirates»; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two veins that are at the collarbone; and the two veins that are under the tongue.</start_of_turn
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins in both arms are five in number. One is the cephalic, and it runs on the left side of the chest; they call it the great vein. The middle one is called the fasted, and it is composed of the cephalic and brachial veins; they call it the arm vein. The brachial vein if it is either right or left side runs on the chest; they call it the belly vein and it is above the scapula, and this is the one from which we take blood, which appears openly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The ulnar vein is between the elbow and wrist, and if there are two, there are also three in the leg and foot: one which is below the cubital vein of the left side of the chest, the second which is in the ankle of the right side; and the vein which is called the sural, which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps to expel old blood and foreign matter; and the quality of the blood, as I have told you, is that you raise up the head of the patient and wipe away the blood or the veins are of a rough texture; then stretch out the patient’s neck with a hook, as long as two veins appear behind the ears in two loops depending on the head: if the patient has a sense of swelling on one side, or if he feels a throbbing on one side, this is a sign of infection; then take the lancet and pierce through the vein until it reaches the bone, then keep your hand over the whole vein above, and clench and pull the skin and the vein well together, and make the bleeding cease as long as you see; then strain and tie, until it is healed; and I have already mentioned the incision and the cautery or first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries which are in the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration, sode, and obtalmia which is customary, and at the root of the tears there are glands; and the quality of the physician is such as I have said: and that the patient has strained his neck, as the two veins open widely; and he feels the pulse down his thumb, and then he seizes; then he places his index finger on the vein above his thumb, and removes the lancet from the vein, and places the vein above, and the cope, as he has done in two other veins, and makes correction of the blood according to his need; then he frees the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, then places on cotton; and then the bleeding stops, and he leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of this above and of its treatment and its extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as the blood from the cephalic vein; there are diseases of the face of old age, and a migraine, and redness; and if the patient strains his neck twisting, as the vein bursts; then take the instrument which is called the "forceps," which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as the blood from the cephalic vein; there are diseases of the face of old age, and a migraine, and redness; and if the patient strains his neck twisting, as the vein bursts; then take the instrument which is called the "forceps," which is like this. Put the point on the vein, and hold with your hand, or something else, and let the blood escape according to the quantity that you see; then loosen the patient’s neck, and ligate the vein until it is whole and never again let it bleed from a wide opening.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not fitting that the flames be too great; and the same with the vessel, for the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.</start_of_turn
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood from the two veins that are two fingers wide helps with the swelling, and the stiffness, and the redness, and the yellowness, and there are diseases of the face; and the quality of their blood is that if the patient strains his neck twisting from side to side, as before; then do the same, and let the blood spurt, a little long with a wide flame, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance if it breaks; then make evacuation of blood, as much as you are able, and then bind up the wound, and bind it firmly.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein does not flow if it is cold, and with swelling, and with diseases of the face, as with measles and redness that comes on the face, and even when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient bites his neck, then he strains his head to his left hand, and takes a long flame, and puts it into the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open very well indeed; and without beginning to correct it now, it will not recover; and do not go too quickly, but correct the blood according to your need, and leave it for one night, for it is quite restored by then; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two veins helps to ease swelling, and to begin mixing, and with many diseases, and with boils, and corrosions, and herpes, and tumors; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient bites his neck from both sides, as we have said; and let the master be on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on one seat, then grasp the vein long and wide, then draw the blood calmly, or as much as is necessary; then do the other half in the other vein, then remove the ligature, and strain the veins moderately, that the patient is not strangled; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the liver.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins from the arms above helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and wounds of the arms, and swelling and pain.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	When the blood of the liver is dark, command the patient to hold his head forward and grasp his collar as I have said; then open the liver, and see if there are two veins, one on the right side of the liver and the other on the left side, and know them by their darkness, and because there are small black veins running alongside them: grasp both of them, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, if you grasp the larger one from the front, and like so do the two veins that are below and above, for this is the right method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	When the blood is dark of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	When the blood of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the blood of the cephalic vein, and it is at the widening of the throat, and with eye diseases, and with mouth diseases; and the blood is dark if the patient sweats between his hands before the sun, and he holds out the tongue, and look under the ribs on both sides of a black vein: grasp both of them, and do not press too much, for there are arteries there.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins which commonly cause pain are usually sound in two ways: either by pricking with a burning flame as large as a match, or by olive oil as thick as cut trenching, and is called 'anesil'; and they are large and thick according to the size and breadth of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the violent flame is known, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there is another method for opening the large veins filled with visible blood, which contain blood and blood clots; and this is the form of the olive oil flame
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And is more subtly pointed, and is for healthier the veins subtly, or there is subtle blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.
