The blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps to relieve diseases such as hoarseness, and cough, and pain in the feet, and in the belly; and it is useful for healing wounds and preventing infection from the artery which is next to them.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it bites the artery, and blood flows out, if you must hold it back, as I have said; and do not make the flame too large, but keep it as thick as an 'anesil'.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the swelling does not visibly subside, if you must extract it, and bind another in its place; or if you wish to avoid any discharge, or if you leave the vein open in the arm: it will swell visibly; and the swelling will burn, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see the vein pulsating, if you must pull out the arm, touch the limb until you know its extent; then sign the limb, and then bind the arm, and close the vein with the flame; and beware that you do not damage the artery when you see the limb swell, for that is the artery: stop immediately.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see blood spurting out like the urine of a child, and it is pale and limpid, know that it is without an artery: hasten then, place your hand over the length, and stretch your hand until it does not bleed; if it bleeds again, bind the arm and leave it still, and do not move the patient; and if there is doubt, do not move it until it is healed
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If it is not bleeding, and it is painful, and the physician is not present, if the artery has burst, for the limb will shrink; staunch it without delay.</start_of_turn
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a sponge of alum, and make it, and take one half and bind it well until the other half; if it is without stain, it is well; if not, if the physician wishes, as we have said, powders that stain blood; and the styptic does not matter in many situations by the small extent of the wound, and the position of the hand.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in the middle helps to stop bleeding from the head downwards, and from the ribs, because it is composed of the basil and cephalic nerves, as we have said; and it is fitting for the patient that he move for the nerve which is at the ribs, and if it is not too deep, and if he finds the nerve, and it swells, the bleeding will either stop or will be reduced; and if the bleeding does not stop, the nerve is often opened several times, and if it does not open in some people because of its subtlety, it is fitting that you take the sensation away from the instrument that is anesiolized; and withdraw the nerve from your hand.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the armpits, if the blood flows long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The blood of the cephalic vein helps, that it pulls blood quickly, and aids the eyes; and it is best to cauterize with the olive or myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all veins, for it has neither nerves nor arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is best to ask more gently at first, and do not grieve if it does not work the first time; and by chance it will swell up with some people, which cannot be helped the first time, but it does not grieve anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is as you think.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about cautery is that it should only be used to preserve health and to ward off future diseases; and it should be done in one of the three veins that are or are not harmful: namely the cephalic, facial, or basilar. It must be done at the beginning of a prayer, in fasting and in eating afterwards when the sign of repletion appears; and it must be done immediately or after two or three hours.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The blood which is administered for diseases has no definite measure, but when it is necessary for spur or nut, at all hours and in all tensions; and it is not proper to give it to children under twelve years of age, nor to women who are pregnant for more than four months up to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	It is not permitted for the physician to treat those who have passed sixteen years.</start_of_turn>
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone sees a physician, in whatever way, if he commands the intestines to be cleansed with a mild enema, if there is retained bile, so that the veins do not extract the useful humors from the principal parts; neither too much meat, nor too little, neither too fat, nor too watery; and if after eating there follows colic, vomiting, and swelling of the belly, and multiple evacuations of the bowels, and vomiting, and guarding and vomiting, and all the things which are useful, or by weapon or poison; then subtilize the humors, if they are not too thick, by meat and by drinks and by medicines, if you have the power; then enter or bathe, so that nothing hinders the sublimity of the blood, and leave the vein empty from the wrist up to the third part, as we have said; and keep that occupation of work, of fasting, and of luxury, and similar things; and be tied and bound, and be more attentive than you are accustomed, and let the physician touch your hand twice or three times, and then remove the thread from below the middle, for if it is too tight or loose, it will not be able to correct it without; then touch the limb with your hands, until the veins swell, and you feel them; then moisten the physician with a little oil, then put his thumb on that vein below the elbow, which is where the physician saw the physician give the medicine, that the vein does not swell and cause injury.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like threads from a tailor, and if they are of such kind that are filled with windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is this; and if one opens the vein, if the wound is too wide, for this reason one must advise the tailor in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If the vein swells up for the first time, that is good; but if this does not happen, one must repeat the process several times, until the swelling subsides.</start_of_turn>
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	If the limb is inflamed and the patient is anxious, and one lets it hang limp or for two, and does not bind the arm: by chance there will be apostemes in the flesh; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it stops; and if the wound is small, or without proper support and you doubt that there will not be enough blood as you see, if you trust in this loss itself with all the flame downwards; and make the work promptly, even if the limb is inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If thou seest the limb inflamed, and dost not wish to renew the blood, put upon a little piece of lint soaked in oil, for it doth soften the pain of blood; and it doth stick to the limb the oil which is on it; and give the oil-soaked lint in the hollow of the blood which thou saest the veins, to stop the course of the blood; and this doth make a tremor and swelling about the limb when it is put on; if thou takest it off too soon and it is too great.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a great abscess, which happens often, even when it is not dangerous, save only when the opening of the vein is small, if thou art in a hurry, put upon the limb a wet cloth and a little piece of charcoal, and hold for an hour; and it is advisable that you do this after the blood has stopped flowing from the vein, and if it remains in the limb after a few days, no blackening or greening, if thou dost not see; and if thou seest, put upon no foreign thing or ointment made from eggs, mustard, or any similar thing.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is swelling and appearance of blood in the armpit: put your hand there and if you find the limb soft under the compression of the hand, if that is the bad appearance.</start_of_turn
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Listen then that you do not put anything of what we have said on it, for by chance in court without an artery; but make an embolus dry to harden the limb, then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and of the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is black, leave it be as long as it is red; and if you see it thick, leave it as long as it is subtle; and if it is too thick, leave it cool down.</start_of_turn>
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is to be done to the one who is fair and strong, and has the skill of extracting blood, to make the wound larger; and let the flame be large. And to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and keep it sound often, and must keep it sound by cutting across, without pricking; for this method of bleeding saves from the decay of blood and nerves, and is worth more than bleeding long rather than wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one who needs food for the blood, it is fitting to give soft bread in juice of pomegranate seeds; if he is pale, if take blood three times or four. And if he has a cold complexion, let him eat before the blood soft bread in mustard, or in aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant oil.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he pricks at the blood vessel after the evacuation of blood, it is certain that he will emit thick blood, and an odor of char, and use other things as we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he sees his arm fainting, and recovers again, if it is swollen with great blood, it must be bound up and bound up continuously according to the amount of its continuous virtue.</start_of_turn>
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever sees his arm fainting after the first bleeding, and has severe pain, if he recovers after nine or twelve hours after the first bleeding.</start_of_turn
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever sees himself fainting from another side, if he must recover later from thirst or hunger.</start_of_turn>
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is blood in the body which has already been sucked out, which causes fever; if you attempt to draw out a great quantity, and widen the opening too much, it will cause the arm to bleed profusely; since you must leave all the blood, and put your hand on the pulse when it is well, so that the blood does not reappear in place of the flesh, and this often happens when the patient is negligent; and do not attempt to draw out the blood a second time if you see the limb slip, and the opening is closed, as you must press firmly; if it is crooked, extend the limb immediately, for that would be harmful; but leave it until it bleeds a second time; or you can prick at the tip of the flame, until the one which is frozen at the opening of the vein is forced out, and put some sponges on it and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, if you leave it and do not tighten it too much, until the swelling is reduced.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary, the blood must be drawn again the second time, if the same one is in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is filled with blood instead of the one in the shoulder because it is composed of it
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And thus concerning bleeding, if the patient grasps his hand in hot water, until the foam be red; then bind it moderately, so that the vein opens properly; then draw the hand forward, neither too wide nor too long; or make an opening large, and bring the thumb close to the joint of the hand, and if it is not possible to return it, grasp the hand in hot water and leave the blood flow in the hand until enough; and if it be in this state, do not draw the hand in hot water again, for more is put into it than in this; the blood of this vein is more valuable than all the veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the saliva of the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the method: strain the hand and grasp it in hot water, until the vein is driven out if one sees it; and if it is drawn through, and if you do it all at once, do not grieve; do not go too far, for the nerves are all exposed without covering, and then grasp the hand in hot water again, if it is not frozen in the wound, and cannot be returned.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	When you have treated the blood as much as you can, if you put oil on the wound and bandage it securely, and then make each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth to the disease of the mouse, and do the same as I have said before about the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the sophene is worth for all diseases that are caused by a swelling of the body, such as diseases of the marrow, retention of flowers, diseases of the reins, and of the uterus and the old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its blood is that if the patient has become stiff in hot water, and has rubbed on the belly until it swells, and has put his finger under the joint of the bone; and if the belly is at the ankle, and from under the bone comes out drops of urine; the same as if there were a large wound or a wide wound at the ankle, or at the elbow, that the blood is worth more than any other blood.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you see blood on the hand, if you are wary of the nerves that are sore, and if the limb has been cut as if by a sword; or the flame is near.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be cured, if you reset the bone in water, and leave the vein wide open.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the patient has to be bled for the first time, if he begins the second time from under a little space, because the liquid is salty; do not doubt, as we have said, and do the same with the other arm equally
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The limb of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the buttock, and its blood is worth as much as the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that comes out.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the patient is in bed or in water, and he strains his ankle twice in turning, for otherwise he will not open the vein; and if it opens, do so in all ways that you can, and through and through; it is better to leave it closed, for the blood is thick, and it will soon return by itself.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find [the blood] flowing out or coming back in, towards the little toe, and you suspect it, take hold of the limb firmly; do whatever you can to staunch the bleeding, and then bind up the wound. It is now healed.</start_of_turn>
des sainies de ventouse	from the wound of the vacuum.</start_of_turn
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	And do so diligently with blood that you see, and then loosen the tie, put on a bandage and hold it; it is now healed
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction which is made by cutting if it is done in two ways: either it is with great heat or without heat; and the suction which is made by cutting and by extracting blood if it is done in twelve days of heat, of which one is at the top of the head; and the other is at the bottom of the head; and two others in the two corners of the head; and the suction of the tongue; and the suction of the two scapulae; and the suction on the buttocks; and the suctions at the two arms; and the suctions of the two legs; and the suctions of the two ankles; and the suction does not treat any blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not cause any harm, as when we make a bloodletting; and it must only be administered, neither with great heat nor without heat, in no disease that comes from repletion, as long as all the heat is evacuated.</start_of_turn
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if need be of disease it is allowed to speak, or by custom, if the attendants remain together for an hour at the commencement of the month, or at the end, and every tenth; for there are some who, when they must speak, have a heavy head; and there are some who find swelling and redness in their face, and in their head and neck, and dark circles under their eyes; and some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and spit blood; and some who think, and see nothing but blood and vomit and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	When we see these signs, and the patient is in a state of great fear and distress, we command him to fast for two hours.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The blood of the physician helps with the pain of the head … which comes from these circles under the eyes; and it cannot be done except after the evacuation of all the humors; and this vomiting is useful in place of the cephalic blood, and it cannot be done except by those who have a cold complexion in use, or who have chatarrh, for this makes them vomit greatly; and for this reason it is not to be done except with those who have a cold head and not with those who have hot diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And if those who are well-versed in the matter disagree, and for this reason it is necessary to place the ventouse somewhat lower due to the doubt of compliance.</start_of_turn
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The air that comes out of the head is in lieu of blood and bile, and for that reason it is worth more than gold, and it causes swelling of the face, splitting of the palate, and all around; and it is necessary to be able to push it out, for if it is held too firmly, it can cause swelling of the lip or cheek or stomach or side.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The air that comes out of the head is worth as much as the pains of the head, and vomiting and diarrhea, and strangulation, and toothache; and it is in lieu of the blood of the bile; and it is necessary that you command the patient to put his hand over his [artery], that he does not close the vein, and does not let blood spurt out.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds of the south blow over the mouth if it is sick with mouth disease, and with corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in the cause of the health of the teeth.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the south blow over the teeth if it is sick from heat and swelling
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The air from the chest is worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and command the patient not to be too tight, for it is dangerous, and knows nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling that is on the buttocks is worth having haemorrhoids from the foundation, and has diseases of bones and arteries; and it is recommended that the swelling be large and of hair, that it has much to do with well-treating; and by chance, if it should be ruptured, there will be great wounds
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings of the legs are apt to open widely, because they attract blood from all over the body, and cause old pains of the veins, and of the marrow, and of the bladder, and reinforce the flowers; and are in place of the spleen, and the kidneys, and all of them cause the body to swell up later on, and cause vomiting of blood in various situations.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the suction cup is as follows: if you apply it at first glance, and do so promptly, and put it on firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing so until you see the blood flow red and swelling, and open the wound; then withdraw, and take care of the patient’s condition, for there are some who have a tender scar, and clear pores: if you must cut once alone, and you must make large wounds, and a deep wound; and do so cautiously.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If it is not large, if you must cut once: the first time to staunch the flow of blood from the large vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If it is very thick, if you must cut three times; and when our wings grow weary of blood, if we only suffer once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if our wounds bleed profusely, if we rejoin them too often; and if they are not expected to heal, if they are fiercely inflamed, and if they persist even when the cause has disappeared, it is better for those who have thick skin and hard, and who have numerous pores, to apply to the wounds a liberal amount of aperitif and dissolvent oil: if it is for an abscess, violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is for a wound, cresson oil, or lavender oil, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluous moisture is great and cold, take olive oil of marigold, or balsamite, or olive oil of anet, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the wound has a thick edge and large pores, it is not to be oiled, but it is to be washed after the evacuation of rose water, or cold water, or elderflower water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if there is moisture in the mouth, if it easily rises, or of mistletoe, and sumac, and the like.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And he who has excessive liquor, from wine old or water of sweat, or decoction of elderberry or chamomile, or other like things; must not trust his health before the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and must not sleep after the ventosation, and must know that he must rise when he must rise and when he is risen.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard him who is feverish is cold and if he is too hot and inflamed; if you must give him cold things, as with pomegranate seeds and radishes and lettuce easily, and other like things; and eat barley meals, and broth of broth, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, if you give him honey syrup and scented wine medium, which is between old and new, and eat broth, and eat barley and eat herbs and small oils and simples; and when he must vomit, he must drink more than he eats; and you must not give to anyone triacle or mustard before or after the ventosation, but rather comfort the principal members; and be discreet about it, but he must only drink those who are hot drink it
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The wounds which are made to bleed are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and podagra, and upon the belly and the bowels and the veins and the testicles, for these members do not suffer from any wound upon their outsides, and they are made only to draw blood from member to member, as we do when we put them upon the nipples when they do not bleed; to remove the viscosity which is in the member, as we do when we put the cautery upon the belly and the bowels to make the member softer; and to stop the pain, when there is an opening or stone, for the opening or stone to be attracted by its attractive power by chance or to empty the stone from its place; and thus it is made high when it is put upon the liver and the spleen when there is retained moisture, and these cautery are administered empty without any liquid, and never administered together with water, except in cases of pleurisy, and in such a manner we fill the cautery with warm water, or with water or herbs that are appropriate for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the ventouse administered to fire is like this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And there are two large and half palms of mustard, or cost the rent of a thousand little holes, as for driving out an awl; and it may be of rain, sulfur before if it does not irritate the patient when putting it on the limb; and there is in the middle a twig of thorn or iron, to put a bandage on, and it is to be large or small according to the illness and the nature of those who take it; for the bellies of the sick are other than the rich, and the leaner than the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And must be placed on the limb: grasp the bandage with the thumb or index finger, and insert it through the twig which is already in the suction cup, so that it sticks neither at the bottom of the suction cup nor burns the patient; and then put it on the limb, and two must be placed either on the hole that we have said, or on the awl that has gone in; and when you pull, if there is vapor, remove the suction cup; and grasp the linen again as before, and repeat often, if you must.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the chest where it is administered in the disease of pleuresin, at all times, there is no bulge or perforation, and it is administered only when it is clear of pain, and is placed upon the limb just as little as possible; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	They are not administered except in limbs where it is impossible to place a ventouse because of their smallness, such as bones and teeth, and similar things; or in wounds stripped of flesh, such as wounds from nails or bites, and others; and when the quality of the patient is that when they find the bubbles that are in soft, clear liquids without any puncture, if they take them; and put a drop of sweet liquid on them until they are full, and do not have anything in their belly; and then either let go of the vein and the ventouse, or rub the limb until it is red, and put the bubbles back on; and when they are full and comfortable, if it is possible to put the ventouse back on, put it back, for it is worth more afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, if you raise the limb easily, and then with water, wet well, and then dry; and if the limb remains too long after washing the hair, if you pour a cloth of linen on the cold water, put on, until the hair is stretched; and if the hair is numerous, put on broken glass, or scraps, and the like, until it is stretched; or you take out half of the hairs, and leave them until they burn out on the limb, if you stop now; if you do more work, take out other hair.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the hair does not take hold, if you rub the limb with fresh blood, or you put in a needle until the hair is embedded, and then put on, as soon as they feel the blood, if they burn; and when you see that they are bleeding, if you sprinkle on some aloes and bruised saffron, or charcoal, they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Ci comence li livre des brisures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and displacement.</start_of_turn>
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Hear now, my son, for the matter which I speak of in this chapter is not found in any former book, neither in letter nor in practice; for this reason it is strange in our land, for I have never learned of it. I know of it only through the study of ancient books, or through my own study and experience, and by the habit of my life; and I have described it in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have summarized at the end, and I have made it clear the forms of the instruments which are brought into use, as I have done in the two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or write in the prologue of this book the sum of the word and the chapters or the knowledge that it contains, and that we remain true, so that those who are learned and who learn this noble art may learn from it and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when there is a fracture or dislocation or torsion or swelling that comes to nothing, if you command the patient to hasten recovery from the one side and from the other, if nothing hinders him, if he is not too weak in body, or if he is a babe or an old man; or if his pulse is not very strong, or too cold; and if he drinks cold water, or oil and vinegar, and does not drink wine, does not eat fatty foods, and does not fill his belly too much with meat, until he has overcome his doubt of incision and expansion of the matter in the limb; if the patient then returns to his former state, he will recover his government as before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, if you must nourish the patient with foods that cause great nourishment, or if he has viscosity, as with wheat flour in water, rye, peas, almonds, cheese, fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at a part nourishment returns muscle and more tension the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones that break in pieces and decrepit ones do not mend well by themselves according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs; for the same reason as those which are too tender, like bones of small children; but there is no cure, remain above the broken bone and hold the limb together, so that it reinforces as if it were before; and do not touch it at all, for because of this it is necessary to nourish it with large foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the limb, or of the foot, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others by bending, as with the size of a pen to write.</start_of_turn>
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small fissure.</start_of_turn
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And sometimes there is its own sign and its own instrument in restoration; as it is remembered that comes to its aid; and it is known that the breaking of the bone by that which it is twisted is opened well by pushing, and by the pressure of the hand; and when there is no swelling or pain, there is no break; but it may well have swelling, or fissure, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not know whether it is moving or not, but put on medicines that come later, and then strain it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	When the bladder bursts, which is two parts of the joint, it is necessary to set them even now, as well as the post-traumatic spurs which are left behind; and if the spurs are hot, do not leave any residue until the spurring has ceased; then set the limb even and gently, and restore the bladder more easily than if there were pieces remaining; then hold it.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, if it is thumb or toe, or at the hand if it is a small limb, or two strings, or an arm and a hand; set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the limb which are broken reunite, if you restore them by all means to the limb as before, and keep that in your work there comes no further injury or pain to the patient; and adjust the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if you think it is not well: if it is swelling well, and it is not straining too much, do not press as those who do who make it come by their work excessive heat and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at a joint, if the patient holds it firmly, so that he does not move it, neither by day nor by night, neither by turning nor in any other way; and keep the limb firmly so that he does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, if it is not at a joint, and you can put it into proper position so that he feels no pain; and keep it straight, so that there is no twisting when you restore it; and the quality of the limb will be as I have told you
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The quality of a broken limb is diverse in small, medium, and large sizes and shapes
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and thighs and the like: if you can cover them with soft and fine linen; and for those that are large, such as bones and legs: cover them with a wide and strong thread, for the large thread embraces the whole great limb and strains it equally, so that there is no slack; then put on firm supports, three turns or four depending on the limb, and strain your hand one inch all around the limb, then go up to the break and strain less, than the break then lets go an inch of the break; and soften the thread both above and below, as long as you take a great part of the limb still attached, then take another thread and turn the support around the limb; then put back to the lower part of the break, and strain moderately, not too strong or too little, as we have said at the beginning of this section; then put between the supports of linen or cloth, so that they are even all around, and then tie everything up with a bow, and then put your pins in place, if there is no incision or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or abscess, if you put upon something soothing the abscess burn, and which closes the swelling, and leaves it thus for some days; then strain upon your testicles, and let them be half of a large sausage-shape, or of cloth from which nails are made, or of poppy seeds, and be in this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the thread which you put upon the break be thicker and wider than the others; and be as long as it is appropriate for the limb in breadth or in length; then strain upon the testicles in the same way as you did at the first hour, and then bind them up with a thread of even thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, made of linen; for if the thread is thick, like those fools who make their threads from hemp fibers, that is a great mistake, for the thread will not be even if it is too subtle, and it will not hold securely.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is numbed by the blows of the needles after the stretching, if you put on stockings of linen or coarse cloth, they will not bleed
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a bruise, and the nerve is severed, I will tell the cure of that later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And as regards those who do not wish to endure this discomfort, they must immediately break the limbs the first moment.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not permissible for me to set these bones except after five days or seven, or more according to the severity of the wound; and when this method of ancient plaster is used to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take flour that adheres to the walls of the mill, mix it with abundant egg yolks, and make this confection, neither too thick nor too thin, and use it. This is the common method of plastering that restores the fracture in various positions, just as much for women as for men and small children, for it is neither too harsh nor too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains and linseed and alum and saffron and Arabic gum and mugwort, all in the amount of eight; mirrace and aloes, in the amount of five; chamomile, in the amount of seven; and grind them together, and mix them with abundant eggs; for if the complexion of the patient is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores the broken bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering that is good for torsion: take mugwort and chamomile, each in the amount of X, three; myrrh and aloes, each in the amount of VIIII, three; acacia five, three; and mastic gum ten, three; grind them well, and mix them with water or abundant egg yolks, and administer them.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of restoring joints and bones that have slipped out of place, and relieves the pain that comes with it, and reduces the swelling: take fresh linen, moisten it in oil and put it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These methods do not restore them completely, but they are good for relieving excessive swelling and pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other means of support that are worth considering are: dried fig tree leaves and terrestrial poppy leaves, ground together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of restoring the fracture and diminishing the remaining swelling
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of gentian, chamomile, violets flowers, barley flour, and fennel seed; grind them and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, soak it in vinegar or water, and apply
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Other methods of restoring the limb are more forceful than the first, when an abscess is hardened and comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of chamomile, seed of flax, balsam, melilot, and chamomile, of all an equal part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras writes in his book that there is no need to put anything on the broken limb to restore its force except for a little wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between soft and firm.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen would have us put on the warm parts of the member broken, to restore things dry a little warm, as for example, myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is worth for pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped almonds, or pine needles, and gum, and mix them evenly, and crush them, and make a dressing of them and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has his bone moved from its place; if you do not loosen by hand for days. And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, whether you are in a hurry or not, loosen it and support the limb now; and put on a lighter bandage, and a wet sponge, and immerse in water, and raise up the limb, until the swelling stops and the pain is relieved; then leave the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, soaked in water or oil of rose, and tie on a nut, until you are sure of the abscess is cured; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and be sure the pain is gone, then renew the gentle binding, and a little support, and do not bind too tightly; and be subtle until it is healed
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see swelling, redness, pain, and swelling about the bone, it is necessary to support and bind, if it recurs, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not yield to the limb what has been said, if it does not yield after three days or four, or five, or seven; do not leave it for twenty days, as we have seen, until the swelling has subsided and the limb has approached its normal position; then tighten the restraint more than before, and swell the meat, as I have said before; and if you see the limb become drier than usual, the swelling will not rise; then raise the limb with warm water, every time you loosen it, two-thirds of the time, and cut a vein. In this way the swelling will be removed from the limb and the patient will recover quickly from what the fools have done, who have left the limb twisted: that is bad, and if the disease is serious, I see nothing better than to leave it alone and do it right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	various ways of breaking.</start_of_turn>
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many forms of fractures are known, and various figures, and the causes are diverse; for there are fractures caused by the percussion of a spear, and the collar bone fractured throughout its entire length up to the syphus which is perforated by the bone, as in the case of the spear or the fist; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear pierces the bone in a transverse direction, and is called this kind of fracture "absolue"; and is the wound of these large or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fracture or dislocation of the bone, or fracture of the bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that approaches the socket which is below the bone, or it is on the bone, then this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound that is closed in the bone is as subtle as a nail, and the tear is small, and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a "capillaire"; and if the wound is made or caused by a stone, or by a thorn, or by a similar thing, and causes the piece of bone to enter the cavity, and the limb is bent as when carrying a burden when it is placed on the embers; if between the bones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in those who have soft bones or joints like children; and this happens in all these ways that small pieces break away from them like stars; and I will speak of it later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And there are many other ways of fracture when small pieces are detached from them as in these; and I will speak of them later.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary resemblance is known by this that when one has discovered the bone, and has wiped around it, if one finds a black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care of the patient’s accidents and if you see no other bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, emission of urine, extension, paleness, fever, and swelling, and other similar things, if it does not recover sense immediately.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you suspect no imminent danger, and hope for recovery, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the limb comes forward first, and it is in swelling, if you can remove the bone before the fourth part of the muscle that you must do so.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this state, if you hurry to remove the bone before the seventh part of the muscle, so that the tissue of the bone is corrupted, there will come the accident that we have said.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone comes up to the covering of the brain, if you must cut the torn part off: and that is that you grasp the head of the patient unmoving, and uncover the bone in all the ways you can, and on the figure of the wound more strongly than you can; and if blood comes out when uncovering the bone, or opening, if you are aided by this, that you fill the cavity with soaked cloths oiled with rose oil; and rest the wound until the swelling subsides, and be sure of bloodletting; then begin to bind the bone to stabilize, and this is done in two ways: one way if the cut is narrow at the front, and that is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then do another incision more extensive than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And thus if you have various sizes of testicles, some large and others small, and they are pointed and made of iron, and in their lighter work, do not bleed the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, if you must pierce through it, even though you administer testicles with tarres, do not pierce beyond the test bone. And you must leave above the point a margin or circle, that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of them, so that if the testicles come out in place of the thickness of the bone, if you have several tarres on the test; and this is the form of the two methods of tarring.
