Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the brittle bone is that you put one tarret on the bone, and turn your two hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the tarret back in another place a little later, and do the same thing to the surrounding area, and cut between the perforations, and do it more skillfully than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you have brought the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have if you have them, pincers; and keep your hands away from the brain and the jawbone.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	When you have perceived the bone and treated it, if it is possible, reset the fragment which is dislocated from the bone to all other instruments which are like incisors; however, it must be firmer and more flexible than the others. If nothing of the small bones remains, do not fear, if the bones are lightly held by instruments; then cure the wound with sutures and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of working is like the Galenicians say, which is more certain; and the lord is very strong, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, either by fracture or by opening the muscle, so that when you have uncovered that part, you put back the head of this lenticular incisor, for this is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not cut too deeply from one side, for the part which is injured lies between the two costs, so that if you cut towards the bone, then hold it in place with a small mallet above, so that you can easily support the bone all around; take good care of the cloth which is beside the bone, for if it is split from the bone, if the bone is easily displaced, because we must support it soundly, and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone breaks through the skin, do not pierce it further with a needle; cut it off just below the fracture, and there will be small pieces left. If you suspect infection, remove the surrounding tissue with a scraper or file of various sizes, in order to prevent infection in each place, according to the nature of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the fracture is great and after more scraping, and does not cease, do it until it is well healed.</start_of_turn>
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In some other capillary and fracture of a subtle kind, it is necessary to bring about the cause according to its location; and this is something that is not easily learned by anyone who has not put his study into this art.</start_of_turn>
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is discovered, you must take I drapeil of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and wet it in oil roset, and place it on the wound; then take I other drapeil doubled in II or III, and wet it in wine and oil roset, and place it on the first drapeil; and do this more gently than you can, that you do not damage the wound, then administer from above I other thread, and do not strain it more than is necessary to hold the wound only; and leave it in place for I or II hours, until the swelling has subsided, then remove it, and administer medicines such as radix of lis, and flour of times, and powdered incense, and an apothecary, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer appropriate medicines in moderation; and keep the wound clean, that you do not leave it dirty, neither do you leave it bound up tightly, for when it is bound up tightly on the head of the nail, if it is twisted and pulled, it causes great harm to the patient; for when something biting is put on the wound, if it is not held in place by something.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Beware then, if any evil event comes to the patient, as we have said, if there is any doubt, it is doubtful sense.</start_of_turn>
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if black bile does not depart quickly except by the medicine we have put on, that some virtue has, if you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one part of glue, and you apply it on the surface; then you will cure in the manner of cures that it is suitable, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Then follow the treatment in the way that is useful, as long as it is safe.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, if you can drink a little wine or vomit what you do not need, and put this break into your index finger and the little finger by pushing out, until it returns to its natural position; and do this gently, and keep the patient from feeling pain by your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the arm, and cannot go down to the root, if you can, put an even support under the arm at the height of a large rib.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, if you do it again, and hasten to restore the first limb, if you wish; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the inflammation of the wound has subsided, then bathe the head of the limb where the fracture is, and if the break is on one side.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you must bind it once more on another side if the break is there; and be the attempt as strong as to fill the hole in the limb.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restorer should attempt to break up the swelling in a burst wound, and die each for himself.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think it is good, but it is proper that they be softened with an egg yolk and meal powder; then leave the wound open until the bone is firm and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never do they put goose feathers in place of tents, and if there is sulfur powder draped around, and it is held in place, and blows the patient among them; or do as you see fit.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if they come to rest while you are working, if you put some butter or cotton soaked in rose oil or some such salve on it.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound does not bleed, if you put on a paste of fuller’s earth, oatmeal, and incense powder, confirmed with egg yolk, then put on light compresses, and do not bind it tightly; and if the break is small and is broken into small pieces, if you have suitable instruments, then cauterize the fracture, and close the wound with stitches, as with pastes and ointments that are suitable for this; and if there is no wound in the break, if you close the wound, and put on bandages, until it is healed
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the root of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without any wound, and the break is only slight, and is not broken through, except for the teeth inside, if one knows it slightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is advisable, if the break is on the outer part, to bite down on the thumb of the affected hand towards the mouth of the patient; and if the break is on the left mandible, if you hold the thumb of the right hand, and gently hold the break inwards, and hold the other hand outwards, and make them even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the mandible is displaced, that is to say, if it is displaced by .ij., it is advisable that you administer an extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth causes pain, or a dislocation, if strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put a broken mandible cerote on and put on an i. two-fold drape; and on the drape put a large sponge well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and tie on the suture that you put in place, and command the patient to rest, and eat soft food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure is changing, if the bone comes loose at the third joint, and then reset it to its place; and put on a dressing of powdered alum with abundant egg or oatmeal, after you have oiled the cerote; and put on a dressing of linen. If the dressing becomes loose, and the patient’s condition does not change, leave it as it is until it is healed; many times it heals in two weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if after suppuration the limb remains swollen, as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, repair so that neither part of the bone is left unboned; if delicate of the bone has instruments that cover this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, if the swelling has flared up as you need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have boned all these parts, and there is no longer any displacement, if the wound is wide, put on some dressings that cover this, to absorb blood, until it is healed
de la forcele	so strong.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strong force breaks several times before, over the shoulder, and the fracture is deemed to be in two ways: either it is broken and split into three pieces, and is the most light to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And when the fracture is with a wound, if you have two assistants, let one hold the limb that feels the strong force; and the other extend the shoulder towards the part; then set the fracture even, so that the form be as it should be, and there be no bulge or protrusion.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you must extend more, put under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of wax, or linen, of the size you need; and stretch and hold the forcele, and strain the ball in your hand, so that you can put the fracture even, as it should be.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you do not manage to push the head of the shoulder back in its place, because it comes out of its socket, you must know that the patient lies groaning on his side, and put a cushion under the shoulder blade, namely the middle rib, and hold the shoulder blade down until the head of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find debris, if you must, make an incision; and force the pieces lightly, and if the bones cannot join together by any means, if there is a fracture at one of the incisors that you have made; but that you put a cushion under the shoulder to prevent infection.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not at all crooked, and should be as wide as it can cover, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; and there should be two holes, as you see, one large and one small, as is the way of closing a wound that has been made when treating the bone; and when you are sure of the closure of the wound, if the wound is small, or if you doubt the closure of the wound, if you put a dressing and bandage over the wound, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the wound comes open again, if there is much blood, apply oil of rose, alum, and wine, and place above.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The tightening of the bone, when it is suffering from wounds and is being treated, is that you put on the bone powdered gypsum and egg white, and put on soft bandages, and put a ball of lead on the heel; then take a great band of silk, then put on two layers of bandage, and put on the gypsum; then take a subtle pin of three twoths of an inch in length, and wrap around that bundle, so that the head of the bundle remains in place; and put the pin on the bulge, and turn the bundle on its collar, and take off the heel of the wound, and the wound of the shoulder; and leave the chest part rest, and when you see that the ligament holds the bulge without any risk, and you see clearly that the pin does not move from the fractured bone, if the reward is repeated, and if the ligament is stretched; and do the patient rest on his back, and put under his heel a little pillow to lift up the shoulder; if you align the fracture by aligning the shoulder blade, or you bind the arm to the collar, and do not unbind it until it is badly inconvenient. Keep it like that for twenty days; then repeat the gypsum if necessary, and strain and leave it in place until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about eight days, and in less time for most people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it has to be done, and hold it and leave it thus until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time to any home.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the scapula is fractured or displaced from its normal position, it will not stay in the middle unless forced by pressure; if the limb appears according to the figure of the fracture, and is reduced according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can; then put the limb into a powder with abundant egg white, and bandage it loosely, and put on a double drape; then put on a broad and subtle splint, a little wider than the scapula, and keep the splint firm so that it does not move from its place; and look at the limb every moment to see if it is improving; and every time it becomes soft, if you re-extend the splint, and put the limb back in its normal position, and let the patient rest on his side; and the scapula will be restored in twenty days or less. And when this number is completed, if it heals, and be joyful, for it is not a bone that easily breaks.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone hangs forward, and does not yield at all, if it remains in place, and the bone itself, do as we have said in the bursting of the forcele to appease the pain of incision.
de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone hangs forward, and does not yield at all, if it remains in place, and the bone itself, do as we have said in the bursting of the forcele to appease the pain of incision.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The body is never completely broken in the middle, but it often happens thus; but it breaks often from excessive force.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in two, if it declines downward, and causes the patient great pain, and weakness, and vomiting, and by chance blood flows from the broken bones, and all that is well.</start_of_turn>
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is this: if the patient lies prone on his back, put one cushion between the scapulae, then press the scapulae together, and reassemble the ribs at your hands, and subtly bring into equal all the ways you can, until the bone is set as it should; then put on bandages and stamp under the staple of salt, or other soft substance, and wrap in one bandage, and bind on the bone break, if it does not move; and turn the limb round about the back, and strain gently, and reward chest pain an hour later, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if it will not come loose, by corrosion or by purulent discharge, or pain or swelling, if you are in a hurry, and it comes loose, loosen the bandage, and rasp off the dressing, and address what has happened in the manner of treatment; then rest the dressing, and strain until it is healed.

Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for after the catarrh has passed, life does not come back by itself.

And they say that no one puts on a bandage on the limb to soak up moisture, for it is like reason; however, there is doubt that the bandage will not retain the excess moisture on the limb due to weakness.

And if pus comes out from the wound, put on moist cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the limb; and treat until the limb stops bleeding at the wound, and do not touch the wound side or it must, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points to the navel, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is commanded to cut above the broken rib, and to put in a sponge; then one must cut the bone lightly, and then sew up the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with sponges, as long as it is healthy. Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a fracture of the bone of the collar, and often it rains; and also at the thorn of the back.

And when this happens to no avail, and you see that it will heal or not, if you take care that you see its hands softened and limp and dead, and that you cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, if you do not feel them.</start_of_turn>

And if a bone breaks, if you cover on the limb; and stretch the bone, then assemble the two ends of the wound, if it is great, with a splint, and bind it up securely; and if the fragment of the bone is broken, which is called the "break of the marrow", if it is in your left hand pouch, and put it equal to the right hand at your side, then put on the dressing and the bandage, if you have need of it; then strain it, and if there are broken bones underneath, if you leave it there, and stretch the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And so there are two methods for restoring it: one is to take one fist full of moistor and hold the patient’s arm above their seat; then bend the patient’s arm towards the shoulder, and put a curve in the fist, and then put the fist on no weight or have the assistant hold it down; and put the eyes level with the hands clasped together, until the dislocation returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is to support the patient’s shoulder and tie the arm to their collarbone, and command the assistants to hold what is on the dislocation at their hands, and to hold down the scapulae at their sides.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the shoulder blade is close to the head of the shoulder, command the patient to place the thumb of the middle finger on the lower part of the shoulder blade, and the other on the upper part, of the shoulder blade; and in like manner if the fracture is on the upper part, command the patient to place the thumb lightly, with force, as long as the fracture is equal on both the shoulder and the upper part; then set the fracture, if possible, and hold it, so that no aftershocks occur.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if after-shocks come, do not strain for more than thirteen days; put on a thick dressing of lint and rose oil until the after-shocks are calmed; then strain, and the way to strain is that you place the bandage over the bristle, then assemble the limb on the shoulder and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; put on the bandage and strain the limb, and the arm will be in its place, without anything hindering it, or without the bone being fractured.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints, and place on the bristle a splint that is wider and stronger than the others, and put between the splints two pieces of wood that are equal in size to the thickness of the bristle; then strain on the splints, as I have said above in the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the swelling subside, and the tightening, as we have said, when you have restored the limb, and you doubt the fracture is complete, if you leave it uninjured until the seventh day, as we have said; then observe for three days whether the swelling subsides or inflammation or discoloration does not occur in the limb, or that the limb does not regain its natural movement due to excessive tension
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the head of the shoulder, as we have said,
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	If no such accident has occurred, if he has slept for three days or more, and the patient lies on his back with his hands on his stomach; and give the sufferer a cushion filled with wool equally, and watch for an hour or two to see whether the limb remains stiff, or if the ligaments are softened; if the case is urgent by the power of medicine, and do the work that we have before us, in part as the meat must be at the first movement; and when it starts to recover, if it is large.

It is customary that the shoulder and limb must be restored within forty days in total; and then one must retake and administer oil baths and ointments to the affected part to restore it correctly
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If the constriction is painful and emboldened, if it persists for more than a day or two.
de la brisure du bras	In the event that the arm is fractured,
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of three bones, which are called the "radius" and the "ulna". One is small and the other is large. The small one is inside and the large one is outside; sometimes the large bone breaks alone, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are fractured, restoration is easy, and the healing; but when the large bone is fractured, if the healing is poor, it is more painful than when they are fractured whole.</start_of_turn>
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is fractured, if the limb is slightly extended and put into its place.</start_of_turn
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	If the large bone is fractured, if the limb is drawn more strongly; and it is extended over the thumb and keep the wrist of the hand higher than the other, and the small bone must be lower than the others, and the patient must be crossed over itself, and the thumb in front of it higher than the patient suffers no pain; then extend the limb from the elbow to the wrist, or to the thumb, and another assistant at the other side.</start_of_turn
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he sets the eye equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture the limb is split into pieces, if one puts in a pin without removing any splinter that may be left in, and you cannot remove it, you must leave it and let it heal naturally as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, as I have mentioned in the singular chapter; take the cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And when restoring the eye, if there are afterimages, if glue I drape with rosin and white wax, that it is neither too firm nor too soft; and I drape it superficially, until the afterimages are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then I put on the cerate, and put in place the filling of fine powder with abundant eggshell; and I put on the stars, and make the main star the strongest, and a little wider than the others; and let there be six stars or arms in various positions: either that the star is in one of the bones, or in two; and I tighten more on the star than elsewhere, and I touch less frequently, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are on the star be soft and moist, and neither too hard nor too rough; and let the thread, which is strained, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And warm the limb and the joint afterwards every day.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any evil accident happens to the limb, if like itching that happens to the limb, then you must know that you must raise the limb with warm water, until the itching is calmed; and leave the limb still until it has rested.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then restart the movement, and if the tendons are softened and the bones are loosened, and similar things, if necessary
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If you take care that the swelling does not come back to the limb, because it is too tight, if you must soften it somewhat, and leave it for some days, until the swelling goes down, and then strain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said do not happen to the patient, then leave it for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or perhaps after that, then he must hold his hands to his chest, and keep his collar even, and be careful of movement and vomiting, and sleep on his back; and change the dressing every thirty days or every fifty, and sometimes every twenty days, according to the composition and the temperament of the patient
de la brisure de la main	From the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	From the fracture of the hand: At the back of the hand there are two bones that often break; and it does not come out but pours out many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the bone of the hand is broken or split, if it is known that the patient is limping, if he is sitting straight before him equally; then put his hand on the extended cloth and stretch out the broken bones, and put them even with the thumbs, until they are well joined; and put on the plaster and the bandage, if the abscess does not come out, then put on a splint as much as is necessary; and be wrapped in one cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is on the edge of the limb towards the belly of the hand, if you make a loop of bandage, and command the patient to hold his broken limb firmly; and then stretch from a long cloth, and be the splint as great as the bone of the hand, and strain it, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is on the side, then command that you place a splint above and below at the root, so that the hand is overextended and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and seal the gap between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture does not come from either side, if it is the pouch, if it is equal, as it should be; and strain with the root, and if you see that it does not move, put a right splint small enough to raise the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is elsewhere, as in the index or one of the others, if it is equal, and bind it with the two fingers that follow; or bind them all together, holding the wrist tightly, or put on a splint, as for a pouch; and take care in restoring and disposing of the wound, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken limb
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often fractured, and it is well seen when they twist before and behind; and the restoration is when it is bound with a thread above the fracture and below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, and extends his limbs equally; and it is when the fracture is within the bone itself
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	If the fracture is near the root of the thigh bone, if one of the ligaments above the ankle and the other the ligament below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then either the ligament above the knee or the ligament below the fracture must be taut; then place the limb parallel to its natural position, and then apply the dressing and bandage, without which there will be no healing.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is an abscess that has burst, let it rest peacefully and then return to your work and your treatment; the bandage is made in a timely manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap the fracture with a strong bandage doubled over twice or thrice; and to drain the excess blood, then bend the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail; and pass a thread long between the thigh and the limb from below the knee, and pass the thread over the top of the bone; then bend the limb and the thigh together, and place the bandage under the fracture, and place a splint on the limb; and put between the limb and the thigh eight cloth squares to equal the tension, and as you go up the fracture and less you strain; and take out two threads that you passed between the limb and the thigh, and tie three knots on top, and leave as much tension as there is no displacement or swelling or anything similar.</start_of_turn
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is an abscess that has burst, if it comes loose, address what has come, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to extract them; and if this cannot be done, it is necessary to cut the limb open and drain the pus.  The treatment is as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in this place where I put the needles, as in the arm or the shoulder; nevertheless, in the restoration made in this place, I do not cause any pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And the swelling that remains in the bone is restored in one or two days, or less or more, according to the variations of temperaments.</start_of_turn>
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the rue du genouil</start_of_turn
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Hairs that are in the groin region have often burst, but they fall out many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	If they break, if not just a split, or a wound, there is pain and injury, and this feeling is very bad.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is set right, do this: put everything that is round back to its place until it is firmly assembled again; then put on the dressing, and put on a round cushion, if you need it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the orders that we have said before, as for example incision and other like that; if you put into practice each of these things that it should be done, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	And if it is set right, do this: put everything that is round back to its place until it is firmly assembled again; then put on the dressing, and put on a round cushion, if you need it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the orders that we have said before, as for example incision and other like that; if you put into practice each of these things that it should be done, until it is healed.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Hairs that are on the leg have two bones, of which one is called the «muscle», and the other is called the «femur». And there is often a breaking of these bones as it happens in the arm, and because of this the restoration is just as in the arm, and the work is like that
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a bone is fractured near the surface, twist the limb forward.</start_of_turn>
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, there is great pain, and one can see it clearly; and there is bursting of the marrow
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	When therefore the fracture is slight, and there is more than one piece, the extension must be less severe and more gentle; and the limb must be aligned according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, if you take .ij. strips of coarse cloth that cover the limb from one side to the other, and be as long as the limb from the knee to the toes; then wrap in .ij. layer of lint from under and from over, and bind firmly in the middle, and with this binding the limb will not bend either to the right or to the left, and that is good; and no one will administer any more than .ij. dose of pain that is long as the limb, and if there is a wound, and put on the limb to prevent movement, and do it properly in the fracture or there is an injury; and move each joint of the limb, to see if there is any swelling or other accident; if the cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of bones at their root.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but in the bones of the root of the limb there is no fracture at all, and two must suffice; there is no other means than to wait until healing is complete.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the root of the limb, and you see these bones pressing against each other, if you put the limb so that it hangs down to the earth like a bird in flight, and then put the limb back in its place, as soon as the bones are raised, then put on the dressing and bandage, and put a little bandage under the limb at the joint, then restrain the limb from moving, and cover it with a cloth bandage.</start_of_turn
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if the limb is healed, because you will find the bones equal, whether fractured or dislocated.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are two fractures, if you restore them as we have said, then hold the hand still; then place under the fracture a splint according to the length of the fracture, and make it wider than the width of the fracture, and put on the dressing that I have said; and if there are three or more, fracture them and place under each fracture a splint according to its quantity, covered with a bandage of linen, and strain the dressing from the bone.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And remember that you must not neglect the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and secure each accident as it should be secured.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	from the fracture of the clavicle bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone is fractured in a woman, if she sits up, the wound must be elevated to the painful part and held in place by the back; then fill the wound with wool, and put as much in as I stand; then withdraw the woman, and keep her back and front supported, and then pull out the wool, until it reaches the bottom of the wound; and bring back the bone with the wool underneath. When she sees blood, if the bone is pulled out, and when she has bled, she must rest for seven days or more: if the fracture is restored, and if you see it, take a bladder of vinegar and bind it to the wound, and keep the bladder over the wound until the bladder is emptied; then the wound will return to its natural state.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of a man or a woman is broken, if you restore it as we have said concerning the thigh bone; these fractures are not hidden from the one who placed his study and his art upon them, and they understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For these fractures signify in many cases the right way of restoration: understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the groin, when it is fractured, take a goose neck and bind it up; then cover it with cloth, and leave it for two days or until it is healed, and it will be perfectly healed then.
de brisure avec plaie	Of sudden with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	In case of sudden fracture with wound, even if it is great, as for the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, that it should be sound now, if what we have said is true
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is sound, if the clot of vitriol remains, if you have nothing else, then resume the fracture in the same hour, or the following, if there is no other sign of fracture.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there is swelling at the fracture, if the swelling persists until the next day, leave the restoration until the swelling has subsided, and do not touch either the third or the fourth part, for you will risk causing further damage.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is fractured and is apparent through the skin, cover it immediately with your hands, lightly extending your fingers.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if extension does not appear to you, hold this instrument of iron, which is about the length of three or four fingers, and its width is according to the extent of the wound; for this reason it is necessary to press three or four fingers, according to what is necessary in the wound of a fracture; and let it be round and firm, so that it does not press against the limb at your work, or be placed before and behind, and large in the middle forward.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," because it must be known that the curved limb should be placed above the head of the apparent bone; and once again, when it returns, it must be equal on one side as the other
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot firmly grasp the bone, if you must hold the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have possession of it
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot restore the bone, as we have said, if you grasp with a covering instrument that can reach that area, or if you must incision or burn, at your peril; then withdraw that which is remaining embedded in the bone, with rough rasps and scanty pus.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the limb is returned to its place, the patient experiences great pain afterward, swelling that is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so until it is in its place, then more I drape it in black wine stain, and so it should be; and do not put any cerote or other thing on the wound except oil, lest it cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer stars when you have restored the limb, and leave the wound uncovered, and close the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with the breaking; and many times this has been done to the fool, and has caused the patient to die or be crippled or caused decay on many occasions; so let the astringency be more gentle and soft than the other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is small or large, and you doubt that the treatment will not suffice, as we have said, and you feel pain in the limb, if it does not suffice to put on bandages; then cover round about with coarse cloth instead of bandages, and bind them tight.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is healing, if the bone that you put on the whole has become loose, and there is swelling of wounds, as with swelling of medicines and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must stretch the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is soldered and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And you must keep the limb perfectly still in some measure that it can move easily without causing harm
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it is dislocated again, and it cannot stay in place, it must be reset while the limb is still slightly bent, as there are small pieces of bone that must be broken in order to stop the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if fistula arises in the limb, or other manner of corruption, if it is necessary to cure it, according to what is said in this chapter above
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if the bone is fractured and opened upon the limb, as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other bones of the great limbs, if I do not treat it, for many times death comes from this; but I leave it until it has healed; by chance it will heal by itself after twenty or thirty days, and then I will cure the wound, if I wish; and if I do not wish, I will leave it
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The hairs which come out from the beard
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The hairs which come out from the beard come out many times after the heat of the summer, even when it is close to the joint, and it is a helpful thing to see how the limb is positioned; and by chance it cannot do its natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Beware then that you take care: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and the like, do not take any of these things, or all of them together, and mix them with wine that is astringent or with plenty of egg or with oil; and put them on the wound in bandages, and strain it well, and do not remove it from the hand for days; and then dislocate it, and do it again, until the dislocations are bony; or you strain it on a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is that it hardens all the swellings under the limb; and if the dislocation has already become hard like stone, and it is necessary to break it, if the swelling above has burst, and to make the excess apparent; or you leave it without a drain, until it is bony, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after the bandage.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break of the bone is restored, and hangs limp after the limb is weak and limp, if there is any cause for it: because it was too tightly bound and was not bound properly; or because there are too many bands, and cannot come back to the limb naturally; or because of many wounds; or from too great movements, not even in its proper place; or because there is much blood in its body, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and make the limb firm, as long as it does not swell in him; and give him bath, and make him joyful and cheerful; then put on a bandage over the limb, so that the bandage attracts to great nourishment, and the blood flows often hot, until the nourishment comes back to the limb; and restore it to its natural position.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is bent after the illness.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is bent after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the limb is deformed, all this without damaging its natural work: for it is not believed that one should break the limb anew, as some fools say; and many have suffered from this treatment in our land; this work is blamed, and many deaths result from it; however, if the swelling and pain are fresh, if you can raise them with warm water or soft herbs, such as meadowsweet leaves, and roots, and honey, and similar things; and you make a soft dressing, like with aquaint well done, and take the nourishing draught of meadowsweet, and mix it with grease of gelline or olive oil, and make a dressing on top; or you take fat figs, and grind them with horse dung, and similar medicines that alleviate the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the bone loosened by continuous rubbing and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be no movement to the limb for an hour
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	If the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron tongs, if you cover it up to the bone, make a superficial incision; and put cushion and packing in the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	If the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron tongs, if you cover it up to the bone, make a superficial incision; and put cushion and packing in the wound.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to no avail, if it can now be remedied.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, if by chance it swells up again, and by chance one tries to move it again; for this reason it must not be moved while it is swollen: many times it brings swelling and other pains; however, when this happens, if you make the patient comfortable, then leave it alone, until the swelling has subsided; then raise the limb with warmth and oil, and move it gently, and cure each limb as it comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters concerning dislocations from the shoulder to the foot
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The jaws are loosened and the dislocation of both is like this: when they are united to their bones, and softened by moisture; or when they are entirely loosened, and hang towards the chin, and close the mouth that it cannot hold it, cannot close its mouth, and engulfs its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, if it returns by itself in several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, if you must move it urgently, do not grasp it; and in such a way that the servant holds the patient’s hand near the root of the dislocation of the jaw in the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other hand must be loosened, to make them even; and command the patient to soften his jaw, his teeth, and move them all around
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And look that you make the thing even, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns grasped, even if both mandibles are together, if they arise with hot water and oil, keep them lightly; do not force the return, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are restored even, and the patient’s mouth is well closed with gentle pressure, lay on moist cloths moistened in cerate made of rose oil and wax, then bind them lightly with linen; and let the patient rest on his back, with his arms resting between two cushions, so that they do not move neither to the right nor to the left, neither to the front nor to the back, but take a little nourishment, until the pains are over, and keep the jaw firmly closed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the jaw bones do not manage to be reset at a single hour, and are not firmly converted to their place, then fever and swelling become accustomed, and by chance solution of the belly, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
