Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	When you see that, then know that it is a loss; and many times death is the consequence in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the forceps.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot remove the bone from its place without causing further damage, and is always damaging when it is used.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	When the patient lies still on his back and extends his arms; then press the limb towards your palm, and it will return; then put on the support and bind it, and strain it; and the limb which is towards the shoulder cannot be dislocated; if it does so once, if you leave it dislocated, if you must restore it, as we have said; then put on the support and the bandage, and strain it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the meantime restore the shoulder, when it is freed from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	De la dislocation de l’espaule.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Hair that has grown on the shoulder is not loosened except in three ways: firstly, it is loosened at the side of the shoulder towards the armpit; secondly, at the side of the elbow; and sometimes it is loosened at the top; thus indeed; do not loosen it from behind on the shoulder, neither from below on the nerves; and often it is loosened from below towards the shoulder, even among those who have little hair, for in these jumps it is greatly hindered; among those who have enough hair, the jump is painful, and it returns painful.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, there happen to be blows or fractures, and swell the shoulder from a deep abscess, and care that it is loosened by that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must certainly be sure, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is known that a dislocation occurs when it is twisted towards the armpit, and it distinguishes between the healthy shoulder and the sick shoulder; and you will find between their diversity an indentation at the head of the shoulder, and the armpit touches the head of the shoulder, just as if it were a wound; and the patient cannot move their arm to its place, neither can they move in any way; and thus, if it has been dislocated upwards, if it is not hidden, since you will find it manifested by touching; and this manner of dislocation is not sufficient to bring it back, when it is new, or when the patient is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is that the assistant holds the painful limb upwards, then places his thumbs below the armpit, and holds the joint forcefully upwards; and the assistant holds the limb, and extends it upwards, because it is put below; if necessary.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If she does not come as we have said above, if you must, the patient must be bathed in warm water; and give him a soft and soothing nourishment, such as broth of elderberry, fenugreek, and melilot in water, or give it to him directly. Then either let the patient lie on his back and put under his buttocks a cushion of linen equal in size, not too soft nor too hard, and put his hand on the cushion, and support his shoulder joint firmly, and treat the hand of the patient; and another attendant will hold his shoulder firmly, so that it does not move backward. When the shoulder joint returns to its place, if you see that it remains in this manner: and it is that you make present a person who is greater than the patient; and stand behind the patient’s shoulder, and stretch the shoulder joint from under the patient’s buttock, and raise the buttock up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another attendant will treat the patient’s hand backward toward his belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, if he can hold nothing heavy, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And so we will repeat it in another way: if you insert a long pin into the earth, and the head of the shoulder is as high as the fist and not too thick or thin; then put on the patient’s hand, but let there be a bandage over it, and let the patient’s arm be resting on a long cushion; then extend the patient’s hand from the other side and the joint will return to its place immediately. And if it does not return with all these things we have said, do this remedy: take two large pins and three thin ones, which have the head bent inwards so as to enter under the scapula, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	If these things fail to restore it, if you wish to perform this cure: take one thumb and two fingers of great length, which have the tip rounded like a mouse entering through an opening in the wall, and place them under the armpit, following this form. Then support the shoulder with a cloth, so that it does not bleed the patient, and place it under the armpit of the patient. Extend your arms above the shoulder, and support the arm at the wrist, and place the thumb on the index finger of a fist, and extend the hand outward. The joint is now restored.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is restored, in whatever way, if you wish to keep it in place, put under the armpit a square ball of wool of equal size, and put on it a pad of powdered meal, with incense and alum of egg, on the whole shoulder and around the joint, then strain under the armpit immediately, and keep the limb resting on the pad, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands still together.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move the limb gently while it is comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then move it more vigorously after five or six days, and move it. And if it is stiff and cannot be softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is forced from its place by moisture or for some other reason, you must administer cautery at three punctures, as is placed before or alongside the cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and the joint remains dislocated after six days, and the limb still cannot be raised, then the nerves at the head of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and if the joint never heals in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The shoulder dislocation which is from the front, and the arm, or behind, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the hands, and is administered with another bandage; and it heals as long as it is sound.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there comes pain in the limb, and later movement, if the patient uses the limb many times, as long as that pain is relieved, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation that remains.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	The joint is dislocated at the point where it is usually stable, and the same thing happens at the front and the back; and it is often detached, both front and back, and the dislocation is not easily remedied, for we see it clearly and feel it well; and it is detached in this way.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the patient with the salve, if he sees it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is shaken, and cannot hold his arm, touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And must keep it still as before, because if it were to come loose again, if it should ever happen, it will bring grief to bring it back; and by chance it cannot be brought back whole, even if it is at the back; for it is better to leave it as it is than to cause further pain, and by chance there comes death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it is restored again, when it is such that it can be brought back, you must extend your hand with both hands; and let your arms be spread out, and your hands down to the level of the patient's shoulders front and back, and hold the joint firmly together, or at the root of the bone, until it returns to its place
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when the patient doubles their hand over their hand, and grasps from the root of the thumb which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not see it return to its place, if you administer strong extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and hold it, if it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from the shoulder, and when you have enveloped a double-long and wide bandage; and when you look at the joint with the hand, if there is any oil on the joint to lubricate it, then restore the joint immediately; and when it is in its place, put on dry plaster with egg yolk, and the strain is formed, and bend the arm to the patient’s chest, and leave it there for some days, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	When the joint is firmly in its place, if you loosen the limb and leave it; if you see that the joint does not hold well, repeat the plastering and the limb, and leave it until it is firmly set; then take it off.</start_of_turn>
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the joint has been reset, and it moves, bathe and rub thoroughly, and press until it is eased; or put upon the joint a poultice of mutton fat, then leave it for a day and a night, and then draw out the bone, and pour in oil; and when it has sweated, rub the joint gently, then put the poultice back, and then draw out or bathe; do this twice or thrice, until it is healed. And if you see that it returns to its place, put upon a moist poultice of rue chaff with vinegar, and strain it; if it returns to its place again.
li dislocation de la main	When the hand is dislocated...
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	When the joint of the hand is loosened, and its return is laborious, more so than the others, it must be immediately reset in its place without delay, even if there is swelling or if there is a fracture.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	If you put the diseased hand on a table, and extend the patient, look at the hand that is being put on, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and press until it returns whole, you must look to see if it is well placed; then put the patient’s hand behind his hand on the table during extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and I will look and put their hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good. If not, if the strain of the resting muscles is appeased after the incisions, and you leave it in its original position, it will resume its course.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if it cannot bear it, and you do not set it in place after a few days, the joint will become stiff; and nothing will help the patient except that his nerves are severed, or an artery is cut. If there is no other reason for straining except to cauterize, do so in this case, and by chance that is the only thing that will help.</start_of_turn
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are in place, if you put on the dressing that we have mentioned, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it easily, and there is no pain, if the wound is filled with warm liquid, and it is washed until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never is the head of the arm loosened from its shoulder-blade at the chest, never at the back of the palm or belly; therefore is the head loosened, and the dislocation is held in your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the arm and incline it towards the part where it is joined; and leave it there for two days, and then put it back in its place; and do not touch it, as we have said, and loosen it, and move it, and bind it up; do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is loosened at the belly of the arm, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is loosened from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	and do the same if it is dislocated at the wrist, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is dislocated from another part.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade or the collarbone is loosened, or if there are several loosenings, if no remedy is found, for the patient is in haste.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign that it is that the blood egestions flow in the contrary direction, it cannot be held, and many times it is softened in no limb, or the two thighs or two arms or one leg. And many times the marrow of the bones moves at three parts; that which moves at the back is called "gilbosite": it is cured if you restore that the gilbosite has come from childhood: if there is no cure or healing of the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting or from blows or from similar things, they say the old methods of treatment with great words, or it has no great benefit; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes before the wound, there is no health; and as much as that which comes straight across two ribs, one can cure nothing except that which comes from behind, as I have said; and that the patient should be placed with his face down one inch equal, and should have a strain from his toes up, that he should not move; then I put a bandage on the head of the wound, and another at the toes, and I bind up the limbs of the patient, and I put on gloves and sleeves; and two assistants know the bands, one at the head and the other at the toes, among the two bands; and they must be well closed, the bandage as I have said, and the patient should put his palms on the spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this treatment, take a table three palms long, and hold the thumbs at the edge, and let the patient sit on the side; grasp the head of the table at the edge and put the middle of the table on the spine; and place the thumbs on the other side of the table, and press firmly, until it returns to its place. If you see that it has not returned, do it with the thumb that is turned at the wrist.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And take two fingers at the head of the patient’s arm of a great span, and grasp two others, and between each finger, put a sow and a nail, a palm’s length; and in each finger put a hole, or the nail is crooked, and let the fingers be firmly fixed in the earth, so that they do not move; and between two fingers let there be one turning, so that the thread that turns returns, and between two turns put two small fingers of a palm’s length, so that the turning returns; and then join the thread that is between the armpits to the turning at the head, and the other thread to the pieces at the other turning, and keep the minister turning his turning all along the thread, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, put upon a dry dressing with abundance of eggs, and then press, and then support with a tab of three fingers' length, that it may reach the root of the rib and the part of the spine that is painful; then bind with a thread as we have said, and use the patient with gentle support, as long as he is sane; and if nothing comes to an end of the sanity, if it is necessary, administer soothing and calming medicines, as we have said before; and under no circumstances give a dose of purgative, and under no circumstances let it appear in the lower spine of the back, and take care that it is not a dislocation; for it is the bone that has opened, for which we must not presume: by chance comes death.
des dislocations de la hainche	hip dislocation
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Hairs that are attached to the hip and shoulder joints only become loose from dislocations alone, and do not come out with other joints; and the hip joint is loosened in three parts: within and without, and in front and behind; and the more within it is loosened, the more loosened is in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is this: when the diseased limb is joined with the flesh, if it is longer, and opens more the patient's joints than before, and cannot double his knee at the fire; and it is the bruise that is left inflamed by cautery, for this is what brings about the dislocation of the shoulder
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes to the aid, if it is that this accident is contrary to those mentioned above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of one who comes to the aid, if it is that he has his limb well in accordance with the accomplishment; however, do not double his knee with pain, and if you see him do so, do not do so before, and retain his urine, and swell his groin, and when he walks, pass over his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of one who comes to the aid, if it is that he cannot expand his knee, cannot double it, and is that his limb is shorter than the other, and his groin is softened, and his shoulder is dislocated from its socket
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	You must take back this semblance of dislocation if it is an old dislocation and it remains according to its habit, if there is no cure; and it is not recommended that you do so unless there is presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you are hasty you will twist the joint, and stretch outwards and downwards, and move it to the right and left; by chance if it returns, and there is no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return in this manner, if you must, appear I strong minister, and grasp the limb with two hands, or with one that you shall bind upon the knee; and another minister extends his hand downwards as far as he can, while he holds his hands above his buttocks, and he grasps it with a loop of thread upon the hip; and another holds the head of the limb. Extend both upwards and downwards together, until the patient is lifted from the earth at once, and remains so.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	Such a method of extension is common in three out of four cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.</start_of_turn>
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this does not happen, if you must, put the patient’s limb in its natural position. When the dislocation is complete, if you can, place the limb on the costal margin and place the ligament at the root of the hip, and the limb that is below the ankle, then extend the ligament upwards towards the ankle and downwards towards the heel; then take another minister and grasp his arms, and embrace the great limb of the painful area, and extend it towards the front: if it returns to its place now; this method of dislocation is less severe than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you do not hold it firm in this manner as we have said, if you must, bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong thread above the two toes and above the two knees; let the limb of the patient extend two inches more than the others; then let it hang suspended from the head of a staff, or on the ground two arms long; then command one minister to grasp the head of the hip, and let another minister hang alongside the patient, who graspes the hip, for the joint is now restored.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	When the dislocation is driving out, if the patient is lying down, as we have said in the case of hiccuping, grasp the limb of the patient firmly above the knee and above the foot; then put two cushions, one at the head and one at the foot, then push one cushion between the hips of the patient, shaping it like this; and plant cloths soaked in moisture around it, so that it does not bleed from the patient; then extend the hands of the ministers towards him, and the one who is holding the dislocation should put it equal in his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put on the table as we said in the previous, and press on it as we have told you, and keep the patient lying on the right side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, if you must, extend the limb gently, as I have said; and look with your eyes where the pain is on the painful side, and press on the other hand, and extend it backwards towards the groin.</start_of_turn>
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation has gone away, if it does not wish to extend the patient’s limb, do not lift it up, but rather keep it as it was before, for it must be as if it had been stretched out beforehand; as we have said concerning the two inches; and let it rest on its face, and the limb must be stretched out as we have said previously, and must press on the joint at the table; and it will be finished when the patient extends his leg, and they will be even; then join the thighs and put on the dressing, and bind with a bandage, so that the limb does not move; and let it rest for three days or four, then take it off and put on the dressing once more; and if you see that they are even, if the bandage is as before, and leave it for three days; then take it off and leave it be quietly, until the limb is comfortable
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the shoulder joint...
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder joint is dislocated in two ways: forward and backward; and do not strain it forward
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his limb at his knee, and if he does not feel it at his knee, take away his socks; and restore him when you make him sit upright, and extend his limb if he can, and put your back against his face, and put your hand on his toes; then take his heel towards your palms, and draw between your thighs, then bend his two thighs together; and another attendant extends his hand, as long as his knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he has properly bent his limb at his knee; and put on the dressing and make the limb rest on the knee, and bind them together firmly for three or four days, and then remove them. And do not work with the patient until his limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at a point, if an extension is administered strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The shoulder is never completely rigid and is always somewhat dislocated and painful.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is if the ankle is swollen, and attempts before at the part where it is loosened: if it is slight, one must extend it slightly with the hands when it is only slightly painful.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely drained, if you do this, make the patient sit upright, and hold him firmly by the leg, under the ankle; then take hold of the limb at your right hand, and then at the left hand twice, and extend it upwards, and keep it well stretched out; do this twice as we have said, pressing in and pulling the limb; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return, make the patient lie face down on the ground, and hold his heel firmly on the ground between his thighs, and cover him with a blanket, so that he does not bleed; then hold the limb firmly with one hand or another, as close as possible to the neck of the limb; and extend the toes equally, and keep the heel either pressed against the thighs of the patient to retain the limb when it is stretched; then put the thumbs equally on the dislocation at your hands, and another assistant holds the limb steady at the ankle, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When it comes to the boil [cautery], if it comes to a head, put on the dressing and stamp upon it, and the strain forms, and join the thumb to the finger, and keep the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature softens, if the strain has gone; then take it off in a third or fourth, and tell the patient for three days. And if it goes before this time, this is not certain except that it will go sour.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he pricks at his base, if you must hold his eyes still as we have said before, until he is whole again.</start_of_turn>
des dois	until he is healed.</start_of_turn>
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if you can gently stretch the limb, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no other place but the back of the thumb, it is to be ordered that the patient sits on one knee or on the ground, and put your thumb on what is open of these joints, and press on your thumb until it returns; and when it is equal, and there is no opening, if you put on the dressing of the thumb a table for two fingers, then the strain forms, and leave it for three days, then take it off; and make it rest until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	with wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound accompanies a dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times the patient dies. If you are not humble in the cure and do not have skill in the art, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and tardy, do not be bold; and begin with calming measures at the outset, and leave the patient in the hands of the Lord, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, if you now restore the limb to its place, even though the abscess remains; and when the limb is in place, if you administer calming measures at the outset, cure the wound, as it is fitting, with dried sponges; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and bones are fractured, if the bones are displaced, do as is said in simple illnesses; and beware of entering into fear, as I have said, for this will be unprofitable to you according to your Creator, and for the salvation of your soul and your body.
Amen	Amen.
